# Backtest Optimization — Architecture Document

**Created:** 2026-06-09
**Owner:** Lead Engineer
**Status:** Step 3 (Architecture) of `/new-feature` — conditional gate = YES (new storage layer + engine SoA rewrite + 3 net-new optional deps)
**Grounding:** `specs/backtest-optimization-findings.md`, `specs/backtest-optimization-discovery.md`, `specs/backtest-optimization-requirements.md` (517 reqs across 15 categories)
**Tracker:** `plans/backtest-performance/progress-tracker.md`

## Prime Directive (binds every section below)

This is a **performance + storage refactor with a HARD zero-business-logic-change constraint**. The optimization changes **HOW** data is loaded, located, looped, and stored — **never WHAT** the business rules decide. Every architectural choice is subordinate to these invariants (from the tracker's Locked Decisions D1–D6 + Hard Parity Constraints):

| Invariant | Enforcement point |
|-----------|-------------------|
| Bit-identical trades + `equity_curve` on canonical **5m no-drill** path (phase-dependent representation — R2-F1-batch4) | Golden-master CI guard (Phase 0 oracle), every phase. **Through P2** (still Decimal engine math): byte-identical to the string→Decimal oracle. **From P3 on** (float64 SoA math lands — §3.3/§3.4): the golden master is **re-frozen AS the float64 representation** (REQ-STORE-040 corrected per R2-F2-batch4 — float64 is the frozen, oracle-diffed representation, NOT a lossless Decimal mirror), and the gate is **discrete fields bit-identical** (trade count, sides, symbols, entry/exit bar indices, ordering — REQ-PAR-018) **AND money fields within a pinned TWO-SIDED `continuous-money-epsilon`** vs the Decimal oracle. **"Non-optimistic" (one-sided float ≤ Decimal) does NOT apply to the 5m no-drill float64 lane (R4-F3-batch6-c3, REQ-TEST-005):** on the no-drill lane the ONLY difference from the Decimal oracle is **symmetric representation-rounding noise** (ULP accumulation that can land float64 net_profit slightly ABOVE *or* below the Decimal value) — there is no intrabar/coarse-resolution ambiguity and therefore no pessimism to enforce, so a one-sided constraint would either false-fail correct runs or be undefined per-field. The 5m no-drill lane is governed by the **two-sided `continuous-money-epsilon` + discrete-bit-identical** gate ONLY, consistent with REQ-TEST-005's tolerance registry tagging money as two-sided `continuous-money-epsilon`. **"Non-optimistic" is reserved for the drill / portfolio / fast-path lanes** (next row), where pessimistic intrabar/coarse-resolution resolution IS the intended invariant. The user's "golden bit-identical on 5m no-drill" holds against the **frozen float64 master** at every phase; only the *oracle it is diffed against* changes representation at P3. |
| <1% per-trade + summary deviation on drill/portfolio paths **AND non-optimistic (one-sided — these lanes have genuine intrabar/coarse-resolution ambiguity, so float ≤ Decimal pessimism is the intended invariant; contrast the no-drill lane above, R4-F3-batch6-c3)** | Differential float64-vs-Decimal harness + two-sided sandwich (REQ-DRILL-018) |
| `Σ trade.pnl == final_equity − starting_capital == net_profit` on every fixture | Three-way reconciliation check, replaces weak `_assert_reconciles` (REQ-PAR / Phase 0). **Tolerance is lane-dependent (R3-F3-batch5, REQ-PAR-018):** EXACT equality holds **only on the P0–P2 Decimal lane**. **From P3 onward (float64)** the two sides are accumulated in **different operation orders** — the wallet is mutated incrementally by `wallet_delta = pnl − exit_fee` with funding applied live per-event (`backtest_engine.py:1410`, `:1257-1263`), while each trade's `recorded_pnl = pnl − exit_fee − entry_fee − funding_paid` is folded separately (`:1411`); float64 addition is non-associative, so `Σ recorded_pnl` and `final_equity − starting_capital` differ by ULPs on legitimate runs. A **pinned per-run reconciliation tolerance** (relative + absolute, scaled to `starting_capital` and trade count) is therefore applied to BOTH the per-run invariant check AND the §5.2 GET-path torn-persist guard from P3 on, so neither false-positives on a valid high-trade-count run and refuses to serve it. A high-trade-count fixture asserts the guard does NOT false-positive. |
| Sealed closed day fetched **exactly once** across N reruns | Mock-client `call_count == 1` test (REQ-CACHE) |
| Golden NO-OP guarantee: empty `instrument_info`/`scan_contexts`/`fine_klines` + no regime → byte-identical to 5m path | Per-phase NO-OP fixture (discovery §8) |
| `metrics.total_trades` never absent/renamed | Frontend breaking-change trap guard (`BacktestResultsPage.tsx:255`) |
| Core files stay semantically identical | `backtest_engine.py`, `backtest_service.py`, `kline_cache_service.py`, `trading_rules.py`, `sweep_tools.py` |
| 120s `_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` hard wall-clock cap (may be raised, never relied upon) | Pre-flight estimator (REQ-PERF-037) |
| `max_same_sector` stays an intentional engine no-op | Do NOT "fix" (D6); service emits `max_same_sector_not_enforced` |
| **Derived-coarse `15m/1h/4h` == legacy native-coarse** for any coarse-interval config (R3-F4-batch2, REQ-TEST-030) | The optimized engine **serves coarse bars DERIVED from the sealed 5m base** (§4.3, REQ-STORE-024), whereas legacy **fetched Bybit native coarse bars** — and Bybit's native coarse aggregation is **not guaranteed bit-equal** to a 5m `time_bucket` resample (boundary / last-bar / volume handling), so a coarse-interval config can decide differently post-refactor. This is a **data-source substitution** the 5m-no-drill golden master does NOT cover (it is pinned to the 5m path) and the `<1%` drill/portfolio tolerance does NOT cover (it is about intrabar fill, not coarse-source swap). Standing gate, run alongside the 5m golden master: derived-coarse must equal the legacy native-coarse result **byte-identical on the Decimal lane (P0–P2) / within the pinned float epsilon (P3+)** for every config whose `simulation_interval` is coarse. The `BT_DERIVE_COARSE` flag-OFF native-fetch path (§7.2) is the documented fallback when derivation diverges. |

**7-phase rollout (P0..P6), each gated by its own golden-master diff:**
P0 golden-master harness → P1 cache re-download fix → P2 batched loaders + parallel sweeps → P3 SoA + merge-walk engine → P4 numba JIT kernel → P5 Parquet/DuckDB read layer → P6 vectorized fast-path + `prange` sweeps.

---

# 1. Architecture Decision Records

## ADR-001 — Keep the sequential cross-sectional event loop (numba-accelerated SoA), reject a vectorbt/framework rewrite

**Status:** Accepted (D1, D5). Implements Phase 3 (SoA) + Phase 4 (numba) + Phase 6 (optional fast-path).

**Context.**
`BacktestEngine.run()` (`backtest_engine.py:122`) is a **cross-sectional, shared-capital portfolio simulation**, not N independent single-asset backtests. Concrete coupling that forbids per-symbol vectorization:
- **Portfolio-level close rules** — `_evaluate_equity_rules` / `_eval_equity_core` (`backtest_engine.py:1496/1580`) act on **basket equity** `E = wallet + Σ open-uPnL` across the whole open book and flatten the basket on a threshold (`EQUITY_DROP_PCT`, `EQUITY_DROP_PCT_SMART`, `close_on_profit_pct`, `EQUITY_RISE_PCT`). No symbol's exit is computable in isolation (REQ-PAR-006).
- **Stateful latches** — `SimulationState.smart_drawdown_fired` one-shot per scan with re-arm at `engine L1139` (REQ-PAR-004); `cycle_start_equity` zeroing on cycle termination (REQ-PAR-003); funding `(date,hour)` boundary dedupe (`_evaluate_candles_until` funding block `L1243`); adaptive-blacklist computed from the run's **own** trade history (`_is_adaptively_blacklisted` `L1083`).
- **Path-dependent sizing** — `qty` sized off running wallet + cross-book available balance (`_open_position` `L825`, REQ-PAR-010/011).
- **Cycle gating** — `skip_if_positions_open` latched at scan start (REQ-PAR-012), per-scan `max_trades`, immediate-vs-batch depletion order (`_process_immediate_signals` `L438` / `_process_batch_signals` `L395`).

**Alternatives considered.**
1. **vectorbt `from_signals` / `Portfolio` (REJECTED).** Vectorizes each asset independently; `cash_sharing` executes all group orders at the same tick (not a true sequential cross-symbol capital walk); OSS has **no leverage / liquidation / funding** concept. Forcing it collapses into `from_order_func`/`@njit` callbacks — at which point we are writing numba anyway, through a foreign abstraction whose parity must be re-proven from scratch. Adversarial verdict in findings §4.2: **infeasible for the general config.**
2. **nautilus_trader as the engine (REJECTED for critical path).** Heavy event framework; re-deriving the 17-step filter chain + portfolio cascade to byte-parity is a multi-month port. Retained only as an **optional out-of-band cross-validation oracle** (Phase 7, off critical path — findings §8).
3. **Pure-Python micro-opt only (REJECTED as sufficient).** Helps constants, not the `O(scans × symbols × N_total)` asymptote (RC-1).

**Decision.** Keep the exact sequential loop and rule ordering. Make it fast by (a) converting per-symbol klines to **structure-of-arrays** (int64 epoch + float64 OHLCV) with a **global sorted-unique timeline** and **non-resetting merge-walk pointers** (Phase 3, parity-neutral — changes *how* prices are located, not *which* decisions fire), then (b) JIT-compiling the per-candle kernel with `@njit` (Phase 4, an **earned** upgrade behind an import guard — D5). A vectorized first-touch barrier fast-path is added **only** for the provably-independent-position config subset (Phase 6), with the **exact eligibility predicate pinned (R2-F11-batch4 + R5-F12-batch1, REQ-ENG-029, NOT left abstract):** `max_drawdown_pct >= 100` **AND** `not close_on_profit_pct` (no EQUITY_RISE/close-on-profit basket exit) **AND** `target_goal_type != 'profit_pct'` **AND** `not trailing_profit_pct` **AND** no breakeven-timeout **AND** `smart_drawdown_close` off **AND** no adaptive-blacklist exclusion in play **AND `drilldown_enabled` is OFF (drill OFF) — R5-F12-batch1** — i.e. exactly the configs where no position's exit depends on any other position's mark. Anything failing this predicate routes back to the sequential kernel.

**`drill OFF` is in the fast-path predicate — a drilled run NEVER takes the fast-path (R5-F12-batch1, Medium — undefined-drill-seam fix).** The Phase A→B drill handshake (§3.4) — `drill_requests[]` emission keyed to `(position_id, bar_open_epoch, exit_reason_code)` + the Phase B `PRICE_CORRECTION` pass — is defined for the **SEQUENTIAL `@njit` kernel** only. The fast-path is a DIFFERENT vectorized first-touch barrier-exit code path; nothing in it emits the `drill_requests[]` array Phase B requires. If a `drilldown_enabled` run were fast-path eligible (its other predicate terms can all hold), the drill seam would be **undefined**: either Phase B gets no requests (drill silently no-ops → an intrabar-price parity break vs the drilled oracle) or the interface is unspecified. **Committed resolution: add `drill OFF` to the eligibility predicate** (above) so EVERY drilled run routes to the sequential kernel that owns the drill seam — the fast-path is reserved for non-drilled runs. (The rejected alternative — specify a parallel `drill_requests[]` emission in the vectorized path with its own keying + a fast-path-drill-on parity test — is recorded as a future option, NOT committed, because the vectorized barrier scan does not naturally produce the per-position close ordering the drill keying needs.) A test asserts a `drilldown_enabled=true` config is classified fast-path-INELIGIBLE (routes to the sequential kernel) for every otherwise-eligible parameter set. Pinned in ADR-001/§3.4.

**Predicate covers EXIT-coupling AND ENTRY/SIZING-coupling — and the fast-path keeps opens sequential (R3-F9-batch2 + R3-F7-batch5, REQ-ENG-029/030).** The exit-only terms above are **necessary but not sufficient**: REQ-PAR-010/011 sizing is **path-dependent** — `qty` is sized off the running wallet + carried uPnL − Σ locked_margin, and immediate-mode depletes sequentially, so a position that closes in scan `j<k` (realizing pnl into `wallet_delta`) changes scan `k`'s sizing_capital. A purely vectorized first-touch barrier reproduces **exit prices** independently but **cannot reproduce sequential entry SIZING** unless opens still walk scans sequentially. Two corrections are pinned:
1. **The fast-path vectorizes ONLY the per-position barrier-exit scan** (`O(open_positions × bars-in-life)`); **opens and wallet-path sizing remain the sequential scan walk.** ADR-001/§3.4 state this invariant explicitly so REQ-ENG-029's predicate provably implies REQ-ENG-030 trade-by-trade equality.
2. **The eligibility predicate additionally requires** (entry/sizing-independence): no running-wallet/cross-book sizing coupling (qty must be provably config-fixed, OR opens stay sequential per (1)), `not skip_if_positions_open`, no per-scan `max_trades`/`max_same_direction` binding in the universe, and **`not mean_reversion_enabled`** (or the MR barrier-exit family — `mr_time_stop_minutes`/`mr_tight_stop_pct`/`mr_target_capture_pct` — is explicitly folded into the eligible set with its OWN oracle). The earlier "exit-only / complete" claim is corrected: the predicate is exit-AND-entry-coupling-free. The REQ-ENG-030 bit-identical-vs-sequential-oracle gate remains the backstop on the eligible subset.

**The ≥10× speedup target is REGIME-SCOPED, because opens stay sequential (R4-F6-batch6-c3, REQ-ENG-029).** REQ-ENG-029's "≥10× over the sequential kernel while producing identical trades" cannot hold uniformly across the whole eligible set once correction (1) keeps opens + wallet-path sizing on the sequential scan walk: for a **high-admission eligible config** (many opens per scan, shallow/short holds) the sequential open/sizing walk is a hard **Amdahl floor** — vectorizing only the barrier-exit scan leaves the dominant cost sequential, so ≥10× is not achievable there. The ≥10× target is therefore **scoped to the sub-regime where barrier-exit work dominates: a deep concurrent book held over long lives** (`O(open_positions × bars-in-life)` ≫ the sequential open/sizing cost). Resolution (committed): **(a)** REQ-ENG-029's ≥10× is re-scoped to that deep-book/long-hold sub-regime, and the **shallow-book/high-churn eligible case is explicitly EXEMPT from ≥10×** (it has its own measured, possibly-modest speedup budget — trade-identity still required, just not ≥10×); **(b)** is NOT taken (vectorizing opens under a proven-config-fixed-sizing predicate is recorded as a future option, not committed). A **fast-path benchmark over a high-admission eligible config** asserts the achieved speedup against the **regime-scoped** target (≥10× only in the deep-book/long-hold regime; the documented modest budget in the shallow/high-churn regime) — NOT just trade-by-trade identity, which REQ-ENG-030 already covers.

**Consequences.**
- (+) Parity is defensible bar-for-bar; the loop semantics never move (REQ-ENG-002/005).
- (+) Phase 3 alone must reach "minutes" so numba is strictly optional (D5: Py3.14.3 + numpy2.4.4 is bleeding-edge for numba 0.65.1 / llvmlite 0.47.0).
- (−) numba debugging is harder (no pdb in nopython, 1–10s first-call JIT). Mitigation: **develop pure-Python-first, assert oracle-identical, then JIT the same code** (REQ-ENG / findings §8 Phase 4).
- (−) Two engine code paths (sequential kernel + optional fast-path) to keep in parity. Mitigation: on the eligible subset the fast-path must be **discrete-bit-identical to the sequential kernel** (REQ-ENG-030 bit-identical trades on the eligible subset + REQ-PAR-018 discrete-bit-identical), **not merely two-sided sandwich-bounded** — the sandwich tolerance (REQ-DRILL-018) governs intrabar fill price, but trade SELECTION and fire order on an eligible config must match the sequential oracle exactly.

## ADR-002 — Postgres write-of-record + Parquet/DuckDB read layer + Arrow hot cache (reject in-memory-only)

**Status:** Accepted (D2 — user chose over in-memory-only). Implements Phase 5; read-tier precedence in Phase 2/5.

**Context.**
Today both READ and WRITE of OHLCV go through Postgres `kline_cache` (`kline_cache_service.py:34 get_klines` / `:72 store_klines`), a row-partitioned table (migration 38, `PARTITION BY RANGE(open_time)`, monthly ±6mo + `kline_cache_default`). Reruns and sweeps re-pay row-scan + wire-serialization cost on every iteration. A backtest is an **immutable historical read** workload — ideal for columnar storage with predicate/column/partition pushdown — but live trading, reconciliation, and the scanner all depend on `kline_cache` as the durable source of truth and cannot be migrated.

**Alternatives considered.**
1. **In-memory-only cache (REJECTED by D2).** A process dict `{(symbol,interval,range): frame}` gives warm-rerun speed but evaporates on restart; every cold process (sweep worker, redeploy) re-hits Postgres. No cross-process warm path.
2. **Replace Postgres with DuckDB/Parquet as SOR (REJECTED).** Breaks live trading, reconciliation, `copy-prod-scans`, and the existing idempotent upsert/coverage contracts; unacceptable blast radius.
3. **Parquet-only, no DuckDB (DEFERRED option).** Loose Parquet is portable but needs an external scan engine; DuckDB gives SQL + predicate pushdown + one connection. Both kept behind the `KlineStore` read abstraction so the engine choice is swappable (REQ-STORE-022/023).

**Decision.** **Postgres stays the write-of-record and the forming-day SOR.** Add a layered **READ** path behind a new `KlineStore` abstraction with deterministic tier precedence (REQ-STORE-012):
`in-process Arrow/SoA hot frame → mmap'd Feather V2 → on-disk Parquet → Postgres SOR`.
Sealing the manifest is committed **LAST**, depends ONLY on durable Postgres rows + manifest (never on a successful Parquet write — REQ-STORE-026), so a columnar-write failure leaves the day **sealed and Postgres-served**, never unsealed/refetchable.

**Consequences.**
- (+) Warm same-process rerun slices from RAM: 0 disk, 0 Postgres kline reads (REQ-STORE-012); cross-process warm rerun pages in from mmap'd Feather: 0 Bybit, 0 kline SELECTs (REQ-STORE-015).
- (+) Columnar pushdown gives ~1–2 orders of magnitude on cold bulk scans (findings §4.1).
- (+) Rollback-safe: a feature flag toggles the columnar tier off → identical Postgres-read results (REQ-DEP-004, REQ-ROLL).
- (−) New durability/consistency surface (file ↔ manifest skew, forming-day torn reads). Mitigated by a SEALED-vs-MATERIALIZED two-state manifest (REQ-STORE-027) and forming-day-routes-to-primary rule (REQ-STORE-030).
- (−) pyarrow + duckdb become deps. Mitigated: import-guarded, optional extra, Postgres fallback (ADR-005).

## ADR-003 — Sealed-day manifest (provenance + immutability), reject count-based coverage

**Status:** Accepted. Implements Phase 1 (the re-download fix) + the v58 migration; underpins Phase 5 read tiers.

**Context.**
The re-download bug is a **false-positive coverage gap**, not a missing cache (findings RC-2, VERIFIED). The legacy detector compared cached `candle_count` against a theoretical-max-per-day (288 for 5m). A legitimately-short day (mid-day listing, halt/outage, the still-forming current day) stores e.g. 144/288; refetch returns the same 144; the `GREATEST` upsert (`_update_coverage` `kline_cache_service.py:303–318`) caps it at 144 < 288 **forever**; `fetched_at` is never consulted (no TTL). The current code already clips first/last day expectations (`_expected_for` `:158–176`) — a real improvement — but **count-vs-expected is still the wrong primitive**: it cannot distinguish "this day is genuinely complete and will never grow" from "this day is mid-fetch." Only a **seal** decision carries that meaning.

**Alternatives considered.**
1. **Count-based coverage with better clipping (REJECTED as primitive).** Still conflates short-but-complete with incomplete; any structural gap (exchange outage) re-reads forever. The completion-frontier truth ("is the bar even closeable yet?") is absent.
2. **TTL on `fetched_at` (REJECTED).** A TTL re-fetches *complete* history on expiry — exactly the cost we are killing. Sealed history has no TTL; only the forming edge is ever re-read.
3. **Sealed manifest (CHOSEN).** A day is **sealed** once it is fully in the past relative to the **completion frontier** `floor(now / T) * T` AND its constituent candles are durably stored + OHLC-validated. A sealed day is **immutable** and fetched **exactly once ever**; only the `(max_stored_ts → frontier)` gap is ever fetched (REQ-CACHE).

**Decision.** Add a **sealed manifest** as net-new columns on `kline_cache_coverage` (the existing per-`(symbol,interval,date)` table — DDL `async_persistence.py:650`), introduced as **migration v58** (next free int after v57, `_MIGRATIONS` `async_persistence.py:992`). Manifest encodes a mutually-distinguishable day-CLASS taxonomy (REQ-STORE-009): `{sealed-full, sealed-short-listing, sealed-interior-structural-gap, sealed-empty-negative, sealed-delist-snapped}` plus `content_sha256` (+ canonicalization version, REQ-STORE-003/004) and SEALED-vs-MATERIALIZED state (REQ-STORE-027). Gap detection becomes: *"unsealed days in `[start, frontier]` only."*

**Consequences.**
- (+) Reruns issue **0 Bybit calls** for fully-sealed ranges (REQ-STORE-009); the dominant wall-clock cost of reruns/sweeps disappears (findings §9, Phase 1 = "High" confidence).
- (+) A negative-cache class (`sealed-empty-negative`) records pre-listing / post-delist / known-gap days so they are never re-probed (REQ-CACHE, REQ-STORE-009).
- (+) The forming-day rule is explicit: `open_time ≥ frontier` is clipped before store (REQ-STORE-006) and served exclusively from Postgres primary (REQ-STORE-030).
- (−) Backfill: existing complete-but-unsealed days must be sealed. **The v58 migration callable itself ships additive DDL ONLY (columns + lifecycle table + index plumbing) and runs NO data-dependent seal backfill inline** (R1-F1). Sealing historical days is the job of a **separate `SealBackfillRunner` background component** (§3.10) that is bounded, resumable, chunked-commit, throttled, off the boot path and off the asyncio loop, gated by its own election lock (NOT the global migration advisory lock), and updates a persisted completion marker. Correctness never depends on the backfill having finished: the pre-flight estimator treats SOR-present-but-unsealed days as **WARM** (refetchable-but-cheap), and the runtime loader treats unsealed rows as refetchable until `backfill_marker = 'complete'`, so rollout never spuriously rejects a feasible run and `schema_version` reaches 58 sub-second regardless of backfill progress (REQ-PERF-038, REQ-MIG-018/020/021/022). **No synchronous mass-backfill ever runs at boot.**

## ADR-004 — Structure-of-Arrays + global timeline + merge-walk pointers, reject `list[dict]` + per-scan re-scan

**Status:** Accepted. Implements Phase 3. **Parity-neutral** (verified RC-1).

**Context.**
`_evaluate_candles_until` (`backtest_engine.py:1165`) rebuilds a `symbol_time_idx: dict[datetime, dict]` + `all_timestamps: set` by walking the **entire** `klines.get(sym, [])` list for **every** open symbol on **every** scan (`:1187–1200`), using `continue` (not `break`) on both window bounds — so it touches all `N_total` candles to extract a window that is often a handful of bars. It then re-seeds every carried position's mark by a **linear prefix scan from index 0** (`:1216–1223`). Net complexity ≈ `O(scans × symbols × N_total)` with a quadratic-in-time seeding term. This is the **single biggest engine win** and is asymptotic-verified.

**Alternatives considered.**
1. **Keep `list[dict]`, add `break` on upper bound (REJECTED as insufficient).** Removes one `continue` but still rescans from 0 for the lower bound and re-seeds linearly; no `O(log N)` lookup; dict-of-datetime hashing overhead remains.
2. **pandas DataFrame per symbol (REJECTED).** Per-scan `.loc`/boolean-mask slicing allocates; datetime64 index hides the epoch-vs-datetime dual representation the parity tests must pin (REQ-ENG-005); not numba-compatible for Phase 4.
3. **SoA numpy + `searchsorted` + non-resetting pointers (CHOSEN).** `{open_time: int64[], open/high/low/close/volume: float64[]}` per symbol (REQ-ENG); a **global sorted-unique timeline** built once via k-way merge (REQ-STORE-017); per-symbol **advancing index pointers that never reset**; price location via `searchsorted(side='right')-1` for "last close ≤ T" (REQ-ENG-005). Out-of-order intra-scan queries fall back to `searchsorted` `O(log N)` for that query — never rescan, never reset to 0 (REQ-ENG-004).

**Decision.** Build SoA + global timeline once per run before the scan loop; drive the sim with merge-walk pointers; locate marks/fills with `searchsorted`. The merge-walk must evaluate **EXACTLY** the same bar set in the half-open interval `[current_time, next_scan_time)` as the legacy window scan (same first/last bar, same boundary inclusivity — REQ-ENG-002), proven by a boundary-bar fixture and a randomized property test over timelines including the `open_time`-may-be-datetime-OR-epoch case (REQ-ENG-005/006).

**Consequences.**
- (+) Per-scan setup scales with window W, not `N_total`: a test that 4×'s pre-window history at fixed W leaves per-scan setup time constant within ±10% (REQ-ENG-001).
- (+) Mark-seeding becomes sub-quadratic (REQ-ENG-007); price lookups `O(log N)` (REQ-ENG-003).
- (+) The SoA layout is the **prerequisite substrate** for Phase 4 numba and Phase 5 zero-copy Arrow handoff (REQ-STORE-019).
- (−) Dual epoch representation (datetime vs int64-ms) must be normalized to one unit (Bybit-native int64-ms, REQ-STORE-040) at the SoA boundary — a parity-frozen conversion.

## ADR-005 — numba / pyarrow / duckdb as import-guarded optional accel, with a pure-Python fallback of record

**Status:** Accepted (D5). Cross-cutting; binds Phases 4, 5, 6.

**Context.**
The backend is currently **pure-Python with zero heavy deps**; the engine is `math`/`Decimal` only (discovery §10). numba, pyarrow, duckdb are ALL net-new. A missing wheel for any one — likely on Python 3.14.3, for which numba 0.65.1/llvmlite 0.47.0 may have **no prebuilt wheel** (D5) — must **not** crash `backend.main` import or disable the *other* optimizations.

**Alternatives considered.**
1. **Hard pins in `[project].dependencies` (REJECTED).** One unavailable wheel fails the entire `pip install` and bricks the backend (REQ-DEP-001).
2. **Single bundled "accel" guard (REJECTED).** Couples three independent libs; a missing duckdb would needlessly disable numba. Must guard **independently** (REQ-DEP-004).
3. **Optional extra + per-module import guard + pure-Python fallback of record (CHOSEN).**

**Decision.** Declare numba/llvmlite/pyarrow/duckdb as an **optional extra** / environment-marker-gated, NOT in core deps (REQ-DEP-001). Guard each independently behind `try/except ImportError` exposing a capability flag (`HAS_NUMBA`, `HAS_PYARROW`, `HAS_DUCKDB`). The **pure-Python path is the source of record** and the parity oracle: numba JITs the *same* kernel code and must produce bit-identical output (REQ-ENG / Phase 4); the columnar read tier is feature-flagged and falls back to a **Postgres-identical** read (REQ-STORE / Phase 5). A committed hash-pinned lockfile captures exact numba/llvmlite/pyarrow/duckdb + transitive versions, with numba+llvmlite carrying BOTH `>=` floors AND upper ceilings (coupled JIT ABI), and the stack must NOT force a numpy/pandas downgrade below existing transitive floors (REQ-DEP-002).

**Consequences.**
- (+) Core `pip install` succeeds on any target Python; the canonical backtest runs pure-Python (CI job asserts this — REQ-DEP-001).
- (+) Each optimization rolls back independently via flag (REQ-ROLL).
- (−) Two execution paths per accelerated stage to test (guarded + fallback). Mitigated: a CI matrix simulates each module absent and asserts `backend.main` still imports + flag toggles to Postgres-identical reads (REQ-DEP-004).
- (−) New transitive CVE surface (pip-audit floors widen — discovery §10). Tracked in §8 Security.

---

# 2. System Context

The backtester is a **closed simulation** over *already-stored* signals: it never re-runs the LLM scanner. It consumes stored scan results as the signal source, prices from a layered kline store, and persists results to Postgres for the React frontend and the MCP sweep tooling.

## 2.0 Deployment Model — PINNED target + fleet-conditional scoping (R3-F2-batch4, Critical)

Earlier drafts designed against a **Linux container fleet** (cgroup CPU quotas §7.4, pgBouncer transaction-mode pooling §3.10, streaming-replica lag throttling §3.10/REQ-MIG-036, multi-pod advisory-lock election §3.10/§3.11, musl/Alpine wheels §11.1, multi-worker uvicorn §7.4) **while the project grounding + §3.6/§3.10 pin Windows 11 + `spawn`** — an unstated, self-contradicted environment. This section pins the real target and scopes each fleet-only requirement **IN or OUT**, so resource budgets, failover, and lock discipline are not sized against a phantom topology.

**PRIMARY (committed) target — single Windows 11 host, multiprocessing `spawn`:**
- **Process model:** ONE FastAPI process; the backtest engine shares it (`ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=_MAX_CONCURRENT=3)`, §7.4). Multi-worker uvicorn is **OUT** by default → §7.4 chooses the **single-worker constraint** (option (a)); the RSS watchdog budget is **per-process == the whole-host budget** (no aggregate-across-workers term needed unless the fleet variant is enabled).
- **Postgres topology:** a **single standalone primary**, **direct asyncpg** (no pgBouncer). Therefore the "session-pinned direct connection vs transaction-mode pooler" hazard (§3.10) is **defensive/forward-compatible**, not load-bearing here; replica-lag throttle (REQ-MIG-036) and streaming-replica offload (REQ-PERF-022) are **OUT** (no replica) — the throttle degrades to WAL/`pg_stat_activity` pressure only.
- **Orchestrator:** none / a Windows service or `systemd`-equivalent supervisor — NOT k8s. **Multi-pod advisory-lock election (§3.10/§3.11) is OUT** in the single-host target: exactly one instance runs, so the election lock guards only against an accidental second process on the same host (still acquired, but never contends fleet-wide). The **survivor re-election poll (REQ-MIG-025)** degrades to a same-host restart picking up the marker.
- **Wheels:** native Windows CPython wheels for numba/llvmlite/pyarrow/duckdb. **musl/Alpine lane is OUT** (no Linux container) — the §11.1 "numba may have no musl wheel" clause applies only to the fleet variant.
- **CPU budget source:** the host core count (NOT cgroup quota) — §7.4's "cgroup-derived ceiling" reads as **"cgroup quota if containerized, else host core count"** on this target.

**Restart discipline (PINNED for the PRIMARY target — R5-F4-batch4, High; scopes the v58 contention apparatus).** The committed restart model is **stop-then-start**: the old single FastAPI process is fully stopped (the live scanner with it) BEFORE the new process boots and runs migrations. Therefore, on the PRIMARY target, **there is NO concurrent live scanner during the v58 DDL window** — the entire ACCESS-EXCLUSIVE-contention apparatus (the `BT_COVERAGE_WRITE_PAUSE` scanner coverage-write gate §4.4, the submission-quiesce DRAIN, and even the savepoint-retry's *contention* role — the retry still guards against an accidental second process but normally never fires) is **[FLEET]-conditional dead-weight on the single-host path** and turns load-bearing ONLY under the SECONDARY fleet variant, where old+new pods overlap during a rolling deploy and a live scanner in pod-A races the DDL in pod-B. The single-host path asserts (test) that v58 runs its `ADD COLUMN`/constraint-swap with **no live `_update_coverage` writer present** (the scanner process is down), so the DDL is uncontended by construction. **Overlapping restart is NOT permitted on the PRIMARY target** (two concurrent FastAPI processes would each hold an up-to-150MB×3 engine RSS budget and double the live-trading footprint, violating the single-worker per-process RSS pin §7.4); an operator who wants zero-downtime overlap must enable the SECONDARY fleet variant (per-pod RSS budgeting, the aggregate connection-budget table §7.3, and the now-load-bearing coverage-write-gate/DRAIN). The deploy contract (§7.3) states the restart mode; the §4.4 scanner-gate/DRAIN bullets are tagged **[FLEET-load-bearing / PRIMARY-degenerate]** accordingly.

**SECONDARY (fleet variant, behind the deploy contract §7.3, scoped IN only when explicitly enabled):** a Linux container fleet (k8s/systemd, multi-pod, primary+replica, pgBouncer). When enabled, the fleet-only apparatus turns ON as a unit: cgroup-quota CPU derivation, pgBouncer-safe session-pinned direct connections, replica-lag throttle + replica read offload, **multi-pod** advisory-lock election + survivor re-election, musl wheel lane, and EITHER the multi-worker uvicorn shared-memory hot-tier option (§7.4 option (b)) OR per-pod single-worker. The **aggregate RSS budget** (§7.4) and the **connection-budget table** (§7.3) then apply across pods.

Every fleet-only requirement below is tagged **[FLEET]** at its site; on the PRIMARY target it is satisfied trivially (N=1 pod, N=1 worker, no replica) and its test asserts the degenerate case. The deploy contract (§7.3) states which target a given deploy is.



```
                         ┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
                         │                     TradingAgents backend (FastAPI)            │
                         │                                                                │
  ┌────────────┐ scans   │  ┌───────────────────┐    config dict (BacktestCreateRequest  │
  │ Stored     │────────▶│  │ BacktestService   │      .model_dump → config.get(...))     │
  │ scan_results│        │  │ (orchestration)   │                                         │
  │ (Postgres) │         │  │ backtest_service  │──signals──▶┌──────────────────┐         │
  └────────────┘         │  │ :83               │            │ BacktestEngine   │         │
                         │  │  _load_signals    │◀──klines───│ (pure sim loop)  │         │
  ┌────────────┐         │  │  _load_klines     │   (SoA)    │ backtest_engine  │         │
  │  Bybit     │  REST   │  │  load_inputs      │            │ :115 run()       │         │
  │  v5 public │◀────────│  │  run_one          │            └────────┬─────────┘         │
  │ /market/   │ (cold   │  └─────────┬─────────┘                     │ BacktestResults   │
  │  kline     │  gap    │            │                               ▼  (metrics,        │
  │  instrument│  only)  │   ┌────────▼─────────┐            ┌──────────────────┐  equity, │
  └────────────┘         │   │   KlineStore     │            │ backtest_metrics │  trades) │
        ▲                │   │ (NEW abstraction)│            │ :607 compute_all │         │
        │ fetch klines   │   │  read tiers ▼    │            └────────┬─────────┘         │
        │                │   │ Arrow▸Feather▸   │                     │ persist            │
  ┌─────┴──────────┐     │   │ Parquet▸Postgres │            ┌────────▼─────────┐         │
  │ KlineCache     │─────│──▶│  write: Postgres │───────────▶│ backtest_runs /  │         │
  │ Service :24    │ SOR │   │  SOR + manifest  │   upsert   │ _results/_trades │         │
  │ (write-of-rec) │     │   │  seal            │            │ (Postgres)       │         │
  └────────────────┘     │   └──────────────────┘            └────────┬─────────┘         │
                         │                                            │                   │
  ┌────────────────┐     │   ┌──────────────────┐                     │ GET /backtest/{id}│
  │ MCP sweep_tools│─────│──▶│ Sweep runner     │                     │ (LTTB-downsampled │
  │ :129 sweep_run │     │   │ (parallel,       │                     │  equity on read)  │
  │ optimize_config│     │   │  shared SoA)     │                     ▼                   │
  └────────────────┘     │   └──────────────────┘            ┌──────────────────┐         │
                         └────────────────────────────────────│ React frontend   │────────┘
                                                              │ BacktestResults  │
                                                              │ Page.tsx :255    │
                                                              └──────────────────┘
```

**Actors & boundaries:**

| Actor | Role | Contract held |
|-------|------|---------------|
| **Stored `scan_results` (Postgres)** | Signal source of record. `BacktestService._load_signals` (`backtest_service.py:523`) reads them by `scan_source`. | The engine never re-analyzes; signals are immutable inputs (discovery §3). |
| **Bybit v5 public REST** | Cold gap-fill ONLY. `KlineCacheService._fetch_klines_from_bybit` (`kline_cache_service.py`, `_BYBIT_KLINE_URL:18`); `InstrumentInfoCache.refresh` (`:516`). | Hit only for the `(max_stored_ts → frontier)` gap; sealed days never refetched (ADR-003). |
| **Postgres** | Write-of-record + forming-day SOR. `kline_cache` (partitioned), `kline_cache_coverage`+manifest, `backtest_runs/_results/_trades`. | Idempotent upserts preserved (discovery §5). |
| **NEW Parquet/Feather store** | Immutable columnar READ cache for sealed days. Operator-configurable dir (REQ-STORE-034). | Never the SOR; sealing independent of materialization (REQ-STORE-026). |
| **`BacktestEngine`** | Pure sync sim — **ZERO I/O**. Reads every field via `config.get(field, default)` mirroring schema defaults (discovery §2). | Semantically frozen (Prime Directive). |
| **MCP `sweep_tools` / `optimize_config`** | Param sweep; calls the pure engine directly, bypassing drilldown (discovery §2). `sweep_run:129`. | Same engine, shared read-only SoA (REQ-SWEEP-002/003). |
| **React frontend** | Consumes `BacktestResults`; `metrics.total_trades` gates the "no trades" fallback (`BacktestResultsPage.tsx:255`). | Backward-compatible JSON only (§5). |

**Run lifecycle (states `pending → running → completed/failed/cancelled`, discovery §4):**
`create_backtest` (`:191`, reserves a `_MAX_CONCURRENT=3` slot, per-client rate limit) → `_launch_background` (`:665`) → `_execute_backtest` (`:671`): cache warm-up owns `[0, _WARMUP_BAND=10%]`, then `load_inputs` (`:1254`) → Phase A coarse engine pass → optional Phase B drilldown (`_build_fine_klines:983`) → `compute_all_metrics` → `_persist_results` (`:1435`) → `_attach_buy_hold` (`:1331`). A `threading.Timer(_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=120)` (`:770`) cooperatively cancels via `threading.Event` (engine checks every 100 candles, `backtest_engine.py:1232`).

---

# 3. Component Architecture

Convention: **[NEW]** = net-new module/class; **[MODIFIED]** = existing file changed under the semantic-parity constraint; **[UNCHANGED-CONTRACT]** = behavior frozen, internals may be re-pointed. Phase tags map to the 7-phase rollout.

## 3.1 [NEW] `KlineStore` — layered read abstraction (Phase 2 seam, Phase 5 tiers)

**Module:** `backend/services/kline_store.py` (new). Owns the tiered READ; **delegates all WRITE to `KlineCacheService`** (unchanged SOR).

**Responsibility.** Resolve a `(symbol, interval, [start,end])` request through a single deterministic tier precedence, short-circuiting at the first hit and recording provenance (REQ-STORE-012):
`in-process Arrow/SoA hot frame → mmap'd Feather V2 → on-disk Parquet → Postgres SOR`.

**Interface.**
- `async get_klines_batch(symbols: list[str], interval, start: datetime, end: datetime) -> dict[str, KlineColumns]`
  - **Input:** dense symbol list (every requested symbol gets an entry, including zero-row negative-cached/unlisted symbols — REQ-STORE-018).
  - **Output:** per-symbol `KlineColumns{open_time: np.int64[], open/high/low/close/volume: np.float64[]}` (SoA-ready; int64-ms epoch, REQ-STORE-040). Strictly ascending, de-duplicated, byte-identical to a pure-Postgres read at every seam — cross-month, sealed↔forming boundary, multi-part-file month, per-day tier interleave (REQ-STORE-031/016).
  - **Errors:** corrupt/short-read partition → invalidate + rebuild-from-SOR or PG fallback (REQ-STORE-028); incompatible/unknown format stamp → rebuild from Postgres (REQ-STORE-029); columnar dir unwritable → degrade to Postgres + structured warning, never crash boot (REQ-STORE-034).
- `async iter_klines_streamed(symbols, interval, start, end, batch) -> AsyncIterator[dict[str, KlineColumns]]` — **streaming/chunked read seam (R1-F3, REQ-PERF-014/015).** The Postgres SOR read uses a **server-side cursor / bounded fetch batches** (NOT `pool.fetch()` which materializes ALL asyncpg `Record`s — ~2.6M+ rows canonical, ~21M wide — *before* SoA conversion, a transient peak far above final SoA size). Each batch fills the SoA incrementally and **releases its `Record`s as consumed**, so build-time peak RSS stays ≤ ~1.5× final SoA (REQ-PERF-014) instead of (materialized-records + SoA). **Streaming is scoped to the LOAD / SoA-BUILD stage ONLY — it bounds the load-peak TRANSIENT, it does NOT reduce RUN-stage residency (R2-F2-batch1, corrected).** The engine is a **cross-sectional shared-capital portfolio sim**: `_evaluate_candles_until` needs EVERY open symbol's price at each timeline tick to compute basket equity `E = wallet + Σ open-uPnL` (REQ-PAR-006), and signals/positions persist across the whole window — so symbol batch 1 **cannot** be released before batch 2 if a batch-1 position is still open (its mark is needed on every subsequent bar). **RUN-stage residency is the full SoA.** Consequently a run whose **FINAL SoA** exceeds the klines budget (≤150MB klines / within the 1GB ceiling, §7.4) is **REJECTED by `PreflightEstimator`** (or partitioned only when positions are *provably symbol-independent* — the same fast-path eligibility predicate, ADR-001) — it is **NOT** "streamed through." Streaming the load merely lets a run whose final SoA *fits* avoid a load-peak transient 2× over that SoA; it never makes an over-ceiling run feasible. (This reconciles R12, §7.4, §11.1, ADR-001/ADR-004.)
  - **Output:** per-symbol `KlineColumns{open_time: np.int64[], open/high/low/close/volume: np.float64[]}` (SoA-ready; int64-ms epoch, REQ-STORE-040). Strictly ascending, de-duplicated, byte-identical to a pure-Postgres read at every seam — cross-month, sealed↔forming boundary, multi-part-file month, per-day tier interleave (REQ-STORE-031/016).
  - **Errors:** corrupt/short-read partition → invalidate + rebuild-from-SOR or PG fallback (REQ-STORE-028); incompatible/unknown format stamp → rebuild from Postgres (REQ-STORE-029); columnar dir unwritable → degrade to Postgres + structured warning, never crash boot (REQ-STORE-034).
- `provenance() -> dict` per symbol/day: which tier served it + `content_sha256` verified (REQ-STORE-028, §9 observability).
- Internal: `_ProcessLRU` (bounded process-level LRU of `KlineColumns`, ≤150MB klines budget — §7), `_ArrowHotCache` (`{(symbol,interval,date-range): pa.Table}` zero-copy), `_FeatherMmap` (mmap'd Arrow IPC, OS-page-cached), `_DuckDBReader`/`_PolarsReader` (one long-lived connection, footers cached, warmed at boot — REQ-STORE-022).

**`KlineColumns` — the most-shared type, pinned home + shape contract (R2-F11-batch5, REQ-STORE-018/040).** `KlineColumns` is defined ONCE in `backend/services/kline_store.py` (its home module) and imported by `SoADatasetBuilder`, `DrilldownLoader`, and every consumer. Pinned definition: a **frozen `@dataclass(frozen=True, slots=True)`** (immutable) with fields `open_time: np.ndarray[int64]`, `open/high/low/close/volume: np.ndarray[float64]` — arrays **required non-None**, all the **same length**, `open_time` strictly ascending + de-duplicated. The **dense zero-row representation** (REQ-STORE-018) is the canonical empty instance: every array is a length-0 typed array (`np.empty(0, int64)` / `np.empty(0, float64)`), NOT `None` — so a negative-cached/unlisted symbol still yields a well-typed `KlineColumns` an SoA build can concatenate. A test pins the dtypes (int64/float64), the equal-length invariant, and the zero-row shape.

**ONE canonical `(symbol, interval)` normalization at ingress (R2-F12/R2-F5-batch4/5, REQ-CACHE-045/STORE-021).** A single canonicalization function `canon(symbol, interval)` is applied at the **ingress boundary** and its output is the ONLY form used by every keyed surface: signals, kline PK, manifest PK, `symbol_lifecycle`, the Bybit fetch ticker, the Parquet partition path, all in-process cache keys, and the symbol→int-code map. This prevents a signal `'BTCUSDT'` vs kline `'BTC/USDT'` silently failing the join. **`SAN(SYM)` (the reversible Parquet-path encoding) is applied AFTER `canon(...)`** — one canonical form in, one path out: `SAN` is the pinned reversible algorithm that percent/hex-encodes any byte not in `[A-Za-z0-9._-]` as `%XX` (uppercase hex, UTF-8 bytes; `%` itself escaped to `%25`), round-tripping to the exact canonical string. Tests: (a) alternate symbol/interval forms resolve to ONE `canon` key; (b) `SAN`+inverse round-trips `BTC/USDT` and an adversarial `'../'` symbol (path-traversal control).

**Cross-tier memory accounting — ONE budget owner (R2-F10-batch5, §7.4).** `_ProcessLRU`, `_ArrowHotCache`, and `_FeatherMmap` can all hold the **same** sealed key, so memory accounting has a single owner: **(a)** `_ArrowHotCache` `pa.Table` bytes and `_ProcessLRU` `KlineColumns` bytes **share ONE ≤150MB klines budget** (a key resident in both is counted once via a shared registry keyed by `(symbol,interval,date-range)`); **(b)** when the LRU evicts a key, the Arrow frame for the same key is evicted in the same step (no orphaned zero-copy view keeping bytes alive); **(c)** `_FeatherMmap` pages are **OS-paged and excluded from the 150MB RSS count** (they are reclaimable file-backed pages, not anonymous heap) — the §7.4 RSS watchdog budget is set to what the caches actually *retain on the heap*, so it never double-counts mmap. A test asserts a key in two tiers counts once and that LRU eviction cascades to the Arrow tier.

**Bounded fd / mmap-handle ceiling (R2-F21-batch4, REQ-STORE-033).** A wide multi-symbol multi-month run must not exhaust file descriptors (`EMFILE`) by opening every Feather/Parquet part at once. `_FeatherMmap`/the readers use **lazy-open + LRU-close** with a **configured open-handle ceiling**, and an **in-use refcount** so the GC/LRU **never closes a file that is currently mmap'd-and-being-read** (which would `SIGBUS` on next page touch). A test opens more parts than the ceiling and asserts the open-handle count stays bounded with no SIGBUS and no EMFILE.

**Read-mostly / lock-free hot-read path — REQ-PERF-025 owned HERE, not by §7.4 (R3-F3-batch1).** REQ-PERF-025 (concurrent runs must NOT serialize on a cache lock; the shared hot/LRU read path must be read-mostly / sharded / lock-free; 3-concurrent-run aggregate throughput ≥ **2.5×** single-run) is **re-mapped from the §7.4 CPU/thread row to `KlineStore`** — neither §7.4 nor §9.5 addresses cache-lock read-path contention, and a **classic LRU mutates recency order on every GET**, requiring a write-lock on the read path that serializes concurrent runs/combos exactly as REQ-PERF-025 forbids; the shared cross-tier accounting registry (above) would add a *second* hot-path lock. Pinned mechanism:
- **Recency without per-GET global mutation:** the `_ProcessLRU` uses a **CLOCK / second-chance** (or **sampled-LRU**) scheme — a GET sets a per-entry atomic "referenced" bit/timestamp (no global linked-list relink, no exclusive lock), and eviction is performed by a single bounded sweeper under a short lock only at insert/evict time, never on the read hot path. Concurrent GETs of resident keys take **no exclusive lock**.
- **Sharded / atomic accounting registry:** the shared `(symbol,interval,date-range)` byte-accounting registry is **sharded by key hash** (or maintained with **atomic counters**) so two runs touching different keys never contend; only a cross-tier *eviction* (rare) takes a shard lock.
- **Immutable, zero-copy handles:** `KlineColumns` is `frozen` and the kline arrays are `writeable=False` (§3.4 read-only-arrays contract), and Arrow/Feather handles are zero-copy, so a reader **borrows** bytes without copying or locking.
- **Gate:** a **3-concurrent-run aggregate-throughput test** asserts ≥2.5× single-run throughput over a shared hot working set (the gate REQ-PERF-025 previously had no owning component). This test lives in the §12.3 Performance row.

**Dependencies.** pyarrow (guarded `HAS_PYARROW`), duckdb/polars (guarded `HAS_DUCKDB`), `KlineCacheService` (SOR fallback always present), `SealedManifest` (tells the store a day is complete + which class).

**Parity contract.** With all columnar tiers flag-disabled, `get_klines_batch` returns exactly what `KlineCacheService.get_klines` returns today (`kline_cache_service.py:34`), float-for-float (REQ-DEP-004). **Forming-day snapshot isolation — isolation level PINNED (R1-F13 mig, R2-F9-batch1, REQ-STORE-030, R13).** The forming UTC day, **and any multi-batch server-side cursor read** (`iter_klines_streamed`), runs inside an **explicit `async with conn.transaction(isolation='repeatable_read')`** so all `FETCH` batches share **one snapshot** — closing the torn-seam hazard that asyncpg's default autocommit/READ COMMITTED reintroduces: under READ COMMITTED a multi-batch cursor can observe *different* snapshots across successive `FETCH`es as the live scanner commits forming-day rows between batches, exactly where the doc claims a torn bar is impossible. Pinning `repeatable_read` makes the whole cursor read point-in-time. When a read stitches replica-offloaded SEALED columnar data with the primary FORMING read (REQ-PERF-022 concurrent path), the consistency contract is explicit: either **all reads come from one `repeatable_read` snapshot**, or the **generation-token protocol** is used concretely — a generation token is **captured before the forming read and re-checked before stitching sealed+forming**, so a lagging-replica sealed read is never silently combined with a primary forming read at a different snapshot (no torn seam). A test interleaves live upserts between cursor `FETCH` batches and asserts a single coherent snapshot.

**Auxiliary-series forming-day snapshot coherency — same snapshot as the engine read (R3-F5-batch2, REQ-PAR-045, REQ-PERF-019).** REQ-PAR-045 requires the B&H baseline, `btc_vol`, and per-symbol MR-mean series to be valued off the **SAME forming-day snapshot the engine consumed**, while REQ-PERF-019 requires B&H to be fetched **concurrently** with the main load (its own connection/transaction). A concurrent aux fetch on a **different pooled connection** runs in its OWN transaction and can observe a **different** forming-day snapshot (the live scanner commits forming-day rows between the two reads) — so when `BTC/USDT` is both traded and the B&H baseline, the engine's BTC marks and the B&H BTC series can diverge by one or more forming bars, a silent parity break the §3.1 snapshot contract otherwise covers only for the engine's own read. Pinned resolution: the concurrent aux reads run under the **SAME `repeatable_read` snapshot** as the engine forming read (a shared exported snapshot id via `pg_export_snapshot()` + `SET TRANSACTION SNAPSHOT`), OR the **generation token is captured before the engine forming read and re-validated on every aux read**, rejecting/retrying on mismatch. A test interleaves a live forming-day upsert between the engine load and the concurrent B&H/`btc_vol`/MR-mean fetch and asserts **identical forming-bar values**.

**Streaming-cursor timeout survival + pool-held-connection budget (R3-F5-batch5, REQ-PERF-021/015).** `iter_klines_streamed` holds a pooled asyncpg connection inside an explicit `repeatable_read` transaction for the **entire** load/SoA-build stage so all `FETCH` batches share one snapshot, and it **pauses between batches** while the SoA is built — held OPEN longer than a `SealBackfillRunner` chunk. It therefore gets the **same §4.4 armor**: `SET LOCAL statement_timeout` per batch + batches sized short enough to survive any server-global `idle_in_transaction_session_timeout` (a prod cluster with that GUC set would otherwise kill the cursor mid-stream). The held-connection count is reconciled against the §3.6 asyncpg pool `max_size` sizing — `live-baseline + _MAX_CONCURRENT×per-run-stream + sweep-read cap` — so 3 concurrent streaming runs + the live scanner cannot exhaust the pool. A "streaming cursor survives a short idle/statement timeout" test mirrors the backfill one.

## 3.2 [NEW] `SealedManifest` + completion-frontier (Phase 1 logic, Phase 5 materialized-state)

**Module:** `backend/services/sealed_manifest.py` (new) — manifest read/seal logic over the **v58-extended `kline_cache_coverage`** table.

**Responsibility.** Replace count-vs-expected gap detection (ADR-003) with seal-state truth. Owns:
- `completion_frontier(interval, now) -> int64_ms` = `floor((now − skew_margin) / T) * T`, a **monotonic ratchet** from one authoritative UTC clock (REQ-CACHE-006, §4.2). Bars with `open_time ≥ frontier` are forming — never sealed, never columnar-written (REQ-STORE-006/030). This is the **identical** function `SealBackfillRunner` calls (REQ-MIG-012).
- `async unsealed_days(symbols, interval, start, end) -> dict[str, list[date]]` — the **only** thing the gap-fill loop fetches: unsealed days in `[start, min(end, frontier)]`, bounded by each symbol's `[listing_time, delist_time]` from `symbol_lifecycle` (NULL ⇒ fetch-everything — REQ-MIG-009). Sealed days return empty → 0 Bybit calls (REQ-STORE-009). **Until `seal_backfill_marker.state = 'complete'`, SOR-present-but-unsealed days are treated as refetchable-but-WARM, not as cache-miss** (REQ-MIG-022).
- `async seal_days(symbol, interval, days, day_class, content_sha256, sha_version)` — commits seal **LAST**, after durable Postgres rows (REQ-STORE-026); upsert on `(symbol,interval,date)` (REQ-MIG-039). Seal predicate includes the `[listing,delist]` bound (REQ-MIG-011); `day_class` derived from a single `GROUP BY` over **actual** `kline_cache` rows, never `count >= expected` (REQ-MIG-013). Seal-upsert failure after rows are durable is **non-fatal** (run completes oracle-identical; day stays unsealed for next-run lazy-seal — REQ-CACHE-050).
- Day-CLASS taxonomy (REQ-STORE-009): `sealed-full`, `sealed-short-listing`, `sealed-interior-structural-gap`, `sealed-empty-negative` (negative cache for pre-listing/post-delist/known-gap — never re-probed), `sealed-delist-snapped` (count-free via explicit `delisted`/`listing_snapped` markers), `derived-coarse` (REQ-STORE-024).
- **`symbol_lifecycle` ownership.** Reads the v58 `symbol_lifecycle(symbol, listing_time, delist_time)` table (created by the v58 DDL, **populated/refreshed by the first-class `SymbolLifecycleRefresher` component, §3.11** — REQ-CACHE-026). The `sealed-empty-negative` class has no data source without it; an absent row means fetch-everything, NEVER seal-known-empty (REQ-MIG-009 invariant), so a wrong lifecycle can never hide real data behind a permanent negative cache.
- **Backfill marker ownership.** Reads/writes `seal_backfill_marker` (states `not_started`/`in_progress`/`complete`/`complete_with_skips` + progress counters + skip set, restart-survivable — REQ-MIG-021/022). This marker is the **sole gate** for the "cache-complete / fully-optimized" signal and the optimization-enable rollout gate (REQ-OBS-035/038/039); `SealBackfillRunner` (§3.10) is the only writer that flips unsealed→sealed in bulk.
- SEALED (manifest commit) vs MATERIALIZED (Parquet fsync'd+renamed) are **distinct** states (REQ-STORE-027): a crash leaving file-present/flag-false or flag-true/file-missing self-heals (adopt-after-sha-verify or atomic re-materialize).

**Interface errors.** OHLC sanity failure pre-seal → record sub-range as confirmed gap, never store-and-seal (REQ-STORE-007). **Seal-guard at the WRITE seam — owned by `KlineCacheService.store_klines`, NOT `SealedManifest` (R2-F4-batch2, REQ-STORE-005).** A novel `open_time` landing in a sealed day must be **rejected/structured-logged, not silently absorbed**. The subtlety: `store_klines` issues `INSERT … ON CONFLICT (symbol,interval,open_time) DO NOTHING` (`kline_cache_service.py:100-109`), and `ON CONFLICT` only suppresses **duplicate** PKs — a **novel** `open_time` is a *new* PK and is silently INSERTED, mutating a sealed day while its `content_sha256` goes stale and `_update_coverage` bumps `candle_count` via GREATEST (so REQ-STORE-028 reads then fail/rebuild forever). The seal lookup therefore lives **at the candle INSERT seam in `KlineCacheService.store_klines`** (the manifest never sees that write path): before inserting into a sealed `(symbol,interval,date)`, novel-`open_time` rows are routed to **reject + structured-log** (via a seal lookup, or a partial unique/exclusion constraint, or a BEFORE-INSERT trigger). The **recovery contract** is explicit: an accepted restatement triggers explicit **re-verify → re-seal + sha recompute** (it does not silently absorb). A test asserts a novel bar into a sealed day is rejected/logged, not silently absorbed.

**Dependencies.** Postgres (`kline_cache_coverage` v58 columns), `KlineCacheService` (durable rows precede seal).

## 3.3 [NEW] `SoADatasetBuilder` — columnar dataset + global timeline (Phase 3)

**Module:** `backend/services/soa_dataset.py` (new). Pure CPU, no I/O.

**Responsibility.** Convert the `dict[str, KlineColumns]` from `KlineStore` into the engine's runtime substrate, built **once per run** before the scan loop (REQ-SWEEP-003):
- **Degenerate-run early-out FIRST (R1-F10 dup, REQ-PERF-044).** Before any SoA/timeline construction, an orchestrator pre-check: if **admitted-signals == 0 OR symbols == 0 OR the window is empty**, **skip the SoA + global-timeline build entirely** and return a real zero-trade result with **`metrics.total_trades` present and `== 0`** (never absent — the frontend trap §5.2), under a **<100ms warm** budget. The full setup cost is NOT paid for no data. This also covers the golden NO-OP guarantee (empty `instrument_info`/`scan_contexts`) which must be byte-identical AND fast. **Parity routing is pinned (R3-F8-batch5):** the early-out skips ONLY the SoA/timeline BUILD — it then feeds the empty inputs through the **identical `compute_all_metrics` + `_attach_buy_hold` + `_persist_results` code path** the full engine uses, so every one of the ~45 metric keys, the seeded `equity_curve` shape, and the buy&hold attachment are **byte-identical to a full-engine run that simply opened zero trades**. It MUST NOT hand-construct a zero-trade `BacktestMetrics`/curve/B&H (that silently diverges from the full path on seeded-equity points, B&H value, and summary slices). A fixture gates BOTH the <100ms latency AND the `total_trades`-present-and-0 invariant, with a **separate case per early-out trigger** (zero-signals-with-symbols, empty-window, zero-symbols), each asserted byte-identical to the full-engine zero-trade output — not just the single NO-OP fixture.
- Per-symbol SoA arrays (already int64/float64 from the store; zero-copy from Arrow via `to_numpy(zero_copy_only=True)` / `np.frombuffer`, asserted to share the Arrow buffer — REQ-STORE-019).
- A **global sorted-unique timeline** via k-way merge of per-symbol pre-sorted ascending arrays (no per-scan sort; transient peak ≤ ~1.5× final array — REQ-STORE-017).
- **Build-stage memory peak is a SECOND transient, distinct from the load transient, and is budgeted (R4-F5-batch6-c2 + R5-F8-batch1, §7.4).** The merge that converts `dict[str, KlineColumns]` → global SoA + timeline holds BOTH the per-symbol **input** arrays AND the merged **output** arrays resident at once — a peak that the streaming load seam (§3.1, which only bounds Postgres-`Record`→`KlineColumns`) does NOT bound. "Pure CPU" (below) does NOT mean "free memory". **The "consumes-and-releases each `KlineColumns` incrementally" option is STRUCK as a peak-capping mechanism for the timeline build (R5-F8-batch1, Medium — it is incompatible with the merge).** The global sorted-unique timeline is built by a **k-way merge of the per-symbol pre-sorted ascending `open_time` arrays**, which by construction requires **ALL per-symbol `open_time` arrays resident simultaneously** (the merge repeatedly compares the current heads of every symbol's array) — and each symbol's `open_time` array is ALSO retained as the per-symbol SoA for the WHOLE run. So per-symbol inputs **cannot** be released during the timeline merge; "cap the peak near 1× by incremental release" is unachievable for the timeline portion. **Pinned (sole mechanism):** the build-stage peak is **budgeted by the PreflightEstimator** as the §3.9 *SoA-BUILD transient term*, and that term is **re-derived as `input-SoA + O(unique-timestamps) timeline`** (the genuine bound) rather than a generic "2× inputs+outputs" — i.e. all per-symbol input arrays stay resident (they are the run's SoA) PLUS the growing union timeline of size `O(distinct timestamps)`. A wide run whose `input-SoA + timeline` build peak would breach the ceiling is admitted/queued at pre-flight rather than caught by the runtime RSS watchdog. A `tracemalloc` test pins the build-stage peak against this `input-SoA + O(unique-timestamps)` bound (NOT against a released-inputs 1× bound, which the k-way merge cannot deliver). **The runtime RSS watchdog (§7.4) covers this build-stage transient via its independent wall-clock sampler (R4-F5-batch6-c4)** — the SoA build runs BEFORE the first engine chunk, so a between-chunk-only watchdog would not see it; the wall-clock sampler fires throughout load+build+merge, and an abort-during-SoA-build test asserts a build spike is preempted before OOM.
- A dense, stable `symbol → contiguous-int-code` mapping (every requested symbol present, even zero-row — REQ-STORE-018), so Phase 4 can index by int.
- Memoized coarse-interval derivation: each distinct coarse TF (15m/1h/4h) derived from the sealed 5m base exactly once and reused across all sweep combos of that interval (REQ-SWEEP-004).

**Interface.** `build(klines: dict[str, KlineColumns], interval) -> SoADataset{codes, open_time[code], ohlcv[code], global_timeline}`. **Errors:** empty array / single-candle / signal-time-before-first / at-or-after-last all map to the documented SKIP/`no-prior-mark` semantics with no `IndexError` (REQ-ENG-006).

**Dependencies.** numpy (already transitively present), `KlineStore`. **No numba** (pure substrate; Phase 4 consumes it).

**SoA/timeline build runs OFF the asyncio loop thread (R3-F9-batch5, REQ-PERF-029, §9.5).** The SoA + global-timeline k-way merge is **pure CPU, O(total_candles)** (≈1.3M candles canonical, more when wide) — a multi-hundred-ms-to-seconds burst that sits at the async/sync seam (after the async `iter_klines_streamed` load, before the sync threadpool engine). It MUST run **inside the `ThreadPoolExecutor` (the same executor the engine runs in)**, NOT on the asyncio loop thread — building it on the loop thread would block the live auto-trade coroutines exactly as §9.5 warns, and the loop-lag SLI would only *detect* it after the fact. Pinned: the build is dispatched to the executor (or interleaved per streamed batch off-loop). §7.4's "columnar materialization off the loop" rule is extended to cover the SoA/timeline build, and the §9.5 loop-lag assertion window is extended to span the SoA-build stage (not just engine run + materialization).

**Decimal→float64 transition is PINNED at P3 (R2-F2-batch4, REQ-STORE-040 corrected, REQ-PAR-016/017).** The engine math representation changes lane at a single, named boundary: **P0–P2 the engine stays Decimal** (the current representation; golden master is byte-identical to the string→Decimal oracle). **P3 is where engine math converts to float64** — the SoA arrays are float64 (OHLCV) + int64 (epoch), and `_evaluate_candles_until`'s wallet/equity/uPnL accumulation runs in float64 from P3 onward (the ≥150k evals/s pure-Python floor §11.2 is infeasible in Decimal, confirming P3 is already float64 — the numba kernel in P4 inherits the SAME float64 math, it does not introduce it). **REQ-STORE-040 is corrected:** "lossless bit-identical float64↔Decimal" is mathematically impossible; the requirement means **float64 is the frozen, oracle-diffed representation** — the single epoch unit (int64-ms) is lossless, but money is float64 and is diffed against the Decimal oracle within a pinned epsilon (non-optimistic), not byte-equated to it. REQ-PAR-016/017 phase tags align to this P3 boundary.

## 3.4 [NEW] `engine_kernel` — numba `@njit` per-candle kernel + pure-Python fallback of record (Phase 4)

**Module:** `backend/services/engine_kernel.py` (new). Guarded `HAS_NUMBA`.

**Responsibility.** JIT the per-candle hot math (funding → per-position liq/TP/SL → equity cascade → trailing → time, REQ-PAR-002) over the SoA arrays + numpy structured-array position struct. The **pure-Python implementation is the source of record and the parity oracle** (ADR-005); `@njit` decorates the *same* logic and must be bit-identical.

**Interface — CHUNKED entrypoint, NOT per-candle (R2-F7, REQ-DEP-018, REQ-ENG-025).** `step_chunk(state_arrays, soa, ptrs, chunk_start, chunk_len, config_scalars) -> events[]` — the entrypoint loops bars **internally in nopython** over `[chunk_start, chunk_start+chunk_len)`, so Python↔nopython dispatch is **O(chunks), not O(candles)** (a per-candle `step_candle` entrypoint would pay a nopython dispatch every bar — ~1.3M crossings on the canonical fixture — violating REQ-DEP-018). Between chunks (back in Python) the orchestrator checks the cooperative cancel `threading.Event` and emits progress, giving cancel/timeout latency ≤250ms (REQ-API-013/REQ-ENG-025) without per-bar overhead. Chunk length `N` is chosen so a chunk runs ≪250ms (e.g. a few thousand bars). Operates on int-coded arrays only (numba-compatible types: int64, float64, bool). Portfolio cascade and stateful latches (`smart_drawdown_fired`, `cycle_start_equity`, funding `(date,hour)` dedupe) stay in the kernel as scalar/array state, preserving REQ-PAR-002/003/004 ordering.

**Mutable-state ownership boundary — the most-implemented interface, fully enumerated (R2-F1 dup, REQ-PAR-002/003).** Every `SimulationState` field is classified KERNEL-mutated (intra-chunk, intra-candle) vs ORCHESTRATOR-mutated (scan-level transitions, between chunks), and the cross-boundary representation is a **fixed-layout scratch-array contract** (no Python objects cross the `@njit` boundary):
  - **Kernel-mutated, in place, every candle:** open-position SoA fields (qty, entry, uPnL, latch flags), `wallet`/`cash`, the funding `(date,hour)` dedupe bitmap (precomputed boundary indices, §below), per-position trailing-peak, `smart_drawdown_fired`, `cycle_start_equity`. These live in fixed-index slots of integer/float scratch arrays; the kernel writes them by index.
  - **Orchestrator-mutated, between chunks only:** scan-cursor advance, cancel-Event check, progress emission, cross-scan cycle reset, drilldown hand-off. The kernel NEVER mutates scan-level cursors; the orchestrator NEVER mutates intra-candle latches.
  - **Representation:** a documented **index map** (`IDX_WALLET=0, IDX_CYCLE_START_EQUITY=1, …`) over a single `float64[]` "state scalars" array + a single `int64[]` "state ints" array, both writeable, owned per-run (never shared across concurrent runs — see read-only-arrays contract §3.6/below). The kernel mutates in place via these indices and returns `events[]` deltas; it does NOT return a new state object. A test pins the index map and asserts no field is mutated on the wrong side of the boundary.

**numba nopython lowering plan (R1-F6, REQ-PAR-002/003/004 vs the 5M/s floor).** Several per-candle operations verified in `backtest_engine.py` do NOT lower to numba nopython as written, threatening both the 5M/s floor and the bit-identical-JIT claim; each gets an explicit kernel-compatible form:
- **Funding boundary dedupe** keys on Python `datetime` `(candle_time.date(), candle_time.hour)` (`:1251`) — `datetime.date()/.hour` are not nopython-lowerable. → **Precompute funding-boundary bar indices** from the int64 epoch timeline **before** the loop (a `bool[]`/`int64[]` of boundary candles); zero `datetime` in-kernel. **Precompute semantics are pinned to reproduce `(date,hour)` EXACTLY, NOT epoch-modulo (R4-F2-batch6-c3, REQ-PAR-013):** the legacy key fires on the FIRST bar whose wall-clock `(date,hour)` lands in an uncharged funding slot {0,8,16}h — so if the exact `08:00:00` bar is missing/misaligned (gap, staggered listing, coarse granularity), legacy still charges on the next in-hour bar (e.g. `08:05`, whose `.hour==8`). A naive epoch-modulo mark (`epoch % 8h == 0`) marks NO bar for that boundary and **SKIPS the charge** — a silent parity break dense-bar fixtures cannot catch. Pinned form: mark the **FIRST stored bar whose translated UTC datetime falls in each uncharged funding `(date,hour)` slot** (not the exact-epoch bar), computed once from the int64 timeline by translating each candle's epoch to UTC `(date,hour)` and taking the first occurrence per uncharged slot — so a missing exact-boundary bar still charges on the next in-hour bar, bit-identical to the legacy `(date,hour)` dedupe regardless of candle granularity. A **frozen fixture with a gapped/missing exact-boundary bar AND a staggered-listing case** asserts the precomputed-index charge set is bit-identical to the legacy `(date,hour)` set; it is added to the §12.3 SSOT formula-differential grid and the bar-by-bar trajectory harness (REQ-TEST-033).
- **Adaptive-blacklist** (`_is_adaptively_blacklisted :1083/:660`) scans the run's own trade history per-symbol-path. → Replace the per-position history scan with a **window-aware O(1)/amortized counter structure** updated on each close (REQ-PERF-010), NOT plain cumulative counters. **The legacy formula is a SLIDING-WINDOW win-rate (R3-F6-batch5):** it counts only trades whose `exit_time >= current_time − lookback_hours` (default 48h) with `min_trades`/`max_win_rate` thresholds, so trades that **age out of the lookback must drop from both `wins` and `total`** — a naive cumulative O(1) counter cannot reproduce window expiry and would diverge on any `adaptive_blacklist_enabled` config. Pinned form: a **time-bucketed ring of per-symbol `(wins, total)` counters** keyed to the lookback granularity, expiring buckets as simulated time advances (amortized O(1) per close + O(expired buckets) per tick). It must be **bit-identical to the legacy windowed scan** over a fixture that **crosses the lookback boundary**. Because this is a *formula* (not a constant), it is added to the §12.3 SSOT formula-level differential grid.
- **Open positions** held as `dict[str,list[Position]]` / dataclasses with `Optional` tuple state (`:62,:110,:112`). → Define an explicit **numpy structured-array / jitclass position layout** (int-coded symbol, float64 fields, int8 flags; `Optional`→sentinel) so the book is array-indexable in-kernel.
- **Any op that still cannot lower** stays OUTSIDE the `@njit` kernel **on the pure-Python path too** (so both paths run identical logic), and a **nopython-compile assertion test** (`njit(..., error_model)`, no object-mode fallback permitted) fails the build if the kernel silently drops to object mode (no speedup, broken parity claim).

**Epoch-translation determinism (REQ-PAR-032) is scoped against absolute-UTC funding (REQ-PAR-013) — pinned, not contradictory (R4-F10-batch6-c3).** REQ-PAR-032 requires byte-identical output under a **constant time-translation of all epochs**, but REQ-PAR-013 charges funding at **absolute UTC {0,8,16}h** boundaries via the legacy `(date,hour)` key — so a constant epoch shift Δ that is **not a whole multiple of the 8h funding grid (and midnight-aligned for the date rollover)** legitimately MOVES which bars land in a funding hour, changing funding charges. This is true of the legacy engine too; arbitrary-Δ invariance for a funding-enabled config is **genuinely false**, not a bug. So the REQ-PAR-032 determinism guard is pinned to hold in exactly two forms, and the §12.3 determinism fixture is **split** accordingly: **(1) funding-OFF, arbitrary-Δ** — with `funding_rate_model='none'`, output is byte-identical under ANY constant epoch translation; **(2) funding-ON, grid-aligned-Δ** — with funding enabled, invariance is asserted ONLY for Δ constrained to **whole-multiples-of-8h AND day-aligned** shifts (which preserve every `(date,hour)` funding slot). The doc records that absolute-UTC funding makes arbitrary-Δ translation legitimately non-invariant, so the guard is **correct rather than over-broad** (an arbitrary-Δ funding-on determinism test would false-fail). This split is added to §12.3 alongside the funding `(date,hour)` differential.

**Pinned kernel compilation flags — float-determinism is not optional (R2-F3, REQ-ENG-023, REQ-DEP-016/019/020, REQ-PAR-033).** The kernel decorator and lowering discipline are fixed, not left to the implementer:
- **`@njit(nogil=True, cache=True, fastmath=False, boundscheck=False)`** — pinned. `fastmath=False` is a MUST: `fastmath=True` permits reassociation/FMA contraction that breaks bit-identity vs the pure-Python/Decimal oracle (REQ-ENG-023). `cache=True` amortizes JIT across runs/sweeps. `boundscheck=False` in **prod**, with a **separate CI lane compiling `boundscheck=True`** so an out-of-bounds index is caught in test rather than corrupting memory in prod (REQ-DEP-019).
- **`nogil=True` is load-bearing** (R2-F3-runtime): three runtime-safety mechanisms require the GIL released during the hot loop — (a) the cooperative 120s cancel `threading.Event` checked **between chunks** (the chunked entrypoint above), (b) the §9.5 always-on event-loop-lag sampler + §7.4 RSS watchdog scheduled on the asyncio loop, (c) live-coroutine non-starvation. Without `nogil=True` a JIT'd run cannot be cancelled or watchdog-aborted and the loop-lag SLI flatlines for the kernel's duration. The chunked `step_chunk` returns to Python every `N` candles so the cancel Event, watchdog, and loop-lag sampler all get scheduled — this is the in-kernel cancellation/heartbeat contract. (Alternative, documented but not default: run the kernel in a separate process.) REQ-PERF-029's GIL-yield assertion and the cancel/timeout/watchdog tests are extended to the **numba lane**, not just pure-Python.
- **Eager single-signature compile (REQ-DEP-016):** the kernel is compiled with one **explicit eager type signature** (no lazy multi-signature dispatch that could pick a divergent specialization at runtime).
- **No reflected `list`/`dict` (REQ-DEP-020):** the kernel uses only typed numpy arrays / scalars — reflected Python containers are prohibited (they break nopython and determinism).
- **Deterministic left-to-right book reduction (R2-F6, REQ-ENG-023, REQ-PAR-011/033):** basket equity `E = wallet + Σ open-uPnL` and the carried-uPnL summation are accumulated by a **sequential scalar loop in stable insertion order** — NOT `np.sum`/numpy pairwise reduction (pairwise float64 accumulation rounds differently than the legacy scalar left-to-right loop, a silent bit-identity break the 5m no-drill golden master must catch). The position struct-of-arrays **preserves insertion order across opens/closes** via **stable compaction (shift-down), NOT swap-remove** (swap-remove reorders the book and changes the summation order). A property test asserts a permuted-but-equivalent book and a vectorized `np.sum` are **REJECTED as non-identical**, and the kernel matches the Decimal/sequential oracle bit-for-bit on discrete fields (REQ-PAR-018).

**Decimal→float64 transition is pinned at Phase 3 (R2-F1/F2-numeric, REQ-PAR-016/017/018, REQ-STORE-040 corrected).** The numeric representation changes phase: **P0–P2 the engine math is `Decimal`** (string→Decimal oracle, REQ-TEST-002) and the 5m no-drill `equity_curve` is **byte-identical** to the oracle; **from P3 onward the SoA math is `float64`** (Decimal at 150k evals/s is infeasible — §11.2). Therefore money/equity **cannot remain byte-identical to a Decimal oracle once float64 lands**: from P3 the gate is **discrete fields bit-identical (trade selection, fire order, counts — REQ-PAR-018) + money within a pinned ε** (the float64 curve IS the frozen, oracle-diffed representation, REQ-STORE-040 corrected — "float64 is the frozen representation", NOT "lossless bit-identical vs Decimal", which is mathematically impossible). The Prime Directive 5m-no-drill gate is restated phase-dependent accordingly (see Prime Directive edit). REQ-PAR-016/017 phase tags align to this P2→P3 boundary.

**Position book — preallocated fixed-capacity SoA, zero hot-loop alloc (R2-F14, REQ-ENG-019/026).** The position book is a **preallocated fixed-capacity** struct-of-arrays sized at run setup by an explicit capacity formula: `cap = max_trades + mr_max_trades + carried_cycle_slack`, where `carried_cycle_slack` covers positions carried across cycle boundaries (a previous cycle's still-open positions coexisting with the next cycle's opens). Open/close are **zero-heap-alloc** index operations into the preallocated arrays (REQ-ENG-026 ~0 alloc in the hot loop). On the rare capacity-exhaustion path a **documented grow-once policy** (double capacity, copy, never per-open realloc) applies; the formula is sized so grow-once is essentially never hit in practice. A test asserts no per-open/close heap allocation in the steady state and that capacity covers the max simultaneous open set incl. carried cycles.

**Kernel-vs-Python division of labor — pinned per scan (R4-F10-batch6-c2, REQ-CFG-001, REQ-DEP-018, REQ-PAR-010/011).** The boundary of WHAT runs in `@njit` vs Python at each scan is load-bearing for parity AND the O(chunks) crossing budget, so it is fixed explicitly:
- **Python-side, per scan (sequential, never in nopython):** the full **17-step filter chain** (REQ-CFG-001 — incl. string-keyed `symbol_blacklist`/`whitelist`, `confidence_filter`, sector concentration — impossible in nopython), **position sizing** (REQ-PAR-010/011 — running wallet + carried uPnL − Σ locked_margin, sequential depletion across scans), and the **OPEN decision** (which signals become positions). These run in the orchestrator between kernel chunks; string-keyed steps NEVER enter nopython.
- **Kernel-side, per candle-chunk (nopython):** the per-candle **exit/equity/trailing/time math** over the already-open book (funding → liq → TP/SL → equity-cascade → trailing → time, REQ-PAR-002), the basket-equity reduction, and the latch updates. One nopython `step_chunk` call per candle-chunk.
- **Consequences this pins:** (a) crossings stay **O(chunks)**, NOT O(scans × signals) — the filter/size/open work is amortized in the Python layer that already owns the scan cursor; (b) the filter chain provably stays Python-side so REQ-CFG-001's string predicates never threaten nopython; (c) sizing stays **sequential** (REQ-PAR-010/011) because opens are a Python-side scan walk (consistent with ADR-001's "opens + wallet-path sizing remain the sequential scan walk"). A **boundary-crossing counter test** asserts the per-run nopython-dispatch count is O(chunks) (≈ candles/`N`), not O(scans×signals), and a **filter-chain-stays-Python test** asserts no string-keyed step is reachable from the `@njit` entrypoint.
