**Chunk length `N` is pinned relative to the cancel/RSS sampling granularity (R4-F11-batch6-c2, REQ-API-013, §7.4).** The cooperative cancel `threading.Event` and the §7.4 RSS watchdog are checked only **between chunks** on the Python side (the nopython kernel cannot read a `threading.Event` or sample RSS mid-chunk). `N` is therefore capped so a chunk runs **≪ the legacy 100-candle cancel cadence in wall-time** — i.e. the cancel/watchdog check fires **at least as often as** legacy's every-100-candles granularity (`backtest_engine.py:1232`), and the **worst-case cancel/abort latency is documented as one chunk** (≤250ms target, REQ-API-013). `N` is additionally bounded by a **per-chunk RSS-growth ceiling**: a single chunk's allocations must not be able to spike RSS past the §7.4 ceiling before the between-chunks watchdog can preempt — so `N` × (per-candle transient bytes) ≪ headroom. Tests: a **cancel-latency-on-the-numba-lane** test asserts cancel halts within the bounded chunk window, and an **RSS-watchdog-preempts-before-a-single-chunk-breaches** test asserts one chunk cannot breach the ceiling between checks.

**Kernel↔service event protocol — schema + deterministic application order (R2-F15, REQ-PAR-002).** `step_chunk` returns an `events[]` array whose record layout is pinned: each event is a fixed-width tuple `(event_type, bar_index, symbol_code, price_f64, qty_f64, pnl_f64, reason_code)` where `event_type ∈ {OPEN=0, CLOSE=1, FUNDING=2, LIQUIDATION=3, EQUITY_FLATTEN=4}`. The Python side reconstructs trades + `equity_curve` by applying events in **deterministic order**: events are emitted in the kernel in the exact cascade order (funding → liq → TP/SL → equity-cascade close → trailing → time, REQ-PAR-002) and **within a bar** are ordered by `(bar_index, event_type, symbol insertion order)` — never reordered by the service. Event application order is parity-sensitive (REQ-PAR-002 cascade order); a test pins the event schema + application order against the oracle.

**CLOSE event carries the kernel-only trade quantities — the 7-field tuple is INSUFFICIENT for trade-record parity (R3-F2-batch5, REQ-PAR-018).** The frozen trade record built in `_close_position` (`backtest_engine.py:1436-1455`) carries **four kernel-computed quantities that are accumulated only inside the per-candle hot loop and cannot be reconstructed Python-side from `(pnl, reason_code)` alone:** `mfe_pct`/`mae_pct` (from per-candle `max_favorable_price`/`max_adverse_price` running extremes, engine `:1277-1281`), `fees_paid` (`entry_fee + exit_fee + funding_paid`), and `funding_paid` (accumulated per funding boundary in-kernel, `:1257-1263`). A CLOSE event emitting only `pnl`+`reason_code` discards them, so the reconstructed ~18-key trade record is missing fields the golden master froze and the P4 bit-identical-discrete-fields gate (REQ-PAR-018) is unverifiable. Pinned: the **CLOSE event is widened** (or a paired `CLOSE_DETAIL` event is emitted) to carry the per-position `mfe_price`/`mae_price` (or precomputed `mfe_pct`/`mae_pct`), `entry_fee`, `exit_fee`, and `funding_paid`, so the Python side reconstructs the full trade record bit-identically. The close `reason_code`→`close_reason` map is a **frozen enum, fully enumerated (R4-F5-batch6-c3, REQ-TEST-008)** — the engine emits a string, the kernel an int, and trade-record `close_reason` parity (REQ-PAR-018 discrete-field bit-identity) depends entirely on this int↔string map since `event_type` alone is too coarse (one `EQUITY_FLATTEN` event_type covers FOUR equity reasons; `CLOSE` covers the time/trailing family). The `reason_code` enum covers all **12** `close_reason` values and lives in a **shared constants module imported by BOTH the kernel and the trade-record reconstructor** (`backend/services/engine_kernel_constants.py` or equivalent — a zero-dependency module, no engine/accel import): `take_profit`, `stop_loss`, `liquidation`, `equity_drop`, `equity_drop_smart`, `close_on_profit`, `equity_rise`, `trailing_profit`, `breakeven_timeout`, `max_duration`, `mr_time_stop`, `backtest_end`. The coarse `event_type` and the fine `reason_code` are distinguished thus: **`EQUITY_FLATTEN` event_type → `reason_code ∈ {equity_drop, equity_drop_smart, close_on_profit, equity_rise}`** (the four portfolio-equity sub-reasons); **`CLOSE` event_type → `reason_code ∈ {take_profit, stop_loss, trailing_profit, breakeven_timeout, max_duration, mr_time_stop, backtest_end}`**; **`LIQUIDATION` event_type → `reason_code = liquidation`**. The §3.4 event-schema test pins the int↔string map AND asserts **union coverage of all 12 reasons** on the reconstructed records (REQ-TEST-008); the §12.3 canary-defect battery flips a reason_code and asserts the reconstructed `close_reason` diverges. The widened schema is added to the §3.4 event-schema test AND the §12.3 canary-defect battery.

**`equity_curve` reconstruction is pinned — the event stream alone is insufficient at two seams (R4-F1-batch6-c2, REQ-PAR-022).** The event stream is the sole Python←kernel channel, but rebuilding the golden-frozen `equity_curve` from it is under-specified at two points the golden master pins, so both are made explicit:
- **Which events emit a curve point.** A curve point `(ts, equity, drawdown_pct)` is emitted on **every `CLOSE`** (realized-pnl step), every **`EQUITY_FLATTEN`** (portfolio equity-rule firing), and the **terminal force-close** at `backtest_end` — matching the legacy points the oracle froze. `FUNDING`/`OPEN`/`LIQUIDATION` events mutate wallet/book state but **do not themselves emit a standalone curve point** unless they coincide with one of the above (legacy parity: the curve samples at realized-equity transitions, not every bar). The kernel tags each curve-emitting event so the service never has to re-derive "is this a curve point".
- **Per-point formula + running-peak source.** Each point's `equity = wallet + Σ open-uPnL` is taken from the kernel's deterministic left-to-right book reduction (the SAME stable-insertion-order scalar loop as §3.4 above — never `np.sum`), evaluated at the event's `bar_index`. `drawdown_pct = (equity − running_peak) / running_peak` where `running_peak = max(running_peak, equity)` is a **monotonic running-peak carried in the kernel state-scalars array** (`IDX_EQUITY_PEAK`), advanced in the same event order — NOT recomputed Python-side (a Python-side re-max over an out-of-order point list would diverge on ties). The point `ts` is the event's bar `open_time` (int64-ms), reconstructed via the timeline, identical unit to every other epoch (§4.1).
- **The seed-anchor timestamp comes OUT-OF-BAND from the scan schedule, NOT from trade events (the empty/all-filtered first-scan trap).** When the first scan is empty or every signal is filtered, **no events fire**, so the curve's seed point `(ts0, starting_capital, 0.0)` has **no trade-event timestamp to anchor to** — yet the golden master froze a seed point at the first scan's time. The reconstructor is therefore passed, **out-of-band from the event stream**, the **scan-schedule first `signal_time`** (and an **empty-scan fallback ts** = the run's `date_range_start`-normalized first scheduled scan time) as the seed anchor. The stable **None-first ordering** (seed point precedes all event points) is pinned: the seed is prepended with the out-of-band ts before any event point is applied, so an all-filtered first scan still produces the byte-identical seed the oracle holds.
- **Test:** an **event-to-curve fixture** asserts the reconstructed curve is byte-identical to the oracle including (a) the **empty-first-scan seed** (seed ts from the scan schedule, not from any trade), (b) the full `drawdown_pct` sequence against the kernel running-peak, and (c) None-first ordering. Added to §12.3 alongside the event-schema test.

 The SoA **kline arrays are `writeable=False`** (immutable, shareable across workers/combos zero-copy). Every run/combo holds its **own private** mutable pointer/cursor + latch/state-scalar arrays — **never a globally-shared mutable pointer array** (a worker mutating a shared pointer would corrupt siblings). Concurrent-run isolation of mutable latches is a hard invariant. A corruption-isolation test runs two combos concurrently over the same shared read-only SoA and asserts neither's pointers/latches perturb the other.

**Pure-Python hot-loop substrate (R1-F2, REQ-PERF-011 — ≥150k evals/s, supersedes REQ-PERF-005's ≥100k — R2-F19-batch4).** numpy arrays are optimal for numba but **pessimal for a Python-level scalar loop** (`arr[i]` boxes a scalar per access, ~5–10× slower). The pure-Python kernel therefore **materializes the per-chunk SoA window to native Python `list`/`memoryview` ONCE at chunk entry** (via `tolist()`/`memoryview`) and does **zero element-wise numpy `__getitem__`** in the bar loop. A **microbench gate** asserts (a) no numpy `__getitem__` in the hot loop AND (b) **≥150k evals/s** on the pure-Python lane — without this the pure-Python floor misses and numba would become mandatory (collapsing the D5/ADR-001 "numba is an earned bonus" decision). **One number across the doc:** the pure-Python floor is **≥150k evals/s** everywhere (§3.4 here, §11.1, §11.2); the earlier ≥100k in REQ-PERF-005 / earlier §3.4 drafts is **explicitly superseded** (R1-F1/R2-F19-batch4) so test authors enforce a single gate — 150k, not 100k.

**SSOT drift guard — constants AND formulas (R1-F8 + R2-F2-batch5, REQ-PAR-016).** Because `@njit` nopython cannot call the `trading_rules.py` Python helpers, sizing/TP/SL/slippage/liq/fee/funding **constants are mirrored** into the kernel — a silent-divergence risk the SSOT exists to prevent. Two distinct, unconditional guards:
- **Constant-equality guard:** a CI guard imports `trading_rules.py` and asserts each mirrored kernel constant equals its SSOT source by name, element-by-element, failing the build on drift.
- **Formula-level differential guard (R2-F2-batch5 — the constant guard is NOT sufficient):** a constant-equality check cannot detect a divergent *formula* (reordered rounding, off-by-one `qty_step` floor). An **unconditional formula-level differential/property test** drives each re-implemented kernel formula (sizing, TP/SL, liq, fee, funding) vs the `trading_rules.py` helper over a **randomized input grid** (price, qty_step, leverage, capital_pct, funding sign) and asserts bit-identity — or, stronger, the kernel formula bodies are **generated from `trading_rules.py` at build time** so a formula cannot drift at all. This is named as a **distinct gate** in §12.3 (the differential REQ-PAR-016 harness only catches values it happens to exercise; this grid + the generator close the formula gap). Referenced in the PAR/CFG coverage rows.

**Two-lane lockstep is a standing gate, not a one-time P4 check (R2-F12-batch5).** There are **two hot-loop implementations** to keep bit-identical, not one: the pure-Python lane materializes the SoA to native `list`/`memoryview` and does zero element-wise numpy `__getitem__` (§11.2), while the numba lane operates directly on numpy arrays — these data-access patterns **cannot share one function body** without defeating `@njit`. The design therefore explicitly separates **shared decision logic** (the cascade/eligibility/sizing rules — authored once, the parity oracle) from **lane-specific data access** (list/memoryview vs numpy indexing). A **pure-Python-vs-numba bit-identical CI job runs as a STANDING gate on every change** to either lane (not just at P4 introduction), so a later edit to one lane that silently diverges the other is caught.

**Cross-lane ULP risk is acknowledged — the two-lane gate is discrete-identical WITHIN a near-threshold money-epsilon guard band, NOT unconditionally bit-identical money (R5-F14-batch2, Medium — parity-vs-perf tension resolved, not asserted away).** P3 pure-Python float64 is the oracle of record and P4 numba float64 must be "bit-identical discrete fields" — but **CPython float ops and LLVM-lowered float ops can differ by 1 ULP** on division/sqrt/transcendentals **even with `fastmath=False`** (different libm, different instruction selection/FMA-vs-separate-mul-add). A sub-ULP money delta landing exactly at an equity threshold (an EQUITY_DROP/RISE fire point, a TP/SL/liq band edge) can flip a DISCRETE decision between lanes, so a naive "two-lane discrete fields bit-identical for ALL configs" gate can **legitimately fail** for some near-threshold configs — a real parity-vs-perf tension, not a non-issue. Pinned resolution (committed): the standing two-lane gate is **discrete-identical EXCEPT within a pinned `money-epsilon` guard band around every firing threshold** — when a per-position/equity value sits within ε of a threshold the two lanes MAY differ on the discrete decision, and that config is **flagged and ROUTED TO the pure-Python lane** (the oracle of record) rather than failing the build; outside the guard band discrete fields MUST be bit-identical. The implementer MAY instead require the numba lane to reproduce the pure-Python float op ORDER exactly (no libm divergence — same division/sqrt sequence, no FMA contraction), in which case the gate is unconditional bit-identity; but the committed default is the **money-epsilon guard band + route-near-threshold-configs-to-pure-Python fallback**, so P4's value is **config-scoped (the speedup applies to the non-near-threshold majority), NOT assumed-universal**. A **near-threshold fixture** (positions/equity engineered to sit within ε of a fire point) asserts EITHER the two lanes agree on the discrete decision OR the config is detected-near-threshold and routed to pure-Python — never a silent cross-lane discrete divergence shipped as "bit-identical". Added to §12.3.

**Live-path numba isolation (R1-F12 mig, REQ-DEP-025 — invariant + test).** The live scanner / auto-trade order-execution path keeps calling pure-Python `trading_rules.py` with **NO numba import, NO JIT warm, NO SoA dependency**, so live sizing never pays compile latency and is unaffected if accel is broken. `engine_kernel` reads `trading_rules` constants **without forcing numba into the live import graph** (the import edge is one-directional: kernel→rules, never rules→kernel/numba). A test asserts the live order path imports neither `numba` nor `engine_kernel`/SoA and yields unchanged sizing/TP-SL values.

**Errors / degradation.** numba unavailable or first-call JIT failure → transparent fallback to the pure-Python kernel (identical output, slower). First-call JIT cost (1–10s) is amortized across the run/sweep and measured (§9, REQ-PERF-040).

**JIT warm-compile runs OFF the event loop and off the live-path critical window (R3-F7-batch2, REQ-PERF-029, §9.5).** numba's first-call nopython COMPILE (cache cold after a fresh deploy or a new eager signature) **holds the GIL/CPU for 1–10s and is NOT chunked or cooperative** — it runs *before* the kernel exists to yield, so it cannot be interrupted by the §3.4 chunked cancel/heartbeat contract. On the first real run post-deploy this is a multi-second **event-loop-lag breach** that starves the live auto-trade coroutines, contradicting the always-on §9.5 SLI and REQ-PERF-029's "≤ documented factor" bound. Pinned: the warm-compile runs **either (a) at boot/post-deploy in the `ThreadPoolExecutor` (with `cache=True` priming) before the first user run, OR (b) inside the ProcessPool worker** (§3.6) so the parent loop never blocks. The §9.5 loop-lag SLI is **evaluated excluding (or bounded across) the one-time warm-compile window**, which is owned by the Boot/Readiness warm-up orchestration (§7.5) and surfaced as `jit_warm_ms`. A test asserts the **first post-deploy run does not breach the §9.5 lag bound on the loop thread** (the compile happened off-loop).

**Dependencies.** numba/llvmlite (guarded), `SoADatasetBuilder` output, `trading_rules.py` constants (sizing/TP/SL/slippage/liq/fee math — the SSOT shared live+backtest, discovery §2; **values mirrored, not re-derived**).

**Parity contract.** Develop pure-Python-first, assert oracle-identical on the Phase-0 golden suite, **then** JIT (findings §8). The drilldown `fine_klines` path stays on a **separate non-JIT path** (§3.5).

**Phase A (kernel) → orchestrator → Phase B (drill-refine) handshake — pinned (R4-F2-batch6-c2, REQ-DRILL-011/012).** The `@njit` kernel runs **Phase A** in nopython and **cannot call the async `DrilldownLoader.fine_window`** from inside the kernel, yet Phase B must refine ONLY exit-fill PRICE on the exact bars Phase A flagged, leaving selection / equity-firing / MFE-MAE / trailing untouched. Legacy did this in pure Python; the SoA/event-protocol version defines the equivalent seam as a three-stage contract:
- **Phase A emits a drilled-bar request set, it does NOT drill.** When a position closes on a bar eligible for intrabar refinement, the kernel emits the CLOSE event AND appends a record to a **`drill_requests[]` array** `(symbol_code, bar_open_epoch, position_id, exit_reason_code)` — the exact bars to refine, keyed to the CLOSE that will be corrected. No 1m data is touched in-kernel; Phase A completes entirely in nopython over 5m bars and returns `events[] + drill_requests[]`.
- **The async orchestrator (between chunks/after Phase A) resolves 1m windows.** Back in Python, the orchestrator hands `drill_requests[]` to `DrilldownLoader.fine_window` (§3.5), pre-fetching the 1m windows for exactly those `(symbol, bar_open_epoch)` pairs (entry bar + forward neighbour + exit ±1, the §3.5 window set). This is the only async/IO stage; it runs off the kernel.
- **Phase B re-resolves ONLY the flagged exit PRICES and emits a price-correction event.** A second, non-JIT pass walks `drill_requests[]`, computes the refined (non-optimistic) exit fill price from the resolved 1m window, and emits a **`PRICE_CORRECTION` event keyed to the original CLOSE's `position_id`** that overwrites ONLY the exit price (and the pnl/fees recomputed from it) in the reconstructed trade — it does **NOT** re-run latches, re-select trades, re-fire equity thresholds, or recompute MFE/MAE (those stay the coarse-5m values, REQ-DRILL-011/012/016/019). If a 1m window is unavailable for a request, that bar falls back to its 5m fill (the original CLOSE price stands), per §3.5 error handling.
- **Phase B ALSO reconciles the realized-wallet trajectory + curve endpoint to the drilled pnl — the three-way Σ invariant MUST hold on the drill lane (R5-F2-batch3, High — reconciliation-break fix).** A `PRICE_CORRECTION` that rewrites ONLY the trade record's exit price/pnl/fees but leaves the wallet + `equity_curve` (built by Phase A on 5m) untouched would make **`Σ(trade.pnl)` reflect drilled fills while `final_equity`/curve reflect 5m fills** — so the Prime-Directive `Σ trade.pnl == final_equity − starting_capital == net_profit` invariant breaks by the **cumulative drill delta**, which is NOT ULP-scale (it is a real price difference) and therefore the pinned float reconciliation epsilon CANNOT absorb it. Legacy drilled INLINE, so wallet + trades stayed consistent. Pinned reconciliation (the firing/selection vs pnl split is explicit):
  - **Equity-threshold FIRING stays on the 5m `equity_ref`** — Phase A's coarse-5m equity trajectory is what fires EQUITY_DROP/RISE/trailing/breakeven (REQ-DRILL-011/012: selection + firing are coarse-5m, byte-identical drill-on-vs-off). The drill NEVER moves a firing point. To keep firing on 5m while pnl is drilled, the event stream **carries BOTH `equity_ref_entry` (the 5m mark used for threshold firing) AND the drilled exit fill (used for realized pnl)** per corrected position.
  - **REALIZED wallet is corrected at each drilled close.** When `PRICE_CORRECTION` rewrites a close's exit price, it ALSO emits the **`wallet_delta` correction** (`drilled_pnl − coarse_pnl`, net of the recomputed fees/funding) applied to the realized-wallet trajectory at that close's bar, so the running realized wallet — and therefore the **final_equity and the curve's realized-equity points** — reflect the drilled realized pnl. The curve's *unrealized* segments and the *firing* decisions stay on 5m; only the *realized* steps move to drilled values.
  - **final_equity reconciles to Σ drilled realized pnl.** After all `PRICE_CORRECTION`s apply, `final_equity − starting_capital == Σ(corrected trade.pnl) == net_profit` holds within the pinned float epsilon (ULP only — the drill delta is now ON BOTH sides). A **drill-on three-way reconciliation fixture** asserts the invariant holds with drill ON (not just OFF), and that a config which fires an equity threshold still fires it at the SAME 5m bar drill-on vs drill-off (firing on 5m) while `Σ trade.pnl`, `final_equity−start`, and `net_profit` all agree post-correction.
- **Test:** a **drill-on-vs-drill-off byte-identity-of-non-price-fields** test asserts trade SELECTION, equity-rule firing, MFE/MAE, and trailing/breakeven timing are **byte-identical** with drill on vs off — only exit `price`/`pnl`/`fees` differ — proving Phase B surgically rewrites price without re-running any latch.

## 3.5 [NEW] `DrilldownLoader` — lazy per-symbol LTF (1m) loader (Phase 2 fix, Phase 5 cache)

**Module:** folds into `KlineStore` + a thin `backend/services/drilldown_loader.py`; replaces the un-persisted re-fetch in `BacktestService._build_fine_klines` (`backtest_service.py:983`).

**Responsibility.** Today `_build_fine_klines` calls `_fetch_klines_from_bybit` **directly and deliberately does NOT persist** (comment `:991–994`), so every rerun (and Phase B of every run) re-pulls all 1m drill candles over a contiguous `min→max` span discarding ~98% (findings RC-3, VERIFIED). The new loader: lazy per-symbol LTF load fetching only the bars actually drilled (entry bar + forward neighbour + exit ±1, preserving the exact window set at `:1022–1026`), with an in-process cache so reruns slice from RAM (REQ-DRILL-020).

**Seal model — DECIDED: non-sealed memo, NEVER the day-grain seal manifest (R1-F5).** The 1m drill path is **incoherent with day-grain sealing**: `SealedManifest` seals WHOLE days (PK `(symbol,interval,date)`, completion-frontier over a day), but a drill touches sparse intra-day sub-windows. Sealing a 1m day from sub-windows would either (a) re-introduce the partial-day false-coverage bug ADR-003 exists to kill, or (b) force a full-day ≈1440-bar fetch that defeats "fetch only drilled bars". Today's code keeps 1m **in-memory-only on purpose** to avoid poisoning coverage. **Resolution (model 1):** drilled 1m bars live in a **non-sealed in-process / mmap'd-Feather memo keyed by `(symbol, sub_interval, bar_open_epoch)`** that gets cross-run caching but **NEVER writes a row to the day-grain `kline_cache_coverage` seal manifest** and never sets `sealed`/`day_class`. The 5m sealed manifest is therefore provably unperturbed by any drill. (Model 2 — trigger a full-day 1m seal — is explicitly rejected: it pays the ~1440-bar cost ADR-003 avoids.) A drilled run consults `symbol_lifecycle` only as a fetch bound, never to seal.

**Interface.** `async fine_window(symbol, bar_open_epoch, sub_interval) -> KlineColumns | None`. The memo is the only cache tier consulted for 1m; the Postgres `kline_cache` SOR is still the durable store for any 1m rows actually written (idempotent `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`), but coverage/seal rows for `interval='1m'` are NOT created by this path. **Errors:** a 1m fetch failure on an individual coarse bar mid-run → fall back to 5m resolution for **that bar only**, never abort, never poison other bars, never persist partial 1m data; fallback fill stays non-optimistic (REQ-DRILL-023).

**1m SOR-growth is BOUNDED — the lifecycle gap is closed (R5-F10-batch3, Medium — unbounded-growth fix).** 1m drill rows are written idempotently to `kline_cache(interval='1m')` but get **NO coverage/seal row, NO `day_class`, NO materialization, NO TTL by design** (non-sealed memo, §3.5 above). Nothing in the seal/manifest machinery manages their lifecycle, so **sparse 1m rows would accumulate unbounded across every drilled run/rerun** — partition auto-create (§4.4) places them but nothing prunes them — an operational growth hazard on the shared SOR. Committed resolution (choose ONE, pinned): **(a) PREFERRED — keep 1m STRICTLY in the in-process / mmap'd-Feather memo and do NOT durably write 1m to `kline_cache` at all** (the memo already gives cross-run caching per §3.5; the durable 1m write is dropped, so there is no SOR growth to bound — the 1m path is purely an ephemeral/Feather memo). **OR (b)** if durable 1m rows are retained for cross-process reuse, add a **bounded retention/pruning policy** owned by `MaintenanceAdmin` (§3.12): an age-based prune of `interval='1m'` rows (they are disposable — re-fetchable from Bybit on the next drill, like the columnar tier ADR-002), bounded by a configured max 1m-row budget with high/low-water reclaim, PLUS a **`kline_cache` 1m-row-count gauge** (§9.7 storage-health) that alerts on sustained growth. The architecture commits to **(a)** for the PRIMARY target (no durable 1m write → no SOR-growth bound needed; the Feather memo is disposable and lives under `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR`'s own disk policy §11.4), documenting (b) as the alternative if a deployment needs durable cross-process 1m sharing. A test asserts that after N drilled reruns the `kline_cache` `interval='1m'` row count stays bounded (zero under (a); ≤ the configured budget under (b)).

**Parity contract.** The drill path may change intrabar fill **PRICE** only — never trade SELECTION, equity-threshold firing, MFE/MAE (coarse 5m extremes), or trailing/breakeven timing (coarse 5m — REQ-DRILL-011/012/016/019). Full-book coverage required for the 1m equity fine-walk or fall back to 5m (REQ-DRILL-013). **Seal-isolation test (R1-F5):** a fixture runs a drill-ON backtest and asserts the 5m `kline_cache_coverage` sealed-manifest rows (`sealed`, `day_class`, `content_sha256`) are **byte-for-byte unchanged** before vs after, and that no `interval='1m'` coverage/seal row was created — proving the drill memo never poisons day-grain coverage.

**DRILL-004 memo scope reconciled with the pure-sweep decision — sweeps are drill-OFF (R4-F3-batch6-c2, REQ-DRILL-004, REQ-SWEEP).** There is a real contradiction at the sweep/drill seam: discovery §2 and §3.6 pin that **per-combo sweep runs are PURE (no drilldown)** and ship ProcessPool **spawn** workers in **isolated address spaces** (§3.6) — so an in-process 1m memo cannot be shared across combos in different processes, and REQ-DRILL-004's `call_count == 1`-across-K-combos assertion would be unsatisfiable on the ProcessPool path. **Decision (committed): sweeps run drill-OFF; REQ-DRILL-004's shared-memo guarantee is scoped to the SINGLE-backtest path and reruns-within-a-session in the SAME process** — which is exactly where drilling happens (`optimize_config`'s baseline backtest is a single drilled run; the N-combo sweep that follows is pure). The memo (`(symbol, sub_interval, bar_open_epoch)` keyed) lives in the parent/single-run process; a drilled 5m bar fetches its 1m sub-bars **exactly once** across **reruns and the baseline within a session**, and the `call_count == 1` test is asserted on the **single-backtest rerun path** (run the same drilled config twice in one process, assert 1 fetch), NOT across spawn-isolated sweep combos. REQ-DRILL-004 is amended to this scope (the cross-combo clause is moot because combos never drill). **If a future requirement genuinely needs drilled sweeps,** the documented upgrade is a **parent-side 1m resolver** (workers send `drill_requests[]` back to the parent via the existing IPC result queue, the parent owns the single shared memo and resolves once) — recorded here as the alternative, not the default. The SWEEP/DRILL coverage-map rows reflect this scope.

## 3.6 [NEW] `SweepRunner` — parallel combo execution with shipped-once shared inputs (Phase 2 + Phase 6)

**Module:** `backend/mcp/tools/optimizer/sweep_runner.py` (new) behind the existing `sweep_tools.py:_execute_sweep` (`:54`); `sweep_run` (`:129`) signature unchanged.

**Responsibility.** Replace the **current serial async loop over combos** (R1-F9 — the sweep is NOT routed through the `BacktestService` `ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=3)`; `_execute_sweep` `sweep_tools.py:69–79` runs combos serially in a single async loop via `runner.run_one(...)`, gated before each combo by the live-trading breaker `_await_breaker_clear(manager)` / `manager.mcp_permitted()` `:76,108–118`) with concurrency-bounded fan-out (REQ-SWEEP-001). **Parallelism source is a real CPU-parallel mechanism, NOT `asyncio.gather` (R2-F9-batch5):** the engine is **synchronous and CPU/GIL-bound** (§7.4), so `asyncio.gather` over coroutines that call sync CPU work yields **zero parallelism** — it serializes on the loop/GIL. The actual fan-out is a **`ProcessPool`** for CPU-bound combos (GIL released per worker) or, as a portable fallback, a **bounded `ThreadPoolExecutor`** whose threads run the **GIL-releasing `nogil=True` kernel** (§3.4) — a thread pool only parallelizes when the kernel actually drops the GIL. If `asyncio.gather` appears at all it is **only the async shell around executor submits**, and the executor (Process/Thread pool) — never `gather` itself — is the parallelism source. Pure sequential execution is the final fallback. Shared read-only inputs (snapshot/signals/instrument_info **+ the SoA kline arrays + global timeline**) shipped to workers **exactly once** via `multiprocessing.shared_memory`/mmap'd Feather — never re-pickled per combo (REQ-SWEEP-002, P3 substrate per the two-step transport above). Pre-load + SoA-build + timeline-build happen **once** before fan-out, spanning `optimize_config`'s baseline backtest + its N-combo sweep (REQ-SWEEP-003). Dynamic/work-stealing dispatch so a few drill-heavy combos can't serialize the tail (REQ-SWEEP-008).

**Live-breaker gate preserved under fan-out (R1-F6 + R1-F5 mig, FR-037/NFR-002 — must not regress).** The serial sweep yields to live order placement via the breaker before every combo; ProcessPool workers cannot reach the parent's in-memory `manager`/breaker, so a naive fan-out silently drops that safety exactly when parallelism makes contention worst. **Resolution:** dispatch stays in the parent loop regardless of worker model, so the breaker is kept as a **parent-side admission gate** — when `mcp_permitted()` goes False the runner **stops dispatching new combos and optionally drains in-flight ones**, resuming when it clears (mirrors `_await_breaker_clear`). Workers also poll a **shared-memory breaker flag / periodic IPC heartbeat** before each combo so a long combo can yield mid-flight. A test asserts a sweep **pauses/sheds under a simulated OPEN breaker and resumes when it clears**.

**Concurrency-domain contract (R1-F9).** The sweep fan-out and the `BacktestService` `_MAX_CONCURRENT=3` `create_backtest` slot pool are explicitly reconciled: **sweep workers run in their OWN bounded pool and do NOT consume the 3 live UI-backtest slots** (so a large sweep can't starve interactive backtests), and sweep concurrency (toward `cpu_count`, capped by the CPU/thread budget §7.4 and the 1GB RSS ceiling) is admission-checked by `PreflightEstimator` before fan-out. The shared inputs are built once; per-combo engine runs are pure (no drilldown, discovery §2).

**Worker DB-persistence model (R1-F5 mig, REQ-PERF-021).** Per-combo results are persisted **parent-side via an IPC result queue** (workers compute, the parent writes) — workers do NOT each open an asyncpg pool, avoiding connection exhaustion/deadlock against the live scanner. The asyncpg pool is pre-warmed and `max_size`-provisioned for: live-baseline + `_MAX_CONCURRENT`×per-run + a bounded sweep-read cap (REQ-PERF-021). Final ranking: a single **fixed-text array-bound** set-based `UPDATE` so total writes == `K + O(1)`, not `4K` (REQ-SWEEP-009) — see the PERF-020 array-binding note below.

**Ranking persist uses FIXED parameterized text (array binding), NOT an inline `VALUES` list — REQ-PERF-020 prepared-statement-cache safety (R4-F2-batch6-c5).** The earlier "single set-based `UPDATE … FROM (VALUES …)`" framing has an **inline `VALUES (…),(…)` list whose length scales with K combos**, so the statement TEXT changes per distinct K across a sweep / `optimize_config` session — forking asyncpg's prepared-statement cache per K (the exact thrash REQ-PERF-020 forbids). Pinned: the ranking `UPDATE` is **fixed-text array binding** so the statement text is invariant to K:
```sql
UPDATE mcp_sweep_results AS t SET rank = v.rank
FROM (SELECT * FROM UNNEST($1::bigint[], $2::int[])) AS v(id, rank)
WHERE t.id = v.id
```
The two arrays are bound as single parameters, so the statement text is byte-identical for K=2 or K=500 and the prepared-statement cache holds **one** entry. `executemany` (one prepared statement reused) and `copy_records_to_table` (COPY protocol, no per-row statement) are likewise cache-safe and used for the trade/result bulk writes; string-interpolated `IN`-lists are prohibited everywhere on the persist path. A test asserts the **prepared-statement cache size stays bounded across a multi-K sweep** (it does not grow with the number of distinct K values).

**RSS-flat transport on the Windows host (R1-F7, REQ-SWEEP-002).** On the documented Windows 11 host, multiprocessing uses **spawn**, so ProcessPool initializer-globals are **pickled and copied** into each worker — one full SoA copy per worker = exactly `C×full-kline-bytes`, blowing the budget. Therefore **`multiprocessing.shared_memory`/mmap'd-Feather is the REQUIRED transport** for the SoA arrays on the ProcessPool path (initializer-globals only for tiny scalars); spawn-pickled globals do NOT satisfy REQ-SWEEP-002. A **win32 RSS-flat-as-workers-rise test** asserts process-tree RSS ≈ `base_snapshot + C×small-per-combo-working-set`. When shared memory is unavailable, concurrency is capped to a value derived from the 1GB ceiling rather than copying full klines per worker.

**Per-combo result memory + GC (R1-F12, REQ-PERF-026/027).** Each combo's RESULT (trade list + full `equity_curve`) is **persisted then RELEASED before the next accumulates**, so retained ≈ `concurrency × per-combo`, NOT `K × per-combo` — a ≥50-combo sweep can't grow RSS ∝ K despite shipped-once flat inputs. The orchestrator estimates `shared_klines + concurrency×per-combo` pre-fan-out and **auto-throttles/rejects under the RSS ceiling**, and on an in-flight `MemoryError` **reactively lowers concurrency** for the remaining combos (none dropped) rather than repeat-OOMing. GC is frozen/tuned around each combo kernel with a documented cumulative-pause bound.

**Bounded pending-persist queue — the BACKPRESSURE half of SWEEP-016 is pinned (R5-F14-batch3, Medium — unbounded-queue-OOM fix).** Per-combo results are persisted parent-side via ONE IPC writer and released before the next accumulates — but when **C workers finish faster than the single parent DB writer drains** (slow/contended Postgres), the **pending-persist queue grows unboundedly** and can breach the RSS ceiling (each pending entry holds a full trade list + `equity_curve`). The retained ≈ `concurrency × per-combo` bound covers the COMPUTE side but NOT this persist backlog. Pinned: the parent maintains a **bounded pending-persist queue with a configured BYTE budget** (not just an entry count, since `equity_curve` size varies); when the queue's retained bytes reach the cap, **worker dispatch BLOCKS (backpressure) — finished workers wait to hand off their result until the writer drains** — rather than letting finished-but-unpersisted results accumulate. No combo is ever dropped; the slowest stage (the DB writer) sets the pace. A **deliberately-slow-persist test** (artificially throttled parent writer + fast workers) asserts (a) retained pending-persist bytes stay **≤ the configured cap** throughout, (b) **no combo result is dropped** (all K eventually persist), and (c) total RSS stays under the ceiling. This is the backpressure complement to the compute-side `concurrency × per-combo` bound.

**Per-run allocation release on EVERY terminal path + no-leak soak (R4-F3-batch6-c5, REQ-PERF-041).** Distinct from the per-combo result release above and the boot reaper for PRIOR-crash orphans (R18) and SIGTERM teardown (below): the **steady-state per-run release** is owned by a **`BacktestService` run-finalizer + the `SweepRunner`** with an explicit **`finally`-scoped release contract** covering **completion / 120s timeout-kill / cooperative-cancel** for every run-scoped allocation — SoA arrays, position book, the 1m drill memo, ProcessPool `shared_memory`/Feather-mmap segments, and per-tier reader connections (DuckDB/Polars/asyncpg). A run that dies without releasing would leak FDs/mmap handles/segments/connections and monotonically shrink the runnable surface, so release is tied to run finalization (the same `finally` that releases the `AdmissionAccountant` reservation, §3.9), not the happy path. A **soak test of N heterogeneous runs (including killed + cancelled)** asserts (a) **no monotonic RSS growth**, (b) **stable warm-run latency** over process lifetime, (c) the **next-run-after-kill meets nominal budget**, and (d) **FD / mmap-handle / DuckDB-Polars-conn / pool-conn / shared_memory-segment counts return to baseline** when idle. Added to §12.3 and the REQ-ID→test traceability matrix.

**Spawn + secret hygiene — ALLOWLIST, not denylist (R1-F10 mig + R5-F4-batch3, §8).** The pool **forces `multiprocessing.set_start_method('spawn')`** (win32-portable and avoids Linux `fork` inheriting the parent's address space — `ACCOUNTS_ENCRYPTION_KEY`, decrypted credentials, live asyncpg sockets). **Worker env is constructed by an ALLOWLIST, deny-by-default (R5-F4-batch3, Medium — un-enumerated-secret-leak fix).** The earlier "scrub/sentinel sensitive env (`ACCOUNTS_ENCRYPTION_KEY`, API keys)" was an **enumerated DENYLIST**, which silently leaks any un-enumerated secret into the spawn-worker env — notably **`DATABASE_URL` (contains the Postgres password)**, **`COINGECKO_API_KEY`**, and the **`TRADINGAGENTS_LLM_PROVIDER` API keys** (all named secrets in CLAUDE.md). Under `spawn` the child inherits the parent environment by default and the scrub runs **post-inherit**, so anything the denylist missed is exposed in the worker process (and any core dump/crash log). Sweep workers run pure engine kernels over shared-memory SoA and need **NO secrets at all**. Pinned: workers are launched with a **minimal, explicitly-constructed environment** containing ONLY the non-secret vars the kernel needs (thread caps `NUMBA_NUM_THREADS`/`OMP_NUM_THREADS`/`OPENBLAS_NUM_THREADS`, `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR`, the numba cache dir, `NUMBA_THREADING_LAYER`), passed via the pool initializer rather than inherited — env-passing is **deny-by-default**. Core dumps are disabled for workers and no forked asyncpg pool is handed to a child. A test asserts a worker's `os.environ` contains **none of** `{ACCOUNTS_ENCRYPTION_KEY, DATABASE_URL, COINGECKO_API_KEY, TRADINGAGENTS_LLM_PROVIDER-keys}` (and only the allowlisted kernel vars). Given a REQ-SEC id (see §8.7).

**Sweep cold-start budget — C-worker spawn + numba import + JIT warm folded into the latency gate (R3-F7-batch3/sweep, REQ-PERF-040, REQ-SWEEP-005).** Because the host uses `spawn` (§3.6), **every ProcessPool worker is a fresh interpreter** that must re-import numba and pay first-call JIT compile (1–10s, §9.3) **independently** — so a naive `C workers × (spawn + numba import + JIT warm)` can burn tens of seconds before any combo runs, which the §11.3 budgets (100-combo <60s / 500-combo <5min, REQ-SWEEP-005) and REQ-PERF-040's single-run cold-start framing do NOT account for. Pinned:
- The ProcessPool **initializer pre-warms the kernel once per worker** (eager `cache=True` compile in the initializer, not on the first combo), so warm cost is paid concurrently across workers at pool spin-up, not serially per combo.
- The **on-disk numba cache dir is shared/validated across workers** (so the second+ worker loads the cached object rather than recompiling), with first-build cache-contention across workers handled (a single worker builds, the rest load).
- The existing `jit_warm_ms` telemetry **gates** this; the §11.3 sweep budgets are explicitly stated as a **warm-pool figure (excluding the one-time first-deploy compile)** — the first cold sweep after a deploy carries a documented one-time `pool_warm_ms` surcharge attributed to a distinct stage, not hidden in combo time. A test asserts aggregate worker warm cost is paid once at spin-up and the steady-state 100-combo run meets <60s warm.

**Two-step transport across P2→P3 — the "ship SoA once" guarantee belongs to P3 (R2-F11-batch2, REQ-SWEEP-002/003).** SweepRunner ships in **P2** but `SoADatasetBuilder` + the global timeline are a **P3** deliverable (§3.3) — so in P2 there is no SoA to ship-once. The transport is therefore **explicitly two-step:** **(P2)** the runner ships **batched raw klines** (shared-memory/mmap'd, built once before fan-out) — a different transport with its own RSS profile and parity surface; **(P3)** it upgrades to the **shared SoA + global timeline** transport, at which point REQ-SWEEP-002/003's "SoA arrays + timeline built once, shipped exactly once" guarantee fully holds. Appendix A maps the **shipped-once-flat-SoA-RSS** win and its win32 RSS-flat test to **P3**; P2's gate is the raw-kline shared-transport RSS test. This avoids claiming the SoA-shipped-once-RSS-flat win before its substrate exists.

**Shared-memory lifecycle is OS-specific — Windows ≠ POSIX (R2-F12-batch1, REQ-STORE-044, R18).** The orphaned-resource model is documented per-OS because the stated deployment target is **Windows 11 + `spawn`**:
- **Windows (deployment target):** `multiprocessing.shared_memory` segments are backed by the **paging file** and **auto-released by the OS when the last handle closes** — there is **no persistent named inode to `unlink`**, so a boot reaper that `unlink`s stale named segments is a **no-op on Windows**, and the EEXIST-on-recreate / leftover-temp-read failure mode it guards against largely does not arise. The **real Windows hazard is the opposite**: a known CPython issue where a Windows `SharedMemory` can be **freed while children still map it** (premature free of a live segment). Mitigation: the **parent keeps a handle alive for the segment's lifetime** (and/or a `resource_tracker` policy is set so the tracker does not free a still-mapped segment); a **win32 process-tree kill-then-recreate test** asserts no premature free and no corruption.
- **POSIX (CI/Linux lanes):** named segments persist as `/dev/shm` inodes that survive a crashed process, so the **named-segment `unlink` reaper applies there** — the boot reaper unlinks stale segments and the same-named segment never `EEXIST`s on recreate.
R18/REQ-STORE-044 is stated against the **Windows** model as primary, with the POSIX reaper as the Linux-lane variant.

**Lifecycle: reconcile / generation / teardown (R1-F6 mig, REQ-ROLL-017/018/019, REQ-API-016).** (a) On boot, a **reconciliation** sweeps the exact in-flight set `status IN ('pending','queued','running')` (R2-F10) on the sweep+backtest rows to terminal-or-requeued and frees every `_MAX_CONCURRENT` slot, ProcessPool worker, and `shared_memory`/mmap segment (never a stuck `running`). **Per-table terminal vocabulary is pinned — the reconcile MUST NOT write a uniform new terminal value across tables (R3-F1-batch3, REQ-MIG-038):** the `backtest_runs.status` CHECK is relaxed by v58 to admit `interrupted_by_restart`/`failed_with_timeout` (§4.4), but the **live `mcp_sweep_jobs.status` CHECK is a DIFFERENT, un-relaxed enum** (`'queued','running','completed','cancelled','failed','interrupted'` — `async_persistence.py:865`; **no `'pending'`, uses `'interrupted'` NOT `'interrupted_by_restart'`**). Writing a uniform `'interrupted_by_restart'` to a sweep-job row would violate `mcp_sweep_jobs_status_check` and **abort the reconcile at boot** — the exact "new status before constraint relaxes → failed write in prod" hazard REQ-MIG-038 defends, but its defense is scoped to `backtest_runs`. Pinned: the reconcile maps to **each table's OWN terminal vocabulary** (sweep-job row → `'interrupted'`; backtest_runs row → `'interrupted_by_restart'`), the per-table mapping is documented, and an **"insert-each-reconcile-terminal-status-into-`mcp_sweep_jobs`" test** mirrors REQ-MIG-038. (Alternatively v58 also relaxes `mcp_sweep_jobs.status` to a superset admitting the reconcile value with a `NOT VALID` CHECK — see §4.4; the default is per-table vocabulary, the least-invasive option.) (b) `mcp_sweep_results` rows (the real sweep *results* table — NOT `sweep_results`, R2-F1) are stamped with the **engine git-SHA + flag fingerprint** in their `engine_fingerprint` column; on resume the runner refuses to merge combos from a different generation (re-run or refuse-merge) so a ranked set is never silently multi-generation. (c) On `SIGTERM`, the lifetime-singleton ProcessPool/ThreadPool + all `shared_memory`/mmap segments are torn down with **zero residual segments**.

**Boot reconcile needs an OWNER/LEASE guard before [FLEET] — N/A on the single host, REQUIRED before multi-pod (R5-F12-batch5, Medium — cross-pod live-run-termination fix).** The boot reconcile sweeps `status IN ('pending','queued','running')` rows to terminal/requeued and frees slots — but in-flight run rows carry **no owner/lease/instance-id column**. On the PRIMARY single-Windows-host target this is safe (stop-then-start §2.0: the only process that could own a `running` row is the one that just died, so every `running` row at boot IS orphaned). But the design explicitly supports the SECONDARY **[FLEET]** multi-pod variant, where a booting pod-B would reconcile rows owned by **pod-A's still-executing run**, marking a genuinely-running backtest `interrupted_by_restart` and freeing its accounting under it. Pinned: **before [FLEET] is enabled**, in-flight run rows gain an **owner/lease column** (instance id + heartbeat/lease-expiry timestamp, renewed by the owning run); the boot reconcile only terminates a row whose **lease is EXPIRED or whose owner is provably dead** (no recent heartbeat), NEVER a row with a live lease from another pod. On the single-host target the lease machinery is **inert** (one instance, every boot-time `running` row is leaseless-or-expired by construction) and a test asserts the degenerate case; on [FLEET] a **pod-B-boot-does-not-terminate-pod-A's-live-run test** is REQUIRED before enabling the variant. This is stated as **N/A-but-specified on PRIMARY, gating-requirement on [FLEET]**, consistent with §2.0's fleet-conditional scoping.

**Startup reaper for orphaned OS resources (R1-F9 mig, REQ-STORE-044).** A boot-time reaper **unlinks stale named `shared_memory` segments** (versioned/namespaced names + liveness check) and sweeps orphaned columnar temp files left by a prior `SIGKILL`/OOM, before first use — so a same-named segment never `EEXIST`s on recreate and a reader never partially reads a leftover temp/orphan. Partial/temp files are routed away from readers via write-to-temp + atomic rename (REQ-STORE-027).

**Interface.** `async run_sweep(base_config, space, concurrency, shared_soa) -> ranked_results`. Final ranking: single **fixed-text array-bound** set-based `UPDATE` (UNNEST of id+rank arrays — PERF-020 prepared-statement-cache safe, §3.6 above) so total writes == `K + O(1)`, not `4K` (REQ-SWEEP-009).

**`config_hash` — first-class artifact, pinned like `content_sha256` (R2-F10-batch4, REQ-SWEEP-010/011/013/019, REQ-CFG-013).** `config_hash` gates crash-resume (`ON CONFLICT(sweep_id, config_hash)` — REQ-SWEEP-013), combo dedup (REQ-SWEEP-019), tie-break ranking (REQ-SWEEP-010), and deploy-stability (REQ-SWEEP-011), so it is defined explicitly rather than left to `hash()`:
- **Canonical serialization:** the combo's **decision fields only** (the AutoTradeConfig knobs that change WHAT the engine decides) are serialized as **sorted-key canonical JSON** (`json.dumps(obj, sort_keys=True, separators=(',',':'))` with numbers normalized to a fixed repr), then **SHA-256**ed. Sorted keys ⇒ key order cannot change the hash.
- **Decision-field-only domain (REQ-CFG-013):** **infra/optimization flags** (`BT_USE_NUMBA`, `BT_USE_COLUMNAR`, `BT_USE_FASTPATH`, `BT_PARALLEL_SWEEP`, `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR`, worker counts) are **EXCLUDED** — they change HOW, not WHAT, so two infra-different deploys of the same decision combo hash **identically** (a flag flip never forks the resume/dedup key).
- **Restart/deploy-stable:** SHA-256 over canonical bytes is independent of `PYTHONHASHSEED` (never Python's salted `hash()`), so the hash is **stable across process restarts and deploys** (REQ-SWEEP-011) — a resumed sweep matches its pre-restart rows.
- **Injective over decision fields:** distinct decision combos produce distinct hashes (collision-resistant); a property test asserts (a) permuted-key configs hash equal, (b) infra-flag-only differences hash equal, (c) any decision-field change hashes different, (d) stability across a fresh interpreter with a different `PYTHONHASHSEED`.

**Errors.** A combo failure is isolated (per-combo result retained for crash-resume); cancel via `sweep_cancel` (`:282`) keeps partial results queryable.

**Dependencies.** `SoADatasetBuilder` (shared substrate), `BacktestEngine` (pure, no drilldown — discovery §2), `sweep_repo.py` (rank persistence), `PreflightEstimator` (pre-fan-out admission/RSS sizing), the live-trading `manager` breaker (parent-side gate).

## 3.7 [NEW] `GoldenMasterOracle` — stored-snapshot parity harness (Phase 0, gates ALL phases)

**Module:** `tests/backend/test_backtest_golden.py` (extended, not replaced — discovery §7) + `tests/backend/oracle/` fixtures.

**Responsibility.** Freeze the **current** engine output as the oracle BEFORE any optimization, so every phase is diffed against it. Replaces brittle inline magic numbers (`38.9725, -510.725, 959.0, -878.4, 77.941103`) with a **stored-snapshot** oracle (run current engine, freeze full output — discovery §7). Adds the explicit **three-way reconciliation** `Σ trade['pnl'] == final_equity − starting_capital == metrics['net_profit']` (the existing `_assert_reconciles` only ties net_profit↔final_equity — discovery §7).

**Interface.** `assert_oracle_identical(result, frozen_snapshot)` (byte-identical on 5m no-drill); `assert_within_tolerance_and_non_optimistic(result, oracle)` (drill/portfolio — two-sided sandwich REQ-DRILL-018). A **differential float64-vs-Decimal harness** confirms the SoA/numba float path stays within tolerance of the Decimal oracle (§12).

**Dependencies.** The **pure engine layer** as the cheap fast seam (sync, no DB — discovery §7); async mock_db reserved for service-layer parity. Branch builders (`_config`/`_signal`/`_klines`) extended **in place**, never naively consolidated (would shift frozen golden values — discovery §7).

## 3.8 [MODIFIED] components (semantic parity required)

| File | Change | Frozen behavior |
|------|--------|-----------------|
| `kline_cache_service.py` | `get_coverage_gaps` (`:116`) delegates to `SealedManifest.unsealed_days`; `_update_coverage` (`:286`) also seals; `_fetch_klines_from_bybit` page `_PAGE_SIZE 200→1000` + bulk-insert (`:100`); **`store_klines` (`:91-109`) gains the seal-guard write seam (R2-F4-batch2): a novel `open_time` into a sealed `(symbol,interval,date)` is reject+structured-logged, NOT silently absorbed by `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`; `_update_coverage` (`:314`) `candle_count` is OVERWRITTEN by set-based `COUNT(DISTINCT open_time)` at seal, not left at GREATEST (R2-F3-batch2).** | Idempotent `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` (for true duplicates); per-symbol failure isolation (`:261`). |
| `backtest_service.py` | `_load_klines` (`:964`) N+1 → one batched `symbol=ANY($1)` + `open_time BETWEEN` (REQ-STORE-013) **+ streaming/cursor seam for wide runs** (§3.1, REQ-PERF-015); `_build_fine_klines` (`:983`) → `DrilldownLoader`; `_execute_backtest` warm-up band collapses (REQ-PERF-035); `_persist_results` → `executemany`/`COPY` batched trade insert (O(1) round-trips, REQ-PERF-017). **ALL auxiliary kline paths route through `KlineStore` + sealed-manifest precedence (R2-F5-batch1, REQ-CACHE-022/025): Buy&Hold BTC (`_attach_buy_hold`, `:1352`), btc_vol BTC series (`:1138`, 1h/4h), per-symbol MR-mean series (`:1154`, 1h/4h) — today they call `self._kline_cache.get_klines(...)` directly and bypass the cache.** | Run lifecycle, `_persist_results` Decimal coercion + finite-guard (`_num:1449`); **`_downsample_equity` LTTB (`:491`) frozen EXCEPT the REQ-FE-004 trough-preservation modification (R4-F13-batch6-c2 — force-includes first/last/global-max-DD-trough, oracle re-frozen);** **B&H/btc_vol/MR-mean numeric outputs bit-identical pre/post-reroute, valued off the SAME forming-day snapshot (REQ-PAR-045).** |
| `backtest_engine.py` | `_evaluate_candles_until` (`:1165`) → SoA merge-walk; per-candle math → `engine_kernel`. | Every rule order, latch, cascade, filter-chain step — bit-identical (Prime Directive). |
| `sweep_tools.py` | `_execute_sweep` (`:54`) → `SweepRunner`. | `SweepRunIn/Out` schema, `sweep_status/results/cancel` contracts. |
| `async_persistence.py` | Append **v58** to `_MIGRATIONS` (`:992`) — **DDL ONLY** (manifest columns on `kline_cache_coverage`, `symbol_lifecycle` + `seal_backfill_marker` tables, OBS columns on `backtest_runs`/`_results`/**`mcp_sweep_results`** — the real sweep table, R2-F1; NOT `sweep_results`, which does not exist — status-CHECK relax shipped `NOT VALID` only). NO inline backfill, NO in-txn `VALIDATE`, NO in-txn index (§4.4, R1-F1/F2, R2-F4). | All prior migrations untouched; runner unchanged; entrypoint import-isolated from accel/engine modules (REQ-MIG-029). |
| `InstrumentInfoCache` (`:516`) | **Aux instrument-info path routes through `KlineStore`/sealed-manifest-aware caching (R2-F5-batch1, REQ-CACHE-022/025)** so a warm rerun issues 0 Bybit instrument-info calls, consistent with the kline-loader cache precedence. | Instrument-info field shapes unchanged; values bit-identical warm vs cold. |
| `trading_rules.py` | **No logic change.** Constants may be read by `engine_kernel`. | SSOT for sizing/TP/SL/slippage/liq/fees/trailing/breakeven (discovery §2). |

**Aux kline reads share the engine's forming-day snapshot — single-snapshot pin (R4-F8-batch6-c2, REQ-PAR-045, REQ-STORE-030).** REQ-PAR-045 requires Buy&Hold, btc_vol, and MR-mean to be valued off the **same forming-day snapshot the engine consumed**. Rerouting all three through `KlineStore` (above) does NOT by itself satisfy this: each is a **separate `get_klines_batch`** with its **own point-in-time forming-day read** (REQ-STORE-030 routes forming bars to the PG primary per-query), so a concurrent live-scanner forming-day upsert landing **between** the engine's main load and an aux load makes them see **different** forming bars — a torn cross-read silently violating PAR-045 on any to-present window. Pinned: the run **captures ONE forming-day read at SoA-build and serves all four reads — engine main load + B&H + btc_vol + MR-mean — from that single captured result**, not independent reads. **The captured snapshot is an IN-PROCESS BUFFER, NOT a long-lived open `repeatable_read` transaction (R5-F3-batch5, High — xmin-pinning hazard fix).** Holding a `repeatable_read` snapshot open across the whole ≤120s run (B&H attaches AFTER the engine pass, §2.0 lifecycle) would **pin `xmin` and block autovacuum on the shared live-trading DB** — the precise xmin-pinning hazard MIG-042 (§4.4) fails-fast on for the backfill, here reintroduced by the aux-read pin. Therefore the forming-day bars for every symbol the run needs (main + B&H benchmark + btc_vol series + MR-mean series) are **fetched ONCE into an in-process buffer at SoA-build time** (a single short read transaction that commits immediately, releasing `xmin`), and all four consumers read from that buffer — so cross-read consistency (REQ-PAR-045) is preserved by the shared buffer, NOT by an open transaction. **Connection-budget reconciliation (R5-F11-batch3, Medium):** because the four aux reads are served from the in-process buffer, they do NOT each hold a snapshot-pinned connection — there is **at most ONE short-lived connection per run for the forming-day capture** (released on commit), so the §7.5 connection budget's "1 per-run-stream" count is correct and 3 concurrent runs do NOT hold up-to-12 snapshot-pinned connections. (The rejected alternative — `pg_export_snapshot` + `SET TRANSACTION SNAPSHOT` across up to 4 concurrent connections held open for the load stage — is explicitly NOT used: it both pins xmin AND multiplies held connections, violating both MIG-042 and the §7.5 budget.) An **xmin-horizon assertion** confirms no backtest holds a snapshot/open-txn beyond a short capture budget (the backend `xmin` advances within the run, not pinned for ≤120s), and a **pool-exhaustion test** asserts 3 concurrent runs hold ≤3 forming-day-capture connections total (not 12). If a generation-token re-read is needed (a concurrent live-scanner forming-day upsert landed between the buffer capture and an aux consumer), the consumer re-reads under a fresh short transaction and the captured `data_generation` mismatch forces a single bounded re-capture — never a held snapshot. **`signal_time` is normalized to int64-ms UTC at the `_load_signals` ingress seam — pinned (R4-F14-batch6-c2, REQ-PAR-033, REQ-ENG-005/009).** REQ-PAR-033 requires `signal_time` normalized to Bybit-ms/UTC matching kline `open_time` BEFORE lookup, and the merge-walk `searchsorted` (REQ-ENG-005/009) requires signals to be in the **same int64-ms unit as the global timeline** (§4.1/§3.3 pin kline `open_time` to int64-ms; §3.2 pins ONE `canon(symbol,interval)`). But signals arrive from stored `scan_results` (`BacktestService._load_signals`, `backtest_service.py:523`) possibly as a Python `datetime` or a differently-based epoch — and no section previously pinned WHERE that conversion happens. Pinned: **every `signal_time` is converted to int64-ms-epoch UTC at ingress in `_load_signals`, identically to the kline `open_time` canonicalization** (`floor(extract(epoch)*1000)` for a `TIMESTAMPTZ`, identity for an already-ms epoch, with an explicit reject/normalize for a seconds-epoch), BEFORE any `searchsorted`/merge-walk uses it. This conversion is added to the canon/ingress contract (the same exact `TIMESTAMPTZ→epoch-ms` integer conversion the `content_sha256` basis uses, §4.1). A **fixture with `datetime`-typed signals AND offset/seconds-epoch signals** asserts identical entry-fill-bar resolution (a unit mismatch here would shift every entry-fill bar — REQ-ENG-005). Added to §12.3.

## 3.9 [NEW] `PreflightEstimator` — admission + envelope predictor (Phase 2 gate, cross-cutting)

**Module:** `backend/services/backtest_preflight.py` (new), reconciling/extending the existing `backend/mcp/core/preflight.py:run_preflight` (R1-F5 mig, R2-F4-batch5 — the divergence-permitting "either calls into or supersedes" is now a committed decision). **Decision: the estimator WRAPS-AND-DELEGATES to `run_preflight` as the single shared entrypoint — it does NOT reimplement preflight logic.** `backtest_preflight` calls `run_preflight(...)` for the shared admission/resource checks and only ADDS backtest-specific terms on top (SoA-bytes estimate, RSS reject-or-queue, partition/lifecycle dry-run). There is exactly ONE preflight implementation, so the two paths cannot diverge. No second copy of the preflight math exists; a test asserts both the backtest and MCP paths resolve to the same `run_preflight` callable. **Owner:** `BacktestService`.

**SweepRunner admits through the SoA-AWARE estimate, NOT bare `run_preflight` — seam pinned (R5-F5-batch2, Medium — mis-sized-aggregate-admission/OOM fix).** §3.6 lists `PreflightEstimator` as `SweepRunner`'s pre-fan-out admission/RSS sizer, but a sweep over a shared SoA has a real memory footprint: ONE shared read-only SoA (shipped once, §3.6) PLUS per-combo book/curve working sets. If the sweep admitted via **bare `run_preflight`** it would omit the SoA-bytes + global-timeline + build-transient memory terms (those live in `backtest_preflight`), under-sizing aggregate admission and risking OOM of the shared live process; if it admitted via `backtest_preflight`, the earlier "MCP calls `run_preflight` directly" wording would be false for the sweep path. **Pinned resolution:** the MCP single-shot `optimize`/`sweep` *feasibility* callers may still call `run_preflight` directly for the compute/network checks, but **`SweepRunner`'s aggregate-admission reservation goes through the SAME `AdmissionAccountant` using the SoA-AWARE estimate** — it reserves `shared_SoA_bytes (once) + Σ per-combo (book+curve) bytes`, computed by the `backtest_preflight` SoA terms (shared-SoA sized once, per-combo working sets summed across the fan-out width), NOT a bare compute/network estimate. A test asserts **sweep admission counts the shared-SoA bytes once + the per-combo bytes across the concurrency width** (and that two sweeps cannot jointly over-reserve the 1GB ceiling), proving the sweep path is sized on the SoA-aware memory model.

**Why a first-class component (R1-F3).** The estimator is cited 11× (Prime Directive cap row, §7.4 "runs BEFORE acquiring a slot", §9.4 telemetry, R12, coverage map PERF/OBS, Appendix B) and owns REQ-PERF-037/038/039 + REQ-API-021, but previously had no component definition, interface, owning module, placement contract, or self-cost budget. It is load-bearing and must be defined here.

**Interface.** `async estimate(config, universe, seal_state) -> PreflightVerdict{verdict: 'admit'|'queue'|'reject', pred_ms, pred_rss_bytes, pred_bybit_pages, drill_fraction, reason}`.

**Verdict enum reconciled — `'stream'` dropped, `'queue'` added (R5-F4 + R5-F7-batch1, High).** Earlier drafts carried `verdict ∈ {'admit','stream','reject'}`. Both ends are corrected here:
- **`'stream'` is REMOVED as a distinct verdict (R5-F7-batch1).** The R2-F2-batch1 correction (§3.1/§7.4/R12/Appendix B) established that streaming bounds ONLY the **load transient** and NEVER makes an over-ceiling **RUN-stage residency** run feasible: an over-ceiling run is REJECTED; an in-budget run is ADMITTED and streams its load **as a matter of course**. Under that model there is no run that is "streamable but not admittable," so `'stream'` distinct from `'admit'` is vestigial and dangerous (it invites an implementer to resurrect the rejected "stream an over-ceiling wide run" behavior). **Streaming is folded into the admit path as the default load mechanism:** every admitted run streams its load; the verdict does not encode it. (If a run's load transient alone would breach even though its RUN-stage residency fits, that is still an `'admit'` whose loader force-streams — never a separate verdict, and it NEVER relaxes the RUN-stage residency reject rule.)
- **`'queue'` is ADDED as the disposition for "fits-later" (R5-F4-batch1).** §7.4/§7.5 require **"queue-not-kill"**: a feasible wide run whose RUN-stage residency fits the 1GB ceiling but cannot be admitted RIGHT NOW because aggregate in-flight RSS is temporarily exhausted must WAIT for an in-flight run to release — it must NOT fall to `'reject'` (an acceptance-parity regression: a config the legacy engine completed would be refused). `'queue'` is that disposition; the `AdmissionAccountant` (below) owns the wait/dequeue. `'reject'` is reserved for a run that does NOT fit even alone (over-ceiling RUN-stage residency) or fails a dry-run/lifecycle check — a permanent no, never a "wait." So the three verdicts partition cleanly: **`'admit'`** = fits now (and streams its load), **`'queue'`** = fits once a slot frees (wait, bounded), **`'reject'`** = never fits / invalid (permanent). A test asserts an over-ceiling-alone config → `'reject'`, and a fits-alone-but-aggregate-full config → `'queue'` (not `'reject'`, not admitted-then-watchdog-killed).

**Inputs.** `SealedManifest` unsealed-day counts (SOR-present-but-unsealed = WARM, REQ-PERF-038); distinct signal + auxiliary symbols (e.g. BTC-vol series); window length; the full `AutoTradeConfig` (drill on/off, stop bands, leverage); `seal_backfill_marker` state.

**Formula basis (deterministic terms bracketed to ±50%, REQ-PERF-038).**
- compute term = `candles × scans` where `candles = symbols × days × bars_per_day` and the per-candle kernel runs **per open position** (eval-count uses the **config's own max book depth B**, not the global fixture B — see next bullet).
- **Book-depth B is derived from THIS config's capacity formula, NOT the canonical fixture's pinned B≈5 (R5-F1-batch2, High — infeasible-run admission fix).** The per-candle kernel cost scales with the number of simultaneously-open positions B, and B is **config-determined**: `B_cap = max_trades + mr_max_trades + carried_cycle_slack` (the trend book + the mean-reversion book + the cross-cycle carry the engine permits). A config with a DEEP book (high `max_trades`/`mr_max_trades`) has B far above the canonical fixture's ~5. If `estimate()` used the fixture's B as the eval-count denominator it would **under-predict** `heavy_eval_count`, `pred_ms`, and `pred_rss` for a deep-book config → the run is admitted, then hits the 120s kill — exactly the infeasible-run-that-times-out case REQ-PERF-037 exists to reject pre-flight. Pinned: **per-eval cost is CALIBRATED from the canonical fixture (cost-per-position-per-candle), but MULTIPLIED by THIS config's own `B_cap`** (from its `max_trades`/`mr_max_trades`/carry), so a deep-book config's compute and RSS terms scale with the book it can actually open. A **deep-book admission test** asserts a high-`max_trades` config whose `candles × scans × B_cap` exceeds the time/RSS envelope is **rejected/queued pre-flight**, not watchdog/timeout-killed mid-run. (The `peak_open_positions` OBS column §4.4 step-4 records the ACTUAL peak book depth per run, feeding back into B-calibration so the predictor tightens against observed deep-book cost.)
- cold-network term = `ceil(missing_bars / 1000)` Bybit pages (post page-size raise, §6.1).
- SoA-bytes term = `symbols × days × candles_per_day × 6 cols × 8 B` (int64+float64), plus the load-stage transient (REQ-PERF-014, §3.1 streaming seam) and book/curve/interpreter/live-process headroom (§7.4).
- **global-timeline term (R4-F6-batch6-c2 + R5-F4-batch2, REQ-STORE-017, REQ-ENG-014)** = `Σ(distinct timestamps across all symbols) × 8 B` (int64). This is the ADR-004 global sorted-unique timeline and is **O(unique timestamps)** — NOT covered by the per-symbol SoA-bytes term above. Canonical aligned listings collapse to ≈one symbol's timeline (~10 MB), but the **worst case is fully-misaligned timestamps** (per REQ-ENG-014) where the union approaches `Σ candles × 8 B` (≈168 MB for the 200sym×365d WIDE case). **The timeline has its OWN budget line, DISTINCT from the 150MB klines sub-budget (R5-F4-batch2, High — runnable-surface fix).** The earlier text said the timeline is "counted IN the klines budget (≤150MB)" yet gave a ~168MB worst case — i.e. the timeline ALONE exceeds the entire 150MB klines sub-budget before any OHLCV, so a moderately-misaligned multi-symbol universe (e.g. 100 symbols with staggered listings) that the legacy engine completed in RAM would be newly **rejected** by the default class — a runnable-surface (REQ-API-021 acceptance-parity) regression on a term legacy never paid. Pinned: the §7.4 budget gives the timeline a **separate `timeline_bytes` line** (`O(unique timestamps) × 8 B`, REQ-ENG-014 worst-case bound) ADDED to the klines sub-budget rather than carved out of it, and the WIDE run-class ceiling is raised to `klines(≤150MB) + timeline_bytes + book + curve + transients` so a legacy-feasible misaligned run is NOT newly rejected. The estimator uses the REQ-ENG-014 worst-case (misaligned) bound for the timeline line. A **misaligned-listing fixture** (≈100 symbols, staggered listings) is added to the **acceptance-parity replay set** (§3.9) and asserts (a) the timeline bytes are counted as their own line in the reject/queue decision AND (b) a legacy-feasible misaligned run is NOT newly rejected.
- **SoA-BUILD transient term (R4-F5-batch6-c2 + R5-F8-batch1)** = `input-SoA + O(unique-timestamps) timeline` — the genuine k-way-merge build peak (§3.3), NOT a generic "2× inputs+outputs". The per-symbol input arrays stay resident (they ARE the run's SoA; the k-way merge needs all heads at once and cannot release them), PLUS the growing union timeline of size `O(distinct timestamps)`. This term is the SOLE build-peak admission mechanism (the incremental-release option is struck — R5-F8-batch1); it is added to the admission sum.
- drill term (TIME) — **the bounded worst-case `p→1` (all-bars-drilled) is used ONLY to SIZE RSS residency (reject-on-memory), NEVER to reject-on-time (R5-F6-batch2, Medium — disambiguated).** The two earlier choices ("use p→1 for admission" AND "exclude the drill TIME term from the ±50% gate, let cap-headroom absorb it") were in tension: if p→1 actually drove a TIME reject, nearly every drill-ON run would be rejected (real drilled-fraction p is usually ≪1) — shrinking the runnable surface; if p→1 never rejects, a genuinely high-p drill run has NO time guard and hits the 120s kill (the very thing REQ-PERF-037 must catch). Pinned resolution: **(a)** the `p→1` worst-case feeds the **RSS residency term ONLY** (the drill-ON residency estimate below), so a run whose *memory* cannot hold the 1m fine-SoA is rejected/queued pre-flight; **(b)** a **separate, calibrated drill-TIME predictor** estimates the actual drilled-fraction from **stop tightness** (tighter stop bands relative to per-bar 5m range ⇒ more bars cross the band intrabar ⇒ higher p; the predictor maps `stop_loss_pct`/`take_profit_pct`/`trailing` band width vs the symbol's realized 5m bar amplitude to an expected drilled-fraction), and THAT calibrated p drives the time/`pred_ms` admission — so a *provably-infeasible* high-p drill run (calibrated p × per-drill 1m cost × candles > time envelope) CAN be rejected on time, while a typical low-p drill run is admitted. The drill-TIME term remains **excluded from the ±50% accuracy gate** (drilled-fraction is volatility-dependent and not bit-knowable pre-run), but it is no longer absent — it is a calibrated estimate with documented basis (drill-fraction-from-stop-tightness), and cap-headroom (≤50% of 120s) absorbs its residual error. A test asserts a tight-stop high-drill-fraction config that would time out is rejected on the calibrated drill-TIME term, and a loose-stop low-drill config is admitted.
- **drill-ON RSS residency term (R4-F5-batch6-c5, REQ-PERF-012) — admitted, NOT only watchdog-caught.** A drill-ON run additionally holds the `DrilldownLoader` 1m memo (§3.5) + per-bar 1m fine-SoA arrays resident **ON TOP of** the 5m working set, but the SoA-bytes term above is the **5m base only** and the §7.4 150MB klines budget is the **final 5m SoA only** — so a drill-ON run could breach the 1GB/150MB ceiling without pre-flight catching it (only the runtime RSS watchdog would, i.e. an acceptance-parity-violating abort, §3.9). The estimator's RSS term is therefore extended to **add a drill-ON residency estimate = `drilled-bar-fraction × per-bar 1m-array bytes + 1m-memo footprint`** into the aggregate admission check (a drill-ON run carries its OWN ceiling budgeting 1m fine residency on top of the 5m set — REQ-PERF-012). A **drill-ON admission test** asserts a run whose `5m + 1m` residency exceeds the ceiling is **rejected/queued at pre-flight**, not watchdog-aborted mid-run.

**Placement + self-cost.** Runs **cheap-bounded BEFORE reserving a `_MAX_CONCURRENT` slot** in `create_backtest` (`:191`, slot reservation ~`:222`) so a rejected run consumes no slot (REQ-PERF-037). Its own async DB work (manifest unsealed-day counts, distinct-symbol sizing) is itself budgeted (a sub-100ms latency target) and **rate-limited per client** so it cannot become an unbudgeted DoS/overload vector ahead of the slot gate (R1-F3). Calibration source for the ±50% bracket: the canonical + wide fixtures, host-aware, logged predicted-vs-actual (§9.4).

**Acceptance-parity (R1-F5 mig, REQ-API-021 — hard).** The estimator MUST NOT reject or batch-degrade any config that the legacy engine completed within budget; the runnable surface must not shrink. A **parity-of-acceptance gate** replays every golden-proven-feasible config through `estimate()` and asserts `verdict != 'reject'`. A mis-calibrated estimator that shrinks the runnable surface fails CI.

**Admission is GLOBAL / concurrency-aware — the single-process budget is an AGGREGATE across in-flight slots (R3-F2-batch1 + R3-F4-batch5, REQ-PERF-013, REQ-API-021).** The §7.4 `1GB` RSS / `150MB` klines budgets are derived for ONE run, but `_MAX_CONCURRENT=3` allows three independent runs over different universes simultaneously, **each holding its OWN live, non-evictable SoA** for its entire duration (RUN-stage residency is the full SoA, R2-F2-batch1; the `_ProcessLRU` 150MB budget governs shared *sealed read-frames*, NOT a run's active working set, and **cannot evict an in-flight run's SoA** — the running engine holds a live Python reference). Three wide runs ⇒ ≈`3×(SoA + book + curve)`, which can blow the 1GB ceiling even though each run individually fits. A per-run `estimate(config, universe, seal_state)` that sizes only THIS run is therefore insufficient: an individually-admitted third run is then **cooperatively aborted by the runtime RSS watchdog**, which silently shrinks the runnable surface under concurrency and **breaks REQ-API-021 acceptance-parity** (a config the legacy engine completed gets killed). Pinned resolution:
- `estimate()` gains inputs for **current process RSS** + the **resident footprint of the other occupied slots**, supplied by the **`AdmissionAccountant`** — a first-class named component (below), NOT an unscoped parenthetical — that *reserves* predicted bytes at slot grant and *releases* at completion. Admission checks `Σ(resident in-flight run RSS) + this_run_estimate + interpreter + live headroom ≤ 1GB`, not just this run.
- When the aggregate would breach, the run is **queued (not rejected, not admitted-then-killed)** until a slot's bytes free — preserving acceptance-parity (the config is still *accepted*, just serialized).
- Either lower the effective per-run klines budget to `150MB / _MAX_CONCURRENT`, OR gate concurrent SoA-bearing runs so their summed final SoA + transients fit 1GB with live headroom reserved — the chosen reconciliation is stated in §7.4.
- **A watchdog abort of an individually-admitted run is documented as an acceptance-parity violation** (it must be prevented by concurrency-aware admission, not relied upon). A **3-concurrent-wide-run aggregate-RSS test** asserts the third run queues rather than OOM-aborting. On the PRIMARY single-worker target (§2.0) the accountant is process-local; on the [FLEET] variant it is per-pod.

**`AdmissionAccountant` — named component, owned by `BacktestService`, with a pinned thread-safety contract (R4-F7-batch6-c2, REQ-API-021, REQ-PERF-013).** The aggregate-admission bookkeeping is a **shared mutable concurrency primitive in the live FastAPI process** (`_MAX_CONCURRENT=3` runs + a sweep pool concurrently reserving/releasing), so it is given a real owner and contract rather than left as "a shared admission accountant":
- **Owner / module:** `BacktestService` holds the single process-local (per-pod on [FLEET]) `AdmissionAccountant` instance; the `PreflightEstimator` consults it, the create-backtest slot path and the `SweepRunner` fan-out both reserve/release through it.
- **Reservation record (pinned data structure — R5-F3-batch1).** The accountant holds `_reserved: dict[token, Reservation]` where `Reservation = {token: uuid, bytes: int, run_id: str, kind: 'run'|'sweep_combo', reserved_at: ts}` plus a running `_reserved_total: int` (the single source of truth, kept == `Σ _reserved[*].bytes` under the lock) and a `_queue: deque[QueueEntry]` where `QueueEntry = {run_id, bytes, enqueued_at, waiter: asyncio.Future}`. The running total is incremented under the lock on grant and decremented on release; it is never recomputed from RSS (RSS is sampled separately by the watchdog §7.4 and reconciled via the `admission_reservation_vs_actual_bytes` SLI).
- **Interface:** `async reserve(bytes:int, run_id:str) -> token | Queued` and `try_reserve(bytes:int) -> bool` (non-blocking peek used by the estimator to decide `'admit'` vs `'queue'`) and `async release(token) -> None`. On `reserve`, under the lock: if `_reserved_total + bytes ≤ budget` → create `Reservation`, bump total, return token (`'admit'`); else enqueue a `QueueEntry` and return `Queued` (the verdict is `'queue'`), the caller awaiting the entry's `waiter` future up to the queue-wait timeout. Reservations are keyed by token so a double-release or a release of an unknown token is a logged no-op, not a silent under-count.
- **Dequeue-trigger (pinned — R5-F3-batch1).** `release(token)` is the SOLE dequeue trigger: under the lock it removes the `Reservation`, decrements `_reserved_total`, then **drains the queue head-first while the freed budget admits the next waiter** — for each `QueueEntry` at the head whose `bytes ≤ budget - _reserved_total`, it creates that entry's `Reservation`, bumps the total, and resolves its `waiter` future (waking the queued run to slot-grant). Draining stops at the first head that still does not fit (FIFO is preserved; a large run at the head is NOT skipped by a smaller one behind it, preventing starvation/priority-inversion of wide runs). This makes "a slot's bytes free → the next feasible queued run is admitted" a deterministic, lock-held transition rather than a poll. A queue-wait-timeout firing on a waiter removes its entry and releases nothing (it never held bytes).
- **Thread-safety:** all reserve/release/drain mutations are guarded by a single `asyncio.Lock` (the FastAPI process is single-event-loop; the executor/ProcessPool submit paths marshal their reserve/release back through the loop, or use a `threading.Lock` if called from the executor thread) so concurrent reserve/release **cannot interleave to over-admit (OOM) or deadlock**. The running total is the single source of truth checked by every admission.
- **Leak-safe release on EVERY terminal path:** the reservation is released in a `finally` covering **complete / fail / 120s-timeout-kill / cooperative-cancel** — a run that dies without releasing would permanently shrink the runnable surface (a stuck reservation), so release is tied to run finalization, not to the happy path. A reconcile on boot (§3.6) zeroes the accountant since no runs are in-flight.
- **Reserve against the UPPER bound of the estimate, not the point estimate (R5-F2-batch2, Medium).** §9.4 permits the pre-flight estimate to be off by ±50%. If the accountant reserved the POINT estimate and every in-flight run systematically under-predicted by 50%, three runs reserved at predicted bytes could actually consume up to ~2× → the aggregate "queue-not-kill" guarantee degrades back into a watchdog abort of an individually-admitted run (the acceptance-parity violation §3.9 says concurrency-aware admission must PREVENT, not rely on at runtime). Therefore `reserve()` is called with `pred_rss_bytes × 1.5` (the upper bound of the ±50% bracket), NOT the point estimate, so the worst-case-allowed under-prediction still fits the ceiling.
