The `admission_reservation_vs_actual_bytes` SLI continuously reconciles reserved-vs-measured; when measured drift is positive (runs consuming more than reserved), future admissions tighten (the accountant raises its reservation multiplier toward the observed p95). A test where EVERY run under-predicts by the full allowed 50% asserts **no watchdog abort** occurs (the 1.5× reservation absorbs it).
- **Test:** a **3-concurrent + sweep reserve/release stress test** asserts no over-admit (Σ never exceeds the budget) and no stuck reservation (every terminal path releases; the accountant returns to zero when idle). A **deterministic-resolution test (R5-F3-batch1)** drives **3 concurrent wide-run admits + a watchdog-down event** (§7.5 tightens admission when the RSS watchdog is unavailable) and asserts every run resolves to exactly one of `{admit, queue, reject}` with **no race** (the lock serializes the three reserves; the watchdog-down state flips the accountant to the conservative reservation multiplier before the admits evaluate) and **exactly-once release** per admitted run (a queued run that is later admitted releases once; a queue-wait-timeout releases nothing). The test pins the outcome (which runs admit, which queue, which reject) as a deterministic function of submission order + reserved bytes, proving the accountant is not best-effort under concurrency.

**Admission-queue semantics are pinned (R4-F6-batch6-c5, REQ-API-021).** The "queue-not-kill" path (a run admitted-to-`queued` until a slot's bytes free) introduces a persisted `queued` state (admitted to the v58 status CHECK, §4.4) whose operational semantics are made explicit rather than left open:
- **Bounded queue depth.** The queue has a documented max depth; a submission past it is **rejected with an actionable message** (not enqueued unbounded) so a wide-run pile-up cannot starve interactive backtests behind an unbounded blocking POST.
- **Queue-wait timeout, distinct from the 120s run cap.** A `queued` run that does not get a slot within a documented queue-wait timeout fails with a retriable "capacity" error — separate from the 120s `_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` run cap.
- **Ordering/fairness.** FIFO by submission time (or a documented priority) so admission is fair and predictable; interactive single backtests are not indefinitely overtaken by sweep-spawned runs.
- **The 120s run-clock ARMS AT SLOT-GRANT, not at enqueue (pinned).** A run's `_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` timer starts when it is granted a slot and actually begins executing — NOT when it enters the queue — so queue-wait time is never charged against the run's compute budget. A test asserts a `queued` run's run-clock starts at slot grant.
- **Interaction with the per-client rate limit.** The §3.9 per-client rate limit on `estimate()` still applies ahead of the queue, so the queue cannot be flooded by one client.
- **Leaked-reservation reconciliation.** A run that terminates (complete/fail/kill/cancel) without releasing its `AdmissionAccountant` reservation is reconciled (released) on run termination and at boot, so a leaked reservation cannot silently shrink the runnable surface; a test asserts a leaked reservation is reclaimed.
- **New SLIs (registered in the §9 central registry, surfaced on §5.4):** `admission_queue_depth` (gauge), `admission_queue_wait_ms` (timer), and `admission_reservation_vs_actual_bytes` (gauge — reserved-at-grant vs measured RSS, so reservation drift / a leaked reservation is observable, not silent). These join the §9.7 alerting set.

## 3.10 [NEW] `SealBackfillRunner` — deferred, resumable, throttled historical sealer (Phase 1, off the boot path)

**Module:** `backend/services/seal_backfill_runner.py` (new). Started as a post-migration background task by `backend.main` lifespan **after** `schema_version` reaches 58 — never inside the migration transaction, never on the asyncio loop's critical path.

**Why (R1-F1 / R1-F1 dup migration, Critical).** v58 ships DDL only; existing complete-but-unsealed historical days still need sealing. Doing that inline at boot under the global migration advisory lock with a 30s `lock_timeout` is a deploy-time crash-loop hazard (§4.4). This component does it safely out-of-band.

**Responsibility.**
- Acquire a **dedicated election lock** (a `pg_advisory_lock` key **disjoint** from the migration key 8675309 and the live-scanner keys — REQ-MIG-025/027) so exactly one instance backfills at a time. **The election lock and every chunk transaction run on a dedicated DIRECT (non-pooled, session-pinned) asyncpg connection (R2-F3-batch3, REQ-MIG-028)** — the same pattern as the migration runner's `asyncpg.connect()` (`async_persistence.py:1588`), NEVER the transaction-pooled app pool. Rationale: if the app pool's DSN targets **pgBouncer in transaction mode**, a session-level `pg_advisory_lock` and session GUCs (`lock_timeout`, `statement_timeout`) are unsafe — the lock could be acquired on one server backend while later work runs on another, silently breaking the "exactly one runner" guarantee (duplicate runners / double-seal) or making the lock a no-op. A pooling-mode test asserts the election lock is held on a **session-pinned backend** (REQ-MIG-028).
- **Bounded-window re-election after runner death (R2-F6-batch3, REQ-MIG-025).** A session advisory lock auto-releases when the elected runner's connection dies, but if no surviving instance is contending, the backfill would stall until the next deploy. Surviving instances therefore run a **periodic `pg_try_advisory_lock` poll** (bounded interval) on the election key; on acquisition a survivor **resumes from the marker/seal checkpoint** within a bounded detection window — no manual restart. A kill-elected-runner-then-resume test asserts a survivor picks up within the documented window (REQ-MIG-025).
- Build `idx_coverage_unsealed` via `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY IF NOT EXISTS` (outside any txn), self-healing an `indisvalid=false` leftover by `DROP`+rebuild, then `ANALYZE` (REQ-MIG-033/034). **A SECOND `ANALYZE` + bounded `VACUUM (ANALYZE)` runs after the bulk seal-backfill flips the marker to `complete`/`complete_with_skips` (R4-F5-batch6, REQ-MIG-034):** the bulk seal `UPDATE` flips rows from ~100% `NOT sealed` to ~0%, so the partial-index selectivity stats captured at build time are stale; without the post-backfill re-ANALYZE the planner can seq-scan the `unsealed_days` query, and without the bounded VACUUM the chunked `UPDATE` churn bloats the table with dead tuples. The REQ-MIG-034 `EXPLAIN`-uses-index gate is asserted on the **post-backfill mostly-sealed distribution**, not the empty freshly-built table. **Bound the no-index window cost (R2-F9-batch2, REQ-MIG-033):** during the entire CIC build the hot `unsealed_days` predicate (`WHERE NOT sealed AND date BETWEEN …` across many symbols) runs **un-indexed** (the PK `(symbol,interval,date)` does not serve a multi-symbol `NOT sealed`+range scan well) precisely while the runner is also scanning/updating the same table. The build is therefore EITHER done **before** bulk sealing begins, OR the unsealed-day query cost during the window is **capped/measured under the §9.5 loop-lag SLI**; the expected degraded-but-bounded query plan during the no-index window is documented. **The CIC build has its OWN bounded duration budget + stall/abort/retry behavior + IO-load telemetry (R4-F6-batch6-c4):** `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` does two full table scans AND waits for all transactions seeing the table to drain — on a DB under continuous live-scanner `_update_coverage` upserts plus long backtest/analytics transactions it can **stall for a very long time or repeatedly leave `indisvalid=false`**, and its WAL/IO competes with the live order path. (A `lock_timeout` on the brief catalog steps does NOT bound the scan duration.) Pinned: the CIC build is given **(a) an explicit wall-time budget** with **progress/stall telemetry** (`cic_build_ms{index}`, a stall gauge); **(b) stall/abort/retry behavior** — if the build exceeds budget or is repeatedly drained, it **aborts and retries on the next maintenance window**, and the loader **degrades to the documented no-index plan** (the bounded-but-degraded `unsealed_days` scan) rather than the runner blocking unbounded against the live process; **(c) its wall-time AND its impact on `live_scanner_fetch_latency_p95` are added to the §9.5/§9.7 measured+alerted set** (the §9.7 `migration_ms` covers only the in-txn v58 and explicitly excludes the out-of-band CIC, and the §9.5 `live_scanner_fetch_latency_p95` window is widened to name the CIC build as a distinct, potentially-longer operation than the v58 DDL + backfill window). A stuck CIC thus degrades observably to the no-index plan, never runs unbounded.
- **Out-of-band `mcp_sweep_results` unique-index build (R4-F4-batch6-c2, REQ-SWEEP-012/013).** If v58's step-4b found no UNIQUE constraint on `(sweep_id, config_hash)` (the `ON CONFLICT` target crash-resume/dedup depend on), `SealBackfillRunner` startup builds it **out-of-band, never inside the v58 txn**: a **dedup pre-pass** removes any pre-existing duplicate `(sweep_id, config_hash)` rows (keep latest by `engine_fingerprint`/timestamp), then `CREATE UNIQUE INDEX CONCURRENTLY IF NOT EXISTS uq_mcp_sweep_results_sweepcfg ON mcp_sweep_results(sweep_id, config_hash)` with the same `indisvalid=false` self-heal as `idx_coverage_unsealed`, then clears the `deferred_unique_mcp_sweep_results` marker to `done`. The **migration-completeness meta-test asserts the constraint is present-or-scheduled** (marker `pending`/`done`), and a sweep persist that runs before the build completes uses a documented fallback (parent-side `SELECT … FOR UPDATE`-then-UPSERT) so no sweep fails on a missing ON CONFLICT target. A dedup-then-build test asserts a populated table with duplicates builds the unique index without error.
- Seal historical days in **separately-committed chunks** (per-symbol-month), each under a short `SET LOCAL lock_timeout` **AND `SET LOCAL statement_timeout`** (R2-F5-dup, REQ-MIG-036 — sized to the per-chunk budget, surviving any server-global `idle_in_transaction_session_timeout`) with retry/backoff and optional `SKIP LOCKED`, recomputing the frontier per chunk (identical code path, REQ-MIG-012), using the frontier+lifecycle predicate + GROUP-BY-over-actual-rows day_class (NOT count-vs-expected — REQ-MIG-011/013).
- **`candle_count` is OVERWRITTEN from a set-based `COUNT(DISTINCT open_time)` at seal (R2-F3-batch2, REQ-MIG-013, REQ-STORE-028).** The live writer maintains `candle_count = GREATEST(existing, this_batch_count)` (`kline_cache_service.py:314`) — the MAX single-batch contribution, NOT the cumulative distinct count: a day fetched in two non-overlapping batches (bars 0–143 then 144–287) stores 288 rows but records `candle_count=144`. If a stale GREATEST value were sealed, the read invariant `row_count == candle_count − gap_count` (§4.1, REQ-STORE-028) would fail forever → perpetual invalidate+rebuild. Therefore BOTH the `SealBackfillRunner` AND the runtime lazy-seal path **recompute and OVERWRITE `candle_count` (and `first/last_open_ts`) with the actual `COUNT(DISTINCT open_time)`** for the day at seal time, superseding the GREATEST-maintained value. A recompute-vs-stored test on a multi-batch (split) day asserts sealed `candle_count` == distinct rows and the read invariant holds.
- **One-shot post-frontier reverify for ambiguous interior holes (R4-F1-batch6, REQ-MIG-014).** The `GROUP BY`-over-actual-rows day_class derivation distinguishes a **complete-but-short** day (first/last bar consistent with a mid-day listing or a known halt → seals terminally `day_class=2`, no reverify) from an **ambiguous interior hole** — an interior missing-bar run that may be a true structural gap OR a legacy-bug artifact (the false-permanent-cache failure ADR-003/the seal model exists to kill). An ambiguous interior hole seals `day_class=3` **with `gap_count`/`gap_ranges` AND `reverify_pending=true`** rather than going straight to permanent `sealed-empty-negative`. The runner then gives that day **exactly one** re-fetch attempt **after it crosses the completion frontier** (so the hole cannot be a still-forming-edge artifact): on the reverify, (a) if Bybit now returns the missing bars, the day is **re-sealed** `day_class=1/2` with recomputed `content_sha256`/`candle_count` (un-seal→re-verify→re-seal cycle); (b) if the hole persists, `reverify_pending` clears to `false` and the day becomes a settled `day_class=3/4` negative-cache, never re-probed again. The reverify is **idempotent and one-shot** — a `reverify_pending=true` row is visited at most once post-frontier, tracked so a runner restart does not re-probe a day already reverified. While `reverify_pending=true` the runtime loader treats the day as **WARM/refetchable** (like an unsealed day), so a feasible run never sees it as a false negative-cache. Tests (REQ-MIG-014): an **interior-hole fixture** (asserts class-3 + `reverify_pending=true`, not class-4 permanent), an **ambiguous-hole-filled-on-reverify** fixture (re-seal to class 1/2), and an **ambiguous-hole-confirmed** fixture (one probe, then `reverify_pending=false` permanent — asserts the second rerun issues 0 Bybit calls).
- **Backfill seals carry NULL `content_sha256` + NULL `fetched_at` — the hash is computed ONLY on a genuine fresh Bybit fetch (R4-F6-batch6, REQ-MIG-016).** REQ-MIG-016 requires a backfilled sealed day to read as "no integrity check available" (never `mismatch→refetch`), and §4.1 already pins **`content_sha256 = NULL` ⇒ no comparable hash ⇒ no integrity check, no refetch** (REQ-STORE-004). These two are reconciled by **scoping which seals compute a hash:** the atomic seal `UPDATE` below computes `content_sha256` from a `kline_cache` sub-select **only on the fresh-fetch seal path** (bars that just arrived from Bybit, whose hash is authoritative for drift detection). The **`SealBackfillRunner` seal of pre-existing stored rows leaves `content_sha256` NULL and `fetched_at` NULL/untouched** (sentinel "no check available") — it does NOT compute a hash from rows of unknown provenance, because a computed-from-stored sha on a day the SOR never freshly fetched could later mismatch a real fetch and re-trigger exactly the false-positive refetch Phase 1 targets. Backfilled days still seal (frontier+lifecycle predicate, `candle_count`/`first/last_open_ts`/`day_class` all set); only the hash stays NULL until a future genuine fresh fetch of that day stamps it. The §4.1 SOR-integrity backstop (REQ-CACHE-043) checks **row-count** for NULL-sha days and **sha** only where present — a NULL-sha day is never treated as drift. Tests (REQ-MIG-016): a **backfilled-seal-carries-NULL-sha / TTL-exempt** test (the day is `sealed=true`, `content_sha256 IS NULL`, and a rerun issues 0 Bybit calls — NULL is "no check", not "stale"), and a **fresh-fetch-stamps-sha** test (the same day later fetched fresh seals with a non-NULL hash).
- **Seal write is serialized against the live coverage upsert — concrete protocol pinned (R2-F8-batch2 + R3-F7-batch3, REQ-MIG-030/031).** The runner computes `candle_count`/`content_sha256` from a `kline_cache` snapshot and must commit the seal so the live scanner's concurrent `_update_coverage` `DO UPDATE SET candle_count = GREATEST(…)` cannot interleave to leave a sealed row whose `content_sha256` (snapshot S1) and `candle_count` (a later S2 batch) describe **different** row sets. The earlier "single statement under `SELECT … FOR UPDATE`" wording was self-contradictory (one statement cannot be both a `SELECT … FOR UPDATE` and an upsert). **Pinned protocol — choose ONE, stated here:** a **single atomic `UPDATE kline_cache_coverage SET sealed=true, content_sha256=…, candle_count=(SELECT COUNT(DISTINCT open_time) …), first_open_ts=…, last_open_ts=…, day_class=…, sealed_at=now() WHERE (symbol,interval,date)=… AND sealed=false`** whose `candle_count`/sha are computed from a **sub-select over `kline_cache` in the SAME statement** — so the count and the row set are read at one point and the live `GREATEST` bump cannot interleave between the sha read and the count read. (Equivalent alternative: hold an explicit `SELECT … FOR UPDATE` row lock across BOTH the snapshot read and the seal write **within one transaction** — two statements, one lock held throughout — never a lock dropped between them.) A post-seal live bump on a sealed day triggers **sha-invalidate / re-seal** (it must not silently raise `candle_count` past the sealed sha). A concurrent-seal-vs-live-upsert **consistency** test (distinct from the existing no-deadlock test) asserts `candle_count` and `content_sha256` describe the same row set. **(Scope note, R4-F6-batch6:** the `content_sha256=…` sub-select term applies only on the fresh-fetch seal path; the `SealBackfillRunner` backfill of pre-existing stored rows sets `content_sha256=NULL` per the NULL-sha bullet above, so the same atomic `UPDATE` writes a literal NULL there and the count/row-set consistency guarantee still holds for `candle_count`/`first_open_ts`/`last_open_ts`.)
- Throttle on replica-lag / WAL pressure (REQ-MIG-036); honor a DRAIN/QUIESCE pause request (REQ-MIG-032); never deadlock or long-block the live scanner's `_update_coverage` upserts (REQ-MIG-030/031).
- **Reconcile rows stranded in `kline_cache_default` (R2-F6-batch2/R2-F35, REQ-STORE-001, REQ-MIG-035).** Detect months with rows in the default partition (written before their monthly partition existed) and move them into the correct monthly partition (move-out → create → re-insert/`ATTACH`), restoring the default-empty invariant the seal/columnar pruning depends on. (Detailed in §4.4 partition bullets.) **Serialized against concurrent live inserts for the same month (R3-F10-batch2, REQ-STORE-002):** the move-out/create/`ATTACH`/verify-empty sequence has no atomicity against (a) the live scanner still INSERTing forming/recent rows that route to `kline_cache_default` for month M, or (b) `store_klines`'s own `_ensure_partition_exists` racing to create the same partition — if rows arrive in the default for M mid-move, the `ATTACH`/verify-empty step can fail or strand rows, re-violating the default-empty invariant. Pinned: the reconcile runs **under a dedicated advisory lock on a disjoint key that `store_klines`'s partition-create path ALSO respects** (so the two cannot both create/attach partition M), OR it **quiesces writes for month M during the swap**; `verify-empty` then **re-checks in a loop until stable**. A concurrency test drives live inserts targeting the default for M while the reconcile runs and asserts **no stranded rows, no double-attach, default-empty after quiescence** (REQ-STORE-002).
- Maintain `seal_backfill_marker` (counters + state + skip set); on completion flip to `complete` (or `complete_with_skips` with a remediation set). Fully resumable from the marker after a restart.

**Marker-ahead-of-data detection after PITR/failover (R2-F1-batch3, REQ-MIG-026).** A session advisory lock and the marker do NOT catch a **same-DB rewind** where a partial restore leaves `marker='complete'` while `kline_cache` data has been rewound below the marker — the runtime would then trust `complete`, treat now-missing days as sealed (0 Bybit calls), and run on an incomplete cache believing it complete (a correctness/data-loss failure the seal model exists to prevent). Resolution: a **durable monotonic data-generation token** (the SOR-wide `sor_data_generation` counter, §4.1) is recorded into `seal_backfill_marker` at completion **and** into each sealed coverage row. On boot the runner compares the marker/seal generation against the **live SOR generation**; on mismatch (data rewound below the marker) it **invalidates the marker (→ `in_progress`), re-evaluates seals, and resumes**. A "marker-ahead-of-data" detection test is added to §12.3 (REQ-MIG-026). (This is the SOR-level generation token of §4 — see the SOR-generation subsection.)

**`data_generation` is stamped at seal time; FROZEN for steady-state + rewind-DETECTION, MUTABLE only via the post-detection PITR/DR re-stamp (R3-F2-batch3 + R4-F7-batch6-c5, REQ-ROLL-023/CACHE-043).** v58 is DDL-only, so all pre-existing coverage rows get `data_generation = 0` (the column default). The `SealBackfillRunner` AND the runtime lazy-seal path therefore MUST **stamp `coverage.data_generation` with the current `sor_data_generation` value at seal time** (it is set in the SAME atomic seal `UPDATE` as `content_sha256`/`candle_count` above). **Precise classification (reconciled with the §4.1 mutability contract):** `data_generation` is **FROZEN in steady state and AT rewind-detection time** — no silent UPDATE, and the seal-time stamp must persist so per-row rewind detection can compare it — with **exactly ONE documented mutation: the post-detection PITR/DR re-stamp.** The order is pinned: a PITR/restore bumps `sor_data_generation` to N+1; rewind **detection compares each sealed row's still-old stamp (N) against the live SOR gen (N+1)** and fires on mismatch; the seal model then **re-evaluates** the affected rows, and rows whose bytes are confirmed unchanged are **re-stamped in place to N+1** (NOT un-sealed/refetched/sha-recomputed — bytes unchanged) so fine and derived-coarse generations **re-converge and stop re-triggering**. Without the re-stamp, `fine_base_generation == data_generation` (derived-coarse) would never re-match after a rewind, forcing perpetual coarse re-derivation; with a naive always-re-stamp, detection could never fire. The frozen-for-detection / re-stamp-after-detection split satisfies both. **Rewind-detection compares per-row `data_generation`** (not only the marker's stored value) so a partial rewind affecting a subset of rows is caught. Tests: a **"backfilled-row-carries-current-generation"** test (a seal stamps the live generation, not 0), a **"PITR-rewind-invalidates-backfilled-sealed-rows"** test, and a **"derived-coarse re-derives exactly once then stops"** test (the re-stamp converges fine+coarse, no perpetual mismatch — §4.1 mutability contract).

**Marker carries its own generation column (R3-F3-batch3, REQ-MIG-026).** The PITR-rewind detection reads a generation value FROM `seal_backfill_marker`, so the marker DDL (§4.4) carries an explicit **`data_generation BIGINT` column** that the runner writes on flip-to-`complete`/`complete_with_skips`. Without it the boot check has nothing to compare against. The migration-completeness meta-test enumerates this column on `seal_backfill_marker`.

**Interface.** `async run() -> None` (idempotent, resumable); `async status() -> {state, days_total, days_sealed, skipped[]}` (feeds the runtime status route §5.4).

**Wrong-DB / standby guard (R1-F7 mig, REQ-MIG-043).** Before any seal write, verify a configured **DB-identity row** (committed concrete guard, not three alternatives) matches the expected environment; on a read-only/standby connection, SKIP/DEFER rather than crash-loop. The backfill is the only "destructive-capable" path and carries this guard explicitly.

**Dependencies.** `SealedManifest` (predicate + marker), Postgres (`kline_cache_coverage`, `symbol_lifecycle`, `seal_backfill_marker`). Import-isolated from accel/engine modules so it runs on the lean image (REQ-MIG-029).

## 3.11 [NEW] `SymbolLifecycleRefresher` — populates/refreshes `symbol_lifecycle` (Phase 1, off the boot path)

**Module:** `backend/services/symbol_lifecycle_refresher.py` (new) — OR folded into an existing maintenance task; either way it is a **first-class, owned component**, not an undefined "background task" (R2-F8-batch1 / R2-F3-batch5, REQ-CACHE-026/030, REQ-MIG-015). Without it, the `symbol_lifecycle` table the v58 DDL creates stays **empty**, the frontier+lifecycle predicate degenerates to `NULL ⇒ [-∞,+∞] ⇒ fetch-everything` for every symbol (correct but the **negative-cache optimization never engages** — pre-listing/post-delist days are re-probed every run), and ~4 of the 7 day-classes (`sealed-empty-negative`, `sealed-delist-snapped`, and the listing/delist seal bounds) have **no data source**. It is load-bearing for those classes.

**Responsibility.**
- **Source of truth:** Bybit instrument-info (listing time / delist/status) via the existing accounts/instrument API surface; refresh `symbol_lifecycle(symbol, listing_time, delist_time, source, updated_at)`.
- **Operator-override preservation (REQ-CACHE-026):** a refresh **merges** Bybit values without clobbering operator-set overrides (an explicit `source`/precedence rule — operator rows win), so a wrong upstream value can't silently erase a manual correction.
- **Schedule + staleness budget:** runs on a bounded periodic schedule (documented interval) with a staleness budget; a row older than the budget is refreshed opportunistically.
- **Election + advisory-lock disjointness:** acquires its own advisory-lock key, **disjoint** from the migration key (8675309), the `SealBackfillRunner` election key, and the live-scanner keys (REQ-MIG-027), on a **direct/session-pinned connection** (same pgBouncer-safety rule as §3.10).
- **Failure / degradation + cold-start contract (the load-bearing invariant):** a **stale or missing `symbol_lifecycle` row degrades to fetch-everything, NEVER to seal-known-empty** (REQ-MIG-009). Until the table is populated the negative-cache classes are **inert** and everything is fetch-and-discover (correct, just unoptimized) — so a refresher outage can never hide real data behind a permanent negative cache.

**Interface.** `async refresh(symbols: list[str] | None = None) -> RefreshReport`; `async status() -> {rows, last_refresh, stale_count}`.

**Late-population reclassification (REQ-MIG-015).** When the refresher populates `symbol_lifecycle` AFTER days were already sealed, it drives the **post-seal reclassification** of `listing_snapped`/`delisted`/`day_class` (per the seal-row mutability contract, §4.1) **without un-sealing, refetching, or changing `content_sha256`** — a documented `UPDATE` path, not a re-seal. A reclassify-after-late-lifecycle test asserts no un-seal, no Bybit call, sha unchanged.

**Dependencies.** Bybit instrument-info source, Postgres (`symbol_lifecycle`, and read of `kline_cache_coverage` for reclassification). Import-isolated from accel/engine modules (lean image, REQ-MIG-029).

## 3.12 [NEW] `MaintenanceAdmin` — seal-reset / manifest-rebuild / DR / provenance-enumeration surface (R3-F6-batch4, High — REQ-ROLL-024/025/030/032/033)

**Module:** `backend/services/backtest_maintenance.py` (new) exposed as **CLI sub-commands ONLY** (`python -m backend.maintenance <cmd>`). Several P1/cross MUST/SHOULD rollback+DR requirements had **no owning component** — `SealBackfillRunner` only seals *forward*; none of these reset/rebuild/DR/enumeration paths were defined. This component owns them so they are not orphaned in the coverage map.

**CLI-ONLY — the "admin-only routes" option is DROPPED; there is no auth substrate to gate them (R5-F3-batch4, High — undefined-interface / unauthenticated-destructive-endpoint fix).** Earlier wording offered "CLI sub-commands and/or admin-only routes (auth-gated, not the public backtest API)". But the repo has **NO authentication substrate** (confirmed grounding: single-user app, "no auth system exists", the backtesting frontend is unauthenticated, §8 intro "no new authentication"). "auth-gated admin-only routes" therefore references a **non-existent mechanism** — an undefined interface; if implemented as HTTP routes they would be **unauthenticated destructive endpoints on the same bound port as the public API** (`reset_seals`, `rebuild_manifest`, `dr_rebuild`, `enumerate_affected→mark-stale/queue-rerun`, `classify_foreign`), reachable by CSRF-from-browser, SSRF, or any local process — a DR rebuild / mass seal reset / bulk result invalidation triggerable with no credential. **Pinned (one choice, not "and/or"):** these operations are **CLI-only, out-of-band**, gated by **OS/file permissions** (who can run `python -m backend.maintenance` on the host) **+ the §8.5 DB-identity guard** (so even the CLI cannot run against the wrong DB). They are **NOT** exposed as HTTP routes. The §8 "no new authentication" claim therefore remains TRUE (no new authn surface is introduced — there are no new routes to authenticate). If a future requirement genuinely needs these over HTTP, that is a **separate work item that MUST first introduce a real auth substrate** (and then §8 is corrected to acknowledge a new authn surface + CSRF/origin protection + an audit trail) — it is explicitly out of scope here. A test asserts the maintenance operations are reachable ONLY via the CLI entrypoint and are NOT registered as FastAPI routes (no destructive maintenance path is bound to the public port).

**Responsibilities (each a named operation with a test):**
- **Reset seal state in place (REQ-ROLL-024).** Clear `sealed`/`day_class`/`content_sha256`/`data_generation` for a symbol/interval/date-range (or globally) back to unsealed, WITHOUT deleting `kline_cache` rows — so a corrupt seal generation can be re-derived by re-running `SealBackfillRunner`. Idempotent; bounded/chunked; never touches the SOR rows themselves.
- **Rebuild the manifest from the SOR (REQ-ROLL-025).** Recompute the entire `kline_cache_coverage` seal manifest (classes, sha, counts, first/last ts) from the durable `kline_cache` rows — the authoritative recovery path when the manifest is suspected wrong but the SOR is intact. Uses the SAME seal predicate/frontier code as the runtime loader (REQ-MIG-012).
- **Holistic DR rebuild from Postgres-only (REQ-ROLL-030).** Reconstruct ALL derived state — Parquet/Feather columnar tiers, Arrow/LRU caches, 1m memo, SoA memo, derived-coarse — from the Postgres SOR alone (the columnar dir is disposable by ADR-002). Bumps `sor_data_generation` so every embedded-token artifact self-invalidates and rebuilds (§4.1). The deploy can run this after restoring only Postgres.
- **Provenance enumeration + bulk re-invalidation (REQ-ROLL-032).** Given an `engine_fingerprint`/`content_sha256`/`data_generation` predicate, **enumerate affected `backtest_results`/`backtest_runs`** (e.g. all runs produced under a buggy engine SHA or a since-rewound data generation) and optionally **mark them stale / queue re-run**. This is the "which results are affected by this defect?" query the OBS fingerprints (§4.4) exist to support.
- **`copy-prod-scans` foreign-provenance handling (REQ-ROLL-033).** When scans/coverage are imported from another environment (the existing `copy-prod-scans` tooling), the imported rows are classified **foreign-provenance**: `materialized` flag **reset to false** (no local Parquet exists), seal trusted only as **Postgres-only-sealed** (no columnar open against a file this process did not write — §8.1/§8.2), and `data_generation` re-stamped from the LOCAL `sor_data_generation` (not the source env's). A test imports foreign scans and asserts no columnar file is opened for them and they are not served as locally-materialized.

**Interface.** `async reset_seals(scope)`, `async rebuild_manifest(scope)`, `async dr_rebuild()`, `async enumerate_affected(predicate) -> [run_id]`, `async classify_foreign(import_batch)`. **Safety:** all destructive-capable ops carry the same **DB-identity / read-only-standby guard** as `SealBackfillRunner` (§3.10, §8.5) and run on a direct session-pinned connection under their own advisory lock (disjoint keys, REQ-MIG-027).

**Dependencies.** `SealedManifest`, `KlineCacheService`, Postgres, `sor_data_generation`. Import-isolated from accel/engine modules (lean image, REQ-MIG-029).

---

# 4. Data Architecture

## 4.1 Sealed-manifest columns (table `kline_cache_coverage`, v58)

Net-new columns ADD'd to the existing per-`(symbol,interval,date)` coverage table (current DDL `async_persistence.py:650`, PK `(symbol, interval, date)`). All `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` with constant defaults → catalog-only, **no table rewrite** (PG11+), idempotent. **Precise lock claim (R1-F2, corrected R2-F5):** the guarantee is **"no table REWRITE"**, NOT "no lock" — each `ADD COLUMN` still takes a **momentary `ACCESS EXCLUSIVE`** on the catalog row, which must not race the live scanner's continuous `_update_coverage` upserts (hence the bounded `lock_timeout`+in-boot-retry and the submission-quiesce DRAIN window, §4.4). The "catalog-only / no rewrite" guarantee applies to the `ADD COLUMN` statements ONLY. The partial index (`idx_coverage_unsealed`) is built out-of-band via `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` (§4.4, REQ-MIG-033), and the data-dependent sealing runs in the separate `SealBackfillRunner` (§3.10) — neither is part of the in-transaction additive DDL.

| Column | Type | Default | Meaning |
|--------|------|---------|---------|
| `sealed` | `BOOLEAN NOT NULL` | `false` | Day is fully past the completion frontier AND durably stored + validated. **Immutable once true** (see post-seal mutability contract below). Gap detection = `NOT sealed` within `[start, frontier]`. |
| `day_class` | `SMALLINT NOT NULL` | `0` | Taxonomy enum (REQ-STORE-009): `0=unsealed`, `1=sealed-full`, `2=sealed-short-listing`, `3=sealed-interior-structural-gap`, `4=sealed-empty-negative`, `5=sealed-delist-snapped`, `6=derived-coarse` (REQ-STORE-024, R1-F15 — coarse TF derived from the sealed fine base, NO `fetched_at`/sha/refetch, distinguishable from legacy-fetched coarse). Routes serve-present / serve-empty / PG-fallback / derive-from-fine. **`day_class=3` is NOT terminal when `reverify_pending=true` (R4-F1-batch6):** an ambiguous interior hole seals as class 3 with `reverify_pending=true` and is held WARM until its one-shot post-frontier re-fetch settles it (clear→confirmed structural gap, or re-seal class 1/2 if filled) — only `reverify_pending=false` class-3/4 rows are permanently negative-cached. |
| `gap_count` | `SMALLINT NOT NULL` | `0` | Known-missing bar count for structural-gap/short days, so `row_count == candle_count − gap_count` is assertable on columnar read (REQ-STORE-028). |
| `gap_ranges` | `JSONB NULL` | `NULL` | Queryable known-gap range boundaries (`[{first_open_ts,last_open_ts}]`), not just the scalar `gap_count` (REQ-CACHE-027) — lets the loader skip exactly the negative-cached sub-windows. |
| `reverify_pending` | `BOOLEAN NOT NULL` | `false` | **One-shot post-frontier reverify gate for an ambiguous interior hole (R4-F1-batch6, REQ-MIG-014).** Distinguishes a *complete-but-short* day (mid-day listing / halt → seals terminally, `day_class=2`) from an *ambiguous interior hole* that may be a legacy-bug artifact rather than a true structural gap. An ambiguous interior hole (`day_class=3`) seals **with `gap_count`/`gap_ranges` AND `reverify_pending=true`** instead of going straight to permanent negative-cache; `SealBackfillRunner`/`SealedManifest` give it **exactly one** re-fetch attempt *after* the day crosses the completion frontier, then clear the flag to `false` (the hole is confirmed real → permanent negative-cache) or re-seal `day_class=1/2` if the re-fetch filled it. Prevents the false-permanent-cache failure (a legacy-bug hole sealed-empty forever) the seal model exists to kill. While `reverify_pending=true` the day is treated as **WARM/refetchable**, never as a settled negative-cache. |
| `listing_snapped` | `BOOLEAN NOT NULL` | `false` | Day's first bar snapped to `symbol_lifecycle.listing_time` (REQ-MIG-005/CACHE-026). Persisted as a column (NOT collapsed into `day_class`) so downstream code keyed to `listing_snapped` finds it (R1-F7). |
| `delisted` | `BOOLEAN NOT NULL` | `false` | Day past `symbol_lifecycle.delist_time`; feeds the `sealed-delist-snapped`/`sealed-empty-negative` classes (REQ-STORE-009, R1-F7). |
| `fetched_at` | `TIMESTAMPTZ` (pre-existing `:655`) | — | **Already present** in the coverage DDL; referenced by REQ-MIG-016 TTL-exempt logic — NOT re-added by v58, but listed here so the manifest column model is complete (R1-F7). |
| `content_sha256` | `BYTEA NULL` | `NULL` | Canonical hash over the day's rows (REQ-STORE-003). **Canonical byte format (R1-F4, pinned):** rows sorted ascending by `open_time`; `open_time` serialized as **int64-ms epoch** (exact `TIMESTAMPTZ→epoch-ms` integer conversion — `floor(extract(epoch)*1000)`, asserted exact on the 5m/1m grid, no float drift); OHLCV serialized as **IEEE-754 raw 8-byte little-endian float64** (`struct.pack('<d')`, NOT `str()`); fixed column order `(open_time,open,high,low,close,volume)`. `NULL` = no comparable hash (no integrity check, no refetch — REQ-STORE-004). |
| `sha_version` | `SMALLINT NOT NULL` | `0` | Canonicalization-scheme version; an older-scheme sha reads as "no comparable hash" not "mismatch" (REQ-STORE-004). |
| `manifest_semantics_version` | `SMALLINT NOT NULL` | `1` | **DISTINCT from `sha_version`** (REQ-MIG-005, R1-F7): versions the seal-logic / day-class semantics, so a manifest written under older seal rules is re-derivable without being treated as content drift. |
| `fine_base_generation` | `BIGINT NULL` | `NULL` | For `day_class=6` (derived-coarse): the generation stamp of the sealed fine base it was derived from, so a regenerated fine base **auto-invalidates** stale coarse (REQ-STORE-024, R1-F15). **Compares against the fine row's `data_generation` (below) — that is the generation source the dangling reference needed (R2-F15-batch4).** |
| `data_generation` | `BIGINT NOT NULL` | `0` | **SOR-wide monotonic data-generation token (R2-F9-batch4/R2-F15-batch4, REQ-ROLL-023/CACHE-043/CACHE-044).** Stamped on every fine `kline_cache_coverage` row at write/seal from a single global counter (a row in a new `sor_data_generation` singleton table, bumped on any operation that can rewind the SOR — notably a Postgres PITR/restore hook). It is the fine-side generation that `fine_base_generation` reads to detect a stale coarse derivation, AND the value every DERIVED artifact embeds (see SOR-token paragraph below). |
| `materialized` | `BOOLEAN NOT NULL` | `false` | Parquet partition fsync'd+renamed. **Distinct from `sealed`** (REQ-STORE-027): seal depends only on PG SOR; materialize is best-effort columnar. |
| `first_open_ts` / `last_open_ts` | `BIGINT NULL` | `NULL` | int64-ms epoch bounds of stored rows for the day (single epoch unit — REQ-STORE-040). |
| `sealed_at` | `TIMESTAMPTZ NULL` | `NULL` | Seal provenance (UTC). |

**Why this table (not `backtest_runs`):** coverage is per-symbol-day, which is exactly the seal grain; `backtest_runs` is per-run and would denormalize. (Discovery §9 flagged both as candidates; the seal grain decides it.)

**SOR-wide data-generation token — every derived artifact embeds + validates it (R2-F9-batch4/R2-F15-batch4, REQ-ROLL-023/CACHE-043/CACHE-044).** A single **monotonic generation counter** is the System-of-Record's "data epoch." Source: a new singleton `sor_data_generation(value BIGINT)` row, bumped on any event that can make the SOR disagree with a previously-derived cache — most importantly a **Postgres PITR / restore / failover**. The fine `kline_cache_coverage.data_generation` column carries the token at write/seal. **Every derived/in-process artifact embeds the token it was built from and validates it on read, invalidate+rebuild on mismatch:** Parquet/Feather part-files (in `_manifest.json`), the `_ArrowHotCache`/`_ProcessLRU` entries, the 1m-drill memo, the SoA memo, and the derived-coarse rows (via `fine_base_generation` vs `data_generation`). So a Postgres restore that rewinds kline data **self-invalidates every columnar/in-RAM cache** rather than serving stale derived bytes against a rewound SOR. `fine_base_generation` (derived-coarse) is the special case the schema already had; this generalizes it SOR-wide. A test rewinds the SOR (bumps generation) and asserts every tier rebuilds rather than serving a pre-rewind artifact.

**PITR/restore DETECTION is concrete, not asserted (R3-F6-batch2, REQ-CACHE-043).** The whole self-invalidation chain depends on the singleton actually being BUMPED when the SOR rewinds, so the boot-hook detection mechanism is pinned (an undetected restore that does NOT route through the hook leaves generation unchanged → the §3.10 marker-ahead-of-data guard and every downstream invalidation silently no-op against a rewound SOR):
- **Primary detector — durable DB-identity tuple compared at boot.** At boot the app reads and stamps a durable tuple `{system_identifier (from pg_control / `pg_controldata`), timeline_id (`pg_control_checkpoint().timeline_id`), a control-file digest (latest-checkpoint LSN / redo LSN)}` and compares it to the last-seen tuple persisted in a small `sor_identity` row. **Any change** (a PITR rewinds the timeline / moves the checkpoint LSN backward; a restore onto a clone changes `system_identifier`) ⇒ **bump `sor_data_generation` and force re-evaluation** of seals + cache invalidation. A standby promotion (timeline increment) is likewise detected.
- **Least-privilege handling of the `pg_control_*` grant — named, fail-loud OR observably-degraded, never silent (R4-F9-batch6, REQ-MIG-043/CACHE-043).** The primary detector's `pg_control_system()` / `pg_control_checkpoint()` reads require an **elevated grant** — membership in the `pg_read_all_stats` role (PG10–14) or `pg_read_server_files` / the version-dependent `pg_monitor` super-role, or superuser; the app's least-privilege role may lack it. The required grant is **documented in the deploy contract** (the app role is `GRANT`ed `pg_read_all_stats` so the PITR primary detector functions). On `permission denied for function pg_control_checkpoint` the detector MUST do ONE of (both observable, never a silent no-op): **(a)** fail-loud at boot with the **missing privilege named** (`REQ-MIG-043: PITR primary detector requires pg_read_all_stats — GRANT it or set BT_PITR_DETECTOR=backstop_only`), OR **(b)** explicitly and observably **fall back to the mandatory sampled-integrity backstop** (next bullet) with a logged degrade reason AND a §5.4 status-route flag `pitr_primary_detector=degraded` (so the marker-ahead-of-data guard the seal model depends on is known to be running on the backstop alone, not silently weakened). The choice between (a) and (b) is a documented config (`BT_PITR_DETECTOR=require|backstop_only`); the default is **fail-loud (a)** because the marker-ahead-of-data guard (§3.10) is correctness-critical after a PITR. A **least-privilege-role test** runs the detector under a role lacking `pg_read_all_stats` and asserts it either raises with the privilege named or sets `pitr_primary_detector=degraded` + logs — NEVER silently disables rewind detection.
- **Required backstop — REQ-CACHE-043 sampled integrity check (promoted from "complementing" to MANDATORY).** Independent of the boot hook, a **sampled row-count / `content_sha256` integrity check** over a rolling sample of sealed days runs periodically; on detected drift it **bumps `sor_data_generation` itself** (does not merely warn) so a rewind that somehow evades the boot-identity comparison (e.g. an in-place restore that preserves `system_identifier`+timeline but rewinds data) still triggers invalidation.
- A **restore/rewind test that does NOT manually bump the token** asserts the backstop independently triggers invalidation (proving the system does not depend on a human or an external tool remembering to bump).

**Post-seal mutability contract — precise frozen vs mutable column set (R2-F7-batch2, REQ-MIG-015).** "Immutable once true" applies to the **content** columns, not the whole row — otherwise REQ-MIG-015 (a late `symbol_lifecycle` population reclassifying `listing_snapped` WITHOUT un-sealing or refetching) is unsatisfiable. The contract:
- **FROZEN post-seal** (never mutated once `sealed=true`): `sealed`, `content_sha256`, `sha_version`, `first_open_ts`, `last_open_ts`, `candle_count`, `sealed_at`. A change to any of these requires an explicit **un-seal → re-verify → re-seal + sha recompute** cycle (never a silent UPDATE).
- **MUTABLE post-seal via the documented lifecycle-reclassification path** (owned by `SymbolLifecycleRefresher`, §3.11): `listing_snapped`, `delisted`, `day_class`. These may be UPDATEd when lifecycle data arrives late, **without refetching, un-sealing, or changing `content_sha256`** — the day's *bytes* are unchanged; only its *classification* sharpens. `manifest_semantics_version` bumps to record the reclassification rule version.
- **MUTABLE post-seal via the one-shot reverify path** (owned by `SealBackfillRunner`/`SealedManifest`, §3.10): `reverify_pending` (and, on a reverify that fills the hole, `day_class`/`gap_count`/`gap_ranges`/`content_sha256`/`candle_count` via an explicit **re-seal**, never a silent UPDATE). `reverify_pending` flips `true→false` exactly once after the ambiguous interior-hole day crosses the frontier and its single re-fetch attempt resolves (R4-F1-batch6, REQ-MIG-014). This is the ONE sanctioned exception to "content columns frozen": a reverify that changes bytes goes through the same un-seal→re-verify→re-seal+sha-recompute cycle as any content change; a reverify that confirms the hole only clears the flag and leaves the frozen set byte-unchanged.
- **MUTABLE post-seal via the PITR/DR re-stamp path** (R4-F7-batch6-c5, REQ-CACHE-043/ROLL-023): **`data_generation`** is explicitly classified MUTABLE-post-seal (it was previously in NEITHER set, leaving its behavior undefined). When `sor_data_generation` advances on a PITR/restore/failover (§4.1 boot-identity hook + backstop), the PITR re-stamp path **updates sealed fine rows' `data_generation` in place** so fine and derived-coarse generations re-converge — this does NOT require un-seal/refetch/sha-recompute because the day's **bytes are unchanged**; only the generation token is re-stamped. Resolution of the §4.1 ambiguity: if sealed fine rows kept their original generation while the global counter advanced, the `fine_base_generation == data_generation` comparison (derived-coarse) would **never re-match after a rewind**, forcing perpetual coarse re-derivation; conversely, re-stamping mutates a row the frozen contract would otherwise imply is immutable. The committed behavior: **a PITR re-stamps existing sealed fine rows' `data_generation`** (an in-place generation update, NOT a content change), so derived-coarse re-derives **exactly once** after the rewind and then stops. A **PITR test asserts derived-coarse re-derives exactly once and then stops** (no perpetual mismatch), and that `content_sha256`/`candle_count`/`first/last_open_ts` are byte-unchanged across the re-stamp (the FROZEN set is untouched).
A reclassify-after-late-lifecycle test asserts the frozen set is byte-unchanged (esp. `content_sha256`), no Bybit call fires, and the day stays `sealed` while `day_class`/`listing_snapped`/`delisted` update.

**SOR type mismatch acknowledged (R1-F4).** The three physical representations the hash must reconcile are NOT identical: the Postgres SOR stores `kline_cache.open_time` as `TIMESTAMPTZ` and OHLCV as `DOUBLE PRECISION` (`async_persistence.py:623–628`); the Parquet tier stores int64-ms + double (§4.3); Bybit returns ms-epoch + decimal strings. The canonical hash basis (pinned in the `content_sha256` row above) **normalizes all three to the same bytes** — int64-ms epoch for time, IEEE-754 LE float64 for OHLCV — so an ingest-time hash, a Postgres-read-rebuild hash, and a Parquet-rebuild hash are bit-identical (REQ-STORE-003). A **tri-source hash-equality CI test** (fresh Bybit ingest vs Postgres-read-rebuild vs Parquet-rebuild over the same sealed day) is the gate for REQ-STORE-003; a mismatch there would silently re-introduce the exact false-positive refetch Phase 1 targets, so it fails the build.

## 4.2 Completion frontier (the seal predicate)

```
T               = interval_seconds (5m → 300; 1h → 3600; 4h → 14400)
skew_margin     = range-validated config lag (default 1×T) absorbing clock skew / late bars
frontier(now)   = floor((now_epoch_ms − skew_margin_ms) / (T*1000)) * (T*1000)   # last safely-closed bar's open, int64-ms
frontier        = MONOTONIC RATCHET: persisted max(prev_frontier, computed); a backward clock step NEVER un-seals
day is sealable ⟺  day_end_utc ≤ frontier(now)
                   AND  day within [listing_time, delist_time]    # NULL lifecycle ⇒ [-∞,+∞] ⇒ fetch-everything, never auto-seal-empty (REQ-MIG-009)
                   AND  all stored candles OHLC-valid  AND  durably committed
forming bar     ⟺  open_time ≥ frontier(now)                    # clipped before store (REQ-STORE-006); PG-primary only (REQ-STORE-030)
```
- **Skew-margin + ratchet (R1-F10, REQ-CACHE-006).** The frontier applies an explicit `skew_margin` safety lag (so the live forming edge is never sealed early on clock skew) and is a **monotonic ratchet** read from one authoritative UTC clock — a backward clock step can never un-seal a day. `skew_margin` is a documented, range-validated numeric config.
- **Identical code path runtime ↔ backfill (R1-F4 mig, REQ-MIG-012).** The runtime loader (`SealedManifest.completion_frontier`) and `SealBackfillRunner` call the **same** frontier function, so they can never disagree on the boundary day's class.
- **Lifecycle bound (R1-F5 mig, REQ-MIG-011).** The `[listing_time, delist_time]` clause comes from `symbol_lifecycle`; an absent/NULL row means fetch-everything (never "out of life ⇒ seal known-empty"), so a wrong/empty lifecycle can never permanently negative-cache real data.

All bucketing, frontier math, lifecycle comparisons, and Parquet hive paths are **UTC-only**, zero naive-local/DST leakage on the Windows host; API/MCP `date_range_*` normalized to UTC before window-bounding (REQ-STORE-010).

## 4.3 Parquet/Feather columnar layout (Phase 5)

**Hive layout (REQ-STORE-020):**
```
<COLUMNAR_DIR>/symbol=<SAN(SYM)>/interval=<I>/year=<Y>/month=<M>/part-<NNNN>.parquet  (+ _manifest.json pointer)
```
- `interval` **in** the partition key so fine base, legacy native-coarse, and aux-series (e.g. BTC-vol 1h) never collide (REQ-STORE-020/024).
- **MONTH** granularity (no per-day small-file sprawl — a per-day 5m universe would be ~4,500 tiny files, findings §4.1).
- **Incremental month sealing — multi-part-file append, NOT full-month rewrite (R2-F6-batch4, REQ-STORE-032).** A forming month is sealed **day-by-day** as each UTC day completes, so the layout is **multiple versioned part-files per month** (`part-0000.parquet`, `part-0001.parquet`, …) plus a small `_manifest.json` that lists the live parts + their `content_sha256` + covered day-range. Sealing a newly-complete day **appends a new `part-NNNN.parquet`** and **atomically swaps the manifest pointer** (write `_manifest.json.tmp` → `os.replace` over `_manifest.json`, which is atomic on Windows and POSIX and never renames over an open mmap'd data file — the data parts are immutable-once-written, only the tiny manifest is swapped). This is **O(month) write-amplification, not O(days²)** (a singular `part.parquet` would force a full-month rewrite per seal). The reader UNIONs all parts listed in the manifest (disjoint day-ranges, merge by `open_time`). A **refcount-guarded background compaction** coalesces many small parts into one larger part when no reader holds an mmap handle on the old parts (Windows-safe: never unlink/replace a part that is currently mapped — see §3.1 fd-refcount), then swaps the manifest to point at the compacted part. The §4.3 layout is thus **multi-part-per-month**; "multi-part-file month" in the §3.1 read seams refers to exactly this.
- Rows **sorted by `open_time`** within each part-file; per-column row-group **min/max stats** emitted (asserted via file metadata) with bounded row-group size so a narrow date predicate prunes at sub-file granularity (REQ-STORE-022).
- `SAN(SYM)` = the pinned **reversible** symbol encoding (§3.1: percent/hex `%XX` uppercase, applied AFTER `canon`) so `BTC/USDT`'s `/` cannot spawn nested dirs; read path decodes back to the EXACT original string (REQ-STORE-021).

**Parquet schema (one base granularity only — REQ-STORE-024):**

| Column | Arrow/Parquet type | Notes |
|--------|--------------------|-------|
| `open_time` | `int64` | Bybit-native ms epoch; **never** auto-cast to a timestamp logical type (REQ-STORE-023/040). |
| `open/high/low/close/volume` | `double` (float64) | No Decimal/float32 drift; byte-identical across DuckDB/Polars/pyarrow readers (REQ-STORE-023). |

File/Feather/Arrow artifacts embed a **format/schema version**; an incompatible-older or unknown-newer stamp (both rolling-deploy directions) → invalidate + rebuild from Postgres (REQ-STORE-029). mmap zero-copy additionally validates byte-order/Arrow-schema/arch before use.

**Coarse-TF derivation:** 15m/1h/4h are **DERIVED** from the sealed 5m base via `time_bucket`/`group_by_dynamic`; a coarse bar is sealed iff ALL constituent fine bars are sealed (forming coarse never cached). Derived rows are marked with **`day_class = 6` (derived-coarse)** and carry a **`fine_base_generation` stamp** (§4.1) — so they are distinguishable from legacy-fetched coarse (which keeps its own `day_class`/`fetched_at`/sha) and **auto-invalidate when the fine base regenerates** (generation mismatch ⇒ re-derive); derived rows have no `fetched_at`/sha/refetch (REQ-STORE-024, REQ-SWEEP-004, REQ-MIG-017). Legacy native-coarse rows already present are sealed by their existing PK without re-derivation (REQ-MIG-017).

**Derived-coarse-vs-native-coarse is a CONTRACT-LEVEL parity gate + has an independent rollback lever (R3-F3/R3-F4-batch2, REQ-TEST-030, REQ-ROLL-015).** Substituting a 5m `time_bucket` resample for Bybit's **native** coarse aggregation is a **data-source change** that can decide differently (boundary / last-bar / volume handling are not guaranteed bit-equal), and the 5m-no-drill golden master does NOT cover it. Two protections, both pinned:
1. **Standing equivalence gate (REQ-TEST-030):** for ANY config whose `simulation_interval` is coarse, derived-coarse must equal the legacy native-coarse result — **byte-identical on the Decimal lane (P0–P2) / within the pinned float epsilon (P3+)** — run as a standing gate alongside the 5m golden master (it is also recorded as a Prime-Directive invariant row). This catches a divergence between `time_bucket` and native aggregation at the contract level, not just at intrabar fill.
2. **Independent toggle with a legacy-native fallback (REQ-ROLL-015):** derivation is gated by its OWN central-registry flag **`BT_DERIVE_COARSE`** (the 6th flag, §7.2). Flag **OFF** reverts a 15m/1h/4h backtest to the **legacy native per-interval fetch/load path** (byte-identical klines+trades), so a discovered derivation divergence has a one-flip rollback lever; flag-OFF native-1h byte-identical parity test in §12.3.

**Compression:** decompression-throughput codec (uncompressed/LZ4/zstd-low), never a max-ratio/high-level codec; documented read-MB/s target (REQ-STORE-036).

## 4.4 v58 migration strategy (idempotent, callable, deferred-backfill-safe)

**Placement.** Append `(58, _seal_manifest_v58)` to `_MIGRATIONS` (`async_persistence.py:992`) — **next free int after v57** (`(57, _backfill_open_trade_filled_qty)` `:1522`). Version-int collisions have happened twice before on parallel branches (discovery §9, e.g. the v42 renumber note at `:1436`); claim v58 + coordinate.

**Callable, not string.** The runner splits a string migration on `;` (`async_persistence.py:1633`) — which corrupts multi-statement DDL — but executes a `callable(sql)` directly (`:1630–1631`, type `_MigrationSQL = Union[str, Callable[[Any], Coroutine]]` `:162`). v58 is multi-statement (additive `ADD COLUMN`s across four tables + `symbol_lifecycle` create + status-CHECK relax + index plumbing) → **MUST be a callable** `async def _seal_manifest_v58(conn)` (precedent: `(52, _SCHEMA_V52)` `:1476`, `(42, _SCHEMA_DEBUG_V42)`).

**Boot-safety split (R1-F1, REQ-MIG-018/020/021/022/028 — load-bearing).** The migration runner wraps every callable in a single `conn.transaction()` (`async_persistence.py:1629`) while holding the **session-scoped** `pg_advisory_lock(8675309)` for the *entire* `_run_migrations` loop (acquired `:1607`, released only in `finally`), under `lock_timeout='30s'` (`:1599`). Therefore `schema_version` advances **only after the whole callable commits**, and the global migration lock is held for the callable's full duration. A data-dependent seal backfill (an `UPDATE` over the whole `kline_cache_coverage` population) inside that callable could exceed 30s and/or contend with the live scanner's `_update_coverage` upserts (`kline_cache_service.py:286–318`), abort the boot migration (schema_version NOT bumped), and **block every other booting instance behind the global advisory lock → deploy-time crash-loop**. "Deferrable" and "runs inline at boot" cannot both be true. **Resolution: v58 is sub-second additive DDL ONLY.** All data-dependent sealing is moved to a separate post-migration background `SealBackfillRunner` (§3.10) that runs OUTSIDE the migration transaction and OUTSIDE the global advisory lock, with its own election lock, chunked commits, and bounded `lock_timeout`+retry. The §4.4 callable below contains zero data backfill.

**Additive DDL only (idempotent + crash-safe, sub-second):**
```python
async def _seal_manifest_v58(conn):
    # NOTE: DDL ONLY. No data-dependent backfill runs here (R1-F1). schema_version
    # reaches 58 sub-second; sealing is deferred to SealBackfillRunner (§3.10).
    #
    # _engine_git_sha is imported from the persistence/DDL layer ONLY (R4-F8-batch6,
    # REQ-MIG-029) — a zero-dependency provenance helper colocated with the migration
    # runner, NEVER from an engine/SoA/numba/scanner/columnar module — so a `migrate`
    # on the lean pure-Python image (numba/pyarrow/duckdb force-absent) cannot fail at
    # import. The §783 import-graph test asserts this helper's transitive imports pull
    # in no accel/engine module on the accel-force-absent image.

    # 0. FAIL-LOUD pre-flight introspection BEFORE any ALTER (R4-F7-batch6,
    #    REQ-MIG-007/008). `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` SILENTLY keeps a pre-existing
    #    wrong-typed column (e.g. a hand-added first_open_ts INT4 that would overflow
    #    epoch-ms per REQ-MIG-006), and the additive columns assume the coverage PK is
    #    exactly (symbol,interval,date). Both are asserted in-callable, not only in prose.
    pk = await conn.fetch(
        "SELECT a.attname FROM pg_index i "
        "JOIN pg_attribute a ON a.attrelid=i.indrelid AND a.attnum=ANY(i.indkey) "
        "WHERE i.indrelid='kline_cache_coverage'::regclass AND i.indisprimary "
        "ORDER BY array_position(i.indkey, a.attnum)")
    if [r['attname'] for r in pk] != ['symbol', 'interval', 'date']:
        raise RuntimeError(f"REQ-MIG-007: kline_cache_coverage PK is {[r['attname'] for r in pk]}, "
                           "expected (symbol,interval,date) — refusing to add manifest columns")
    # per-target-column type-compat probe: fail-loud on a pre-existing incompatible
    # type/width rather than letting ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS silently keep it (REQ-MIG-008).
    _EXPECTED = {  # column -> acceptable information_schema.data_type set
        'first_open_ts': {'bigint'}, 'last_open_ts': {'bigint'},
        'data_generation': {'bigint'}, 'fine_base_generation': {'bigint'},
        'day_class': {'smallint'}, 'gap_count': {'smallint'},
        'content_sha256': {'bytea'}, 'sealed': {'boolean'}}
    existing = {r['column_name']: r['data_type'] for r in await conn.fetch(
        "SELECT column_name, data_type FROM information_schema.columns "
        "WHERE table_name='kline_cache_coverage'")}
    for col, ok in _EXPECTED.items():
        if col in existing and existing[col] not in ok:
            raise RuntimeError(f"REQ-MIG-008: kline_cache_coverage.{col} pre-exists as "
                               f"{existing[col]!r}, incompatible with {ok} — refusing to proceed")

    # Retry helper: each live-shared catalog ALTER (steps 1 + 5) is bracketed in its
    # OWN SAVEPOINT under a short lock_timeout with a bounded retry/backoff loop
    # (R4-F2-batch6 / R2-F5 / R3-F4-batch4, REQ-MIG-020/030). SAVEPOINT is the PINNED
    # scope (NOT out-of-txn autocommit): the runner already opened conn.transaction()
    # and holds pg_advisory_lock(8675309) on THIS conn, so an autocommit ADD COLUMN
    # would need a SECOND connection and would forfeit the "failure leaves
    # schema_version unchanged, no partial DDL" atomicity (REQ-MIG-020). A SAVEPOINT
    # rolls back ONLY the conflicting statement, preserving whole-callable atomicity,
    # and every statement is additive+idempotent (IF NOT EXISTS) so a retried ALTER is
    # safe. NOTE: each ADD COLUMN's momentary ACCESS EXCLUSIVE is held to the outer
    # commit (savepoints do NOT release it early); the lock window is kept short
    # because the whole callable is sub-second catalog-only DDL AND the scanner's
    # coverage writes are gated for the window by the §4.4 quiesce (R4-F3-batch6).
    async def _alter_with_retry(stmt, attempts=5):
        delay = 0.5
        for i in range(attempts):
            try:
                await conn.execute("SAVEPOINT v58_alter")
                await conn.execute("SET LOCAL lock_timeout = '3s'")  # before step-1, not only step-5
                await conn.execute(stmt)
                await conn.execute("RELEASE SAVEPOINT v58_alter")
                return
            except asyncpg.exceptions.LockNotAvailableError:
                await conn.execute("ROLLBACK TO SAVEPOINT v58_alter")
                if i == attempts - 1:
                    raise
                await asyncio.sleep(delay); delay = min(delay * 2, 8.0)

    # 1. additive manifest columns on kline_cache_coverage — catalog-only,
    #    constant defaults, NO table rewrite (PG11+), idempotent. Run via the
    #    savepoint-retry helper because this is the live-scanner-written table.
    await _alter_with_retry("ALTER TABLE kline_cache_coverage "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS sealed BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS day_class SMALLINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS gap_count SMALLINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS gap_ranges JSONB, "          # queryable gap boundaries (REQ-CACHE-027)
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS reverify_pending BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false, "  # one-shot post-frontier reverify gate for ambiguous interior holes (R4-F1-batch6, REQ-MIG-014)
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS listing_snapped BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS delisted BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS content_sha256 BYTEA, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS sha_version SMALLINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS manifest_semantics_version SMALLINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 1, "  # DISTINCT from sha_version (REQ-MIG-005)
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS materialized BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT false, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS fine_base_generation BIGINT, "  # derived-coarse auto-invalidation stamp (REQ-STORE-024)
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS data_generation BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, "  # SOR-wide PITR-rewind token, stamped at seal (R3-F1-batch5/R3-F2-batch3, REQ-ROLL-023/CACHE-043)
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS first_open_ts BIGINT, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS last_open_ts BIGINT, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS sealed_at TIMESTAMPTZ")
        # NOTE: fetched_at already exists in the coverage DDL (:655) — referenced, not re-added.

    # 2. symbol lifecycle table (REQ-MIG-009/011) — NULL/absent row ⇒ fetch-everything,
    #    NEVER 'out of life ⇒ seal known-empty'. Created idempotently; populated by a
    #    background refresh (operator-override-preserving), NOT inline.
    await conn.execute("CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS symbol_lifecycle ("
        "symbol TEXT PRIMARY KEY, listing_time TIMESTAMPTZ, delist_time TIMESTAMPTZ, "
        "source TEXT, updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now())")

    # 3. persisted backfill-completion marker (REQ-MIG-021/022, REQ-OBS-035/038/039) —
    #    the SOLE gate for 'cache-complete/fully-optimized' + the optimize-enable rollout gate.
    await conn.execute("CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS seal_backfill_marker ("
        "id SMALLINT PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT 1 CHECK (id = 1), "
        "state TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'not_started' "          # not_started|in_progress|complete|complete_with_skips
        "  CHECK (state IN ('not_started','in_progress','complete','complete_with_skips')), "
        "days_total BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, days_sealed BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, "
        "data_generation BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, "        # PITR-rewind compare value, written on flip-to-complete (R3-F3-batch3, REQ-MIG-026)
        "skipped JSONB, engine_sha TEXT, updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now())")
    await conn.execute("INSERT INTO seal_backfill_marker (id) VALUES (1) "
        "ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING")

    # 2b. SOR-wide data-generation singleton + DB-identity row (R3-F1-batch5, REQ-ROLL-023/
    #     CACHE-043). The monotonic 'data epoch' every derived artifact embeds + validates;
    #     bumped on PITR/restore/failover (boot-identity hook + sampled-integrity backstop, §4.1).
    await conn.execute("CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sor_data_generation ("
        "id SMALLINT PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT 1 CHECK (id = 1), value BIGINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0)")
    await conn.execute("INSERT INTO sor_data_generation (id) VALUES (1) "
        "ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING")
    await conn.execute("CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sor_identity ("        # last-seen DB-identity tuple (boot PITR detector, §4.1)
        "id SMALLINT PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT 1 CHECK (id = 1), "
        "system_identifier TEXT, timeline_id INTEGER, control_digest TEXT, "
        "updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now())")
    await conn.execute("INSERT INTO sor_identity (id) VALUES (1) "
        "ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING")

    # 3c. flag/config control + audit tables — CREATED HERE, BEFORE step 4b (R5-F1, CRITICAL —
    #     STATEMENT-ORDERING SAFETY). step 4b's deferred-marker INSERT targets bt_flag_config,
    #     and this callable executes top-to-bottom in ONE transaction. On any DB where
    #     mcp_sweep_results lacks the (sweep_id,config_hash) UNIQUE index (`_uc is None` — TRUE
    #     on a fresh 0→58 DB and on any 57→58 upgrade that never had it), step 4b would INSERT
    #     into a not-yet-created bt_flag_config → `relation "bt_flag_config" does not exist` →
    #     the WHOLE v58 txn aborts → schema_version stuck at 57 → every booting instance
    #     crash-loops behind pg_advisory_lock(8675309). That is the EXACT boot-crash-loop hazard
    #     the boot-safety split exists to kill, so the CREATEs are hoisted above every INSERT
    #     that references them. (Both tables were formerly created in step 8; moved up. They
    #     remain additive, catalog-only, sub-second, idempotent — IF NOT EXISTS.) See the step-8
    #     back-reference comment and the 0→58 ordering meta-test (below) that seeds an
    #     index-less mcp_sweep_results to exercise the `_uc is None` branch in CI, not prod boot.
    await conn.execute("CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bt_flag_audit ("
        "id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY, flag_name TEXT NOT NULL, effective_value TEXT NOT NULL, "
        "resolved_reason TEXT, engine_sha TEXT, applied_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now())")
    await conn.execute("CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS bt_flag_config ("    # DB-backed flag control surface (R3-F1-batch4, REQ-ROLL-003)
        "flag_name TEXT PRIMARY KEY, value TEXT NOT NULL, updated_by TEXT, "
        "updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now())")

    # 4. additive OBS provenance/timing/kernel/fingerprint columns on the run tables
    #    (REQ-OBS-001/003/004/009/010/036, REQ-MIG-037/038) — all nullable / constant-default.
    #    LIVE-WRITTEN TABLES → SAVEPOINT-retry (R5-F2, High — contradiction fix). backtest_runs is
    #    CONTINUOUSLY written by the live BacktestService during a rolling deploy (status upserts on
    #    in-flight runs), so its momentary ACCESS EXCLUSIVE ADD COLUMN MUST go through
    #    _alter_with_retry (SAVEPOINT + bounded retry + SET LOCAL lock_timeout='3s'), NOT a bare
    #    `await conn.execute` under the default 30s with no retry. The pinned R4-F2-batch6 txn-scope
    #    decision (§4.4 prose below) requires the live-shared ADD COLUMNs on BOTH
    #    kline_cache_coverage AND backtest_runs to be bracketed this way; a bare unwrapped ALTER
    #    here could time out, abort all of v58 (no savepoint to roll back to), and crash-loop the
    #    deploy — the precise failure that decision removes. backtest_results (written by each run's
    #    _persist_results) and mcp_sweep_results (written by every sweep persist) are likewise
    #    live-written, so they ALSO route through _alter_with_retry. A lock-contention test holds a
    #    ROW EXCLUSIVE on backtest_runs during v58 and asserts the ADD COLUMN retries-and-succeeds
    #    rather than aborting (REQ-MIG-020/030).
    await _alter_with_retry("ALTER TABLE backtest_runs "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS engine_fingerprint TEXT, "      # engine git-SHA + flag set
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS numeric_kernel TEXT, "          # 'pure_python'|'numba'|'fastpath'
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS data_provenance TEXT, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS signal_provenance TEXT, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS stage_timings JSONB, "          # per-stage ms (incl. terminal-on-timeout, R1-F19); versioned blob — carries a `schema_version` key + registry-named timer keys (R2-F13-batch5)
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS peak_rss_bytes BIGINT, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS peak_open_positions SMALLINT, "  # max simultaneous open-book depth (peak P) for PreflightEstimator B-calibration + deep-book-vs-high-turnover diagnosis (R4-F4-batch6-c3, REQ-OBS-009)
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS turnover BIGINT")
    await _alter_with_retry("ALTER TABLE backtest_results "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS engine_fingerprint TEXT, "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS equity_curve_manifest_hash BYTEA, "   # frozen hash over the FULL stored equity_curve JSONB (R4-F12-batch6-c2, REQ-FE-003/015)
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS manifest_hash_version SMALLINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 1, "  # version tag for the hash/serialization scheme; old-version hashes re-validate by recompute-under-old-scheme (REQ-FE-015)
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS data_quality_counters JSONB")    # versioned blob — `schema_version` key + registry-named counter keys; status route §5.4 parses the versioned contract (R2-F13-batch5)
    # CRITICAL TABLE NAME (R2-F1): the real sweep table is `mcp_sweep_results`
    # (created by migration v43, async_persistence.py:897; all writers in
    # sweep_repo.py:130/184/195). There is NO table named `sweep_results` —
    # `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` does NOT guard a missing TABLE, so a wrong name
    # raises `relation "sweep_results" does not exist`, aborts the whole v58 txn,
    # leaves schema_version at 57, and (because the global advisory lock is held
    # across the loop) crash-loops EVERY booting instance — the exact hazard the
    # boot-safety split exists to kill. Must be `mcp_sweep_results`.
    await _alter_with_retry("ALTER TABLE mcp_sweep_results "
        "ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS engine_fingerprint TEXT")      # generation guard for resume-merge (REQ-ROLL-017)
    # 4b. ON-CONFLICT target guard (R4-F4-batch6-c2, REQ-SWEEP-012/013). Crash-resume +
    #     idempotent per-combo writes use `ON CONFLICT(sweep_id, config_hash)` — which
    #     REQUIRES a UNIQUE constraint/index on exactly those columns. If absent, every
    #     sweep persist raises "no unique or exclusion constraint matching ON CONFLICT".
    #     FAIL-LOUD here if it is missing rather than discovering it at first sweep — but
    #     do NOT build it inside this txn: a UNIQUE-index build over a POPULATED
    #     mcp_sweep_results is NOT the sub-second catalog-only additive DDL the
    #     boot-safety split guarantees (it scans/validates and can violate on existing
    #     dup rows). Building it is delegated to SealBackfillRunner startup (out-of-band,
    #     CONCURRENTLY, with a dedup pre-pass) — same discipline as idx_coverage_unsealed.
    _uc = await conn.fetchval(
        "SELECT 1 FROM pg_indexes WHERE tablename='mcp_sweep_results' "
        "AND indexdef ILIKE '%UNIQUE%' AND indexdef ILIKE '%sweep_id%' "
        "AND indexdef ILIKE '%config_hash%' LIMIT 1")
    if _uc is None:
        # Not fatal to v58 (additive DDL still completes); record a deferred-build marker
        # the SealBackfillRunner reads, and let the migration-completeness meta-test assert
        # the constraint is present-or-scheduled. The out-of-band builder runs:
        #   CREATE UNIQUE INDEX CONCURRENTLY IF NOT EXISTS uq_mcp_sweep_results_sweepcfg
        #     ON mcp_sweep_results(sweep_id, config_hash)   -- after a dedup pre-pass
        await conn.execute("INSERT INTO bt_flag_config(flag_name, value) "
            "VALUES('deferred_unique_mcp_sweep_results','pending') "
            "ON CONFLICT(flag_name) DO NOTHING")

    # 5. relax the backtest_runs.status CHECK to admit new terminal states
    #    (REQ-MIG-038, REQ-API-016/020). SHIP THE CONSTRAINT `NOT VALID` ONLY
    #    (R2-F4/F8/F2-dup): a `NOT VALID` CHECK still FULLY enforces on every new
    #    INSERT/UPDATE; the new enum is a strict SUPERSET of the old one, so every
    #    existing row already conforms and VALIDATE can never fail. The expensive
    #    `VALIDATE CONSTRAINT` (a full SHARE-UPDATE-EXCLUSIVE seq-scan of
    #    backtest_runs whose cost scales with row count) is DELIBERATELY NOT run
    #    inside this txn: doing so under the global pg_advisory_lock(8675309) would
    #    re-couple a data-dependent scan to the boot path and reintroduce the
    #    deploy crash-loop on a large backtest_runs. lock_timeout bounds only the
    #    WAIT for the brief catalog-only DROP/ADD, not any scan.
    # The DROP/ADD CONSTRAINT pair takes ACCESS EXCLUSIVE on the live-written
    # backtest_runs table, so it ALSO runs through the savepoint-retry helper
    # (R4-F2-batch6) — not a bare execute under the default 30s.
    await _alter_with_retry("ALTER TABLE backtest_runs DROP CONSTRAINT IF EXISTS backtest_runs_status_check")
    await _alter_with_retry("ALTER TABLE backtest_runs ADD CONSTRAINT backtest_runs_status_check "
        "CHECK (status IN ('pending','queued','running','completed','failed',"
        "'cancelled','interrupted_by_restart','failed_with_timeout')) NOT VALID")
    # NO `VALIDATE CONSTRAINT` here. If a *validated* (not just enforced) constraint
    # is ever genuinely required, VALIDATE runs OUT-OF-BAND in SealBackfillRunner
    # (§3.10) in its OWN short transaction — it needs only SHARE UPDATE EXCLUSIVE,
    # NOT the global migration lock — with bounded lock_timeout + retry, exactly
    # like idx_coverage_unsealed (§4.4 below). A test boots a second instance while
    # a long VALIDATE runs and asserts no crash-loop (REQ-MIG-030).
    #
    # mcp_sweep_jobs.status (a DIFFERENT enum, async_persistence.py:865 — no 'pending',
    # uses 'interrupted' NOT 'interrupted_by_restart') is NOT relaxed here by default:
    # the boot reconcile (§3.6) writes each table's OWN terminal vocabulary (sweep→
    # 'interrupted', backtest→'interrupted_by_restart'), so no superset is needed
    # (R3-F1-batch3). If a future reconcile must write a UNIFORM terminal value across
    # both tables, add a matching `mcp_sweep_jobs` status-CHECK relax here (NOT VALID,
    # superset) + meta-test; otherwise the per-table mapping is the committed default.

    # 6. widen the partial index predicate to cover every in-flight status the boot
    #    reconcile/admission path queries (R2-F10). The existing
    #    idx_backtest_runs_status (:676-678) is `WHERE status IN ('pending','running')`
    #    — it silently EXCLUDES the new live `queued` state, so a reconcile/admission
    #    query filtering on `queued` would seq-scan backtest_runs. The index REBUILD
    #    itself is NOT done here (a plain CREATE/DROP INDEX takes ACCESS EXCLUSIVE);
    #    it is rebuilt out-of-band CONCURRENTLY (below) to the predicate
    #    `WHERE status IN ('pending','queued','running')`, consistent with the
    #    same lock discipline as idx_coverage_unsealed.

    # 7. the partial index for the hot 'unsealed days in range' query is NOT built here —
    #    a non-concurrent CREATE INDEX takes ACCESS EXCLUSIVE on the live coverage table and
    #    CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY is illegal inside this transaction. Built out-of-band (below).

    # 8. durable flag/config control + audit tables — NOW CREATED EARLIER, in step 3c
    #    (R5-F1, moved ABOVE step 4b so the deferred-marker INSERT cannot hit a
    #    not-yet-created bt_flag_config). This step retains ONLY the seeding contract
    #    note (R2-F37/R3-F4-batch3 + R4-F7-batch6-c3, REQ-MIG-037, REQ-CFG-008): v58
    #    CREATEs the tables ONLY (in step 3c); SEEDING (one row per registered flag at its
    #    documented SAFE default) is performed by CapabilityResolver at BOOT, NOT by v58 —
    #    the flag registry is not available at the DDL layer, and bt_flag_audit is
    #    append-only (BIGSERIAL PK, no idempotent conflict target). Per REQ-CFG-008 an
    #    ABSENT bt_flag_config row resolves to the safe default, so the tables coming up
    #    empty post-v58 is correct, not catastrophic; CapabilityResolver populates
    #    bt_flag_config via `INSERT … ON CONFLICT(flag_name) DO NOTHING` on first boot and
    #    appends a bt_flag_audit snapshot per boot/flip. The migration-completeness meta-test
    #    asserts both tables EXIST (created in 3c) AND are POPULATED after first boot
    #    (REQ-OBS-044-style). bt_flag_config is the DB-backed flag/config STORE (REQ-ROLL-003,
    #    §7.2) source of truth; bt_flag_audit remains the append-only audit log distinct from
    #    the control surface. (No CREATE statements here — see step 3c.)

    # 9. durable per-migration provenance (R2-F43/R3-F4-batch3, REQ-MIG-043) — idempotent
    #    INSERT (no duplicate row on re-run). Created by the same additive DDL.
    #    _engine_git_sha() MUST BE TOTAL/INFALLIBLE AT CALL TIME (R5-F5, High — boot-crash-loop
    #    fix). It is called INSIDE the v58 txn; if it shelled to `git rev-parse` on a
    #    stripped/exported prod deploy (no .git, git binary absent) or read a missing embedded
    #    VERSION and raised, the uncaught exception would abort the v58 txn → schema_version
    #    stuck at 57 → pg_advisory_lock(8675309) held across the loop → every booting instance
    #    crash-loops. That is the EXACT hazard the boot-safety split exists to kill, reintroduced
    #    by a provenance lookup. Therefore the helper is pinned to:
    #      (a) PREFER a build-time-stamped constant (embedded at package/build time) over a
    #          runtime `git` subprocess, so prod deploys without git/.git still succeed; and
    #      (b) wrap ALL lookups in try/except returning the sentinel 'unknown' on ANY failure
    #          (FileNotFoundError/CalledProcessError/OSError/anything) — NEVER raise into the
    #          migration txn. Reference shape:
    #              def _engine_git_sha() -> str:
    #                  try:
    #                      return _BUILD_STAMPED_SHA            # build-time constant if present
    #                  except NameError:
    #                      pass
    #                  try:
    #                      return subprocess.check_output(['git','rev-parse','HEAD'],
    #                                 stderr=subprocess.DEVNULL, timeout=2).decode().strip() or 'unknown'
```
