```python
    #                  except Exception:
    #                      return 'unknown'
    #    A test runs v58 with the git binary absent AND .git removed and asserts schema_version
    #    REACHES 58 with the log row recording the 'unknown' sentinel (NOT a crash-loop).
    await conn.execute("CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS schema_migration_log ("
        "version INTEGER PRIMARY KEY, applied_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(), git_sha TEXT)")
    await conn.execute("INSERT INTO schema_migration_log (version, git_sha) VALUES (58, $1) "
        "ON CONFLICT (version) DO NOTHING", _engine_git_sha())
```
- **Index built out-of-band, CONCURRENTLY — column order driven by the real query shape (R1-F2 + R3-F6-batch3, REQ-MIG-033/034).** The unsealed-days partial index is **NOT** created inside the migration transaction: a plain `CREATE INDEX` takes `ACCESS EXCLUSIVE` on the scanner-written coverage table, and `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` is **illegal inside a transaction block**. It is built by a separate non-transactional maintenance step (owned by `SealBackfillRunner` startup, §3.10) using `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY IF NOT EXISTS`, with **self-heal** (interrupted CIC `indisvalid=false` → DROP+rebuild before use) and `ANALYZE kline_cache_coverage` after a successful build. **ANALYZE must ALSO run AFTER the bulk seal-backfill completes, not only post-build (R4-F5-batch6, REQ-MIG-034):** the post-build ANALYZE captures the **pre-backfill** distribution where `WHERE NOT sealed` matches ~100% of rows; the bulk seal `UPDATE` then flips rows to ~0% NOT sealed, so the `idx_coverage_unsealed` partial-index selectivity stats are **stale and wrong** — the planner still estimates `NOT sealed` as common and can seq-scan the exact `unsealed_days` query the index exists to serve. Therefore a **second `ANALYZE kline_cache_coverage` runs after the backfill marker flips to `complete`/`complete_with_skips`** (the mostly-sealed steady state), plus a **bounded `VACUUM (ANALYZE) kline_cache_coverage`** to cap the dead-tuple footprint the chunked seal `UPDATE`s churn (each chunk rewrites rows; without a bounded VACUUM the table bloats and the partial index degrades). The `EXPLAIN`-uses-index gate (REQ-MIG-034) is asserted against the **post-backfill mostly-sealed row distribution**, NOT a freshly-built empty table — a pre-backfill EXPLAIN would pass on stats that no longer hold once rows seal. **Column order corrected (R3-F6-batch3):** the dominant access pattern is **universe-wide** — "unsealed days in `[start, min(end,frontier)]` across MANY symbols" (§3.2) — and §3.10 itself concedes the PK `(symbol,interval,date)` "does not serve a multi-symbol `NOT sealed`+range scan well." Leading the index with `symbol` (mirroring the PK) forces a per-symbol seek for a date-range-driven, all-symbols scan. The index is therefore built to serve the **range/equality-bounded columns first**: `idx_coverage_unsealed ON kline_cache_coverage(interval, date) WHERE NOT sealed` (or a `(date) WHERE NOT sealed` variant) — chosen from the actual `unsealed_days` query, not the PK order. The `EXPLAIN`-uses-index assertion (REQ-MIG-034) runs the **real multi-symbol universe-wide unsealed-range query**, not a single-symbol probe. The §4.1/ADR "no rewrite / catalog-only" claim is **scoped to the `ADD COLUMN` statements only**; the index is explicitly an out-of-band concurrent build.
- **`idx_backtest_runs_status` partial predicate widened the same way (R2-F10 + R3-F8-batch3, REQ-API-016/020).** The existing partial index `idx_backtest_runs_status … WHERE status IN ('pending','running')` (`async_persistence.py:676-678`) does **not** cover the new live `queued` state, so the boot reconcile/admission query — which sweeps the exact in-flight set `status IN ('pending','queued','running')` to terminal-or-requeued (§3.6/§5.4) — would **seq-scan** `backtest_runs` instead of using the index. The index is rebuilt OUT-OF-BAND (same maintenance step as `idx_coverage_unsealed`, owned by `SealBackfillRunner` startup), never inside the v58 txn and never under the global advisory lock. **Rebuild order is CREATE-new-THEN-DROP-old, never DROP-then-CREATE (R3-F8-batch3):** because `CONCURRENTLY` cannot run in a transaction, a `DROP INDEX CONCURRENTLY` + `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` pair is two non-atomic statements with a window of **NO status index** between them (the boot reconcile/admission query seq-scans), and a runner crash after the DROP leaves the table with no status index at all. So: **(1)** `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` the widened index under a NEW name (`idx_backtest_runs_status_v2`, predicate `WHERE status IN ('pending','queued','running')`); **(2)** verify `indisvalid=true`; **(3)** `DROP INDEX CONCURRENTLY` the old `idx_backtest_runs_status` (and rename the new to the canonical name if desired). This never leaves a no-index window. The **self-heal** is extended to detect BOTH an interrupted CIC (`indisvalid=false` → drop+rebuild) AND an "expected status index entirely absent" state (rebuild before use). The reconcile query's exact status set is pinned to `('pending','queued','running')` and an `EXPLAIN` assertion confirms it is index-backed (REQ-MIG-034).
- **The seal backfill is a separate, deferred, chunked background task — not part of v58 (R1-F1/F3, REQ-MIG-020/030/031/032/036).** `SealBackfillRunner` (§3.10) seals historical days in **separately-committed chunks** (per-symbol-month batches), each under a short `SET LOCAL lock_timeout` with retry/backoff and optional `SKIP LOCKED`, so it never deadlocks or long-blocks the live scanner's `_update_coverage` upserts on the shared `kline_cache_coverage` table; it recomputes the completion frontier per chunk (REQ-MIG-012), throttles on replica-lag/WAL pressure (REQ-MIG-036), supports a DRAIN/QUIESCE pause (REQ-MIG-032), is fully resumable from the marker, and updates `seal_backfill_marker` (→ `complete`/`complete_with_skips`). Runtime treats unsealed rows as refetchable until the marker reads `complete`.
- **Backfill seal predicate is frontier+lifecycle, NOT count-vs-expected (R1-F4, REQ-MIG-011/013).** The seal rule is the **same code path** the runtime loader uses (REQ-MIG-012): a day seals ⟺ `day_end_utc ≤ completion_frontier` **AND** the day lies within `[listing_time, delist_time]` (NULL lifecycle ⇒ `listing=-∞`, `delist=+∞` ⇒ fetch-everything, never auto-seal-empty — REQ-MIG-009) **AND** a coverage row exists, with `day_class` derived from a single `GROUP BY` over the **actual** `kline_cache` rows (short-listing / interior-structural-gap / empty-negative / delist-snapped). The legacy `candle_count >= expected` gate is **removed** — it is exactly the count-based logic ADR-003 exists to kill, and would leave legitimately-short historical days (mid-day listing, halt/outage) perpetually unsealed and re-probed every rerun (the original bug surviving the migration). Pre-listing days never falsely seal-empty; short-but-complete days seal.
- **DDL completeness is enforced against LIVE introspection by REAL table name (R1-F2/F6 dup, R2-F1, R3-F4-batch3/R3-F1-batch5, REQ-MIG-037/038, REQ-OBS-044).** A migration-completeness meta-test enumerates every net-new column on `kline_cache_coverage` (**including `data_generation`** — R3-F1-batch5)/`symbol_lifecycle`/`seal_backfill_marker` (**including its `data_generation` column** — R3-F3-batch3)/`backtest_runs`/`backtest_results`/**`mcp_sweep_results`**, **AND every net-new TABLE** (`sor_data_generation`, `sor_identity`, `bt_flag_audit`, `bt_flag_config`, `schema_migration_log` — R3-F4-batch3/R3-F1-batch5, previously absent from the callable so the meta-test could not catch their omission), and asserts each exists post-v58. **Crucially the test resolves each `ALTER`/`CREATE` target against the live catalog (`information_schema`/`pg_class`) by its REAL name BEFORE merge** — so a mis-named or omitted object (e.g. the `sweep_results`-vs-`mcp_sweep_results` trap, or a missing `bt_flag_audit`) fails CI rather than prod boot, where `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` does NOT guard a missing relation. A migration-completeness **meta-test also asserts the target RELATION EXISTS (not merely the column)** before each ALTER, and a fresh-DB `0→58` test actually exercises every new ALTER/CREATE so a wrong/omitted name is caught in CI. A post-migration **canary** asserts the additive columns are actually *populated* (not merely present) once a run has executed (REQ-OBS-044). New-status writes (`queued`, `interrupted_by_restart`, …) are gated on `schema_version>=58` so a deploy that emits a new status before the constraint relaxes cannot fail INSERTs (REQ-MIG-038).
- **Statement-ordering meta-test exercises the `_uc is None` branch (R5-F1, CRITICAL — boot-crash-loop regression guard).** The fresh-DB `0→58` test does NOT merely run the happy path: it explicitly **seeds a `mcp_sweep_results` with NO `(sweep_id,config_hash)` UNIQUE index** so step 4b's `else`-branch (the `bt_flag_config` deferred-marker INSERT) actually fires during the migration, asserting v58 reaches `schema_version=58` WITHOUT a `relation "bt_flag_config" does not exist` abort. This is the standing CI guard that the CREATE-before-INSERT ordering (step 3c above step 4b) is never re-broken by a future re-ordering edit — it must fail in CI, not at prod boot. A companion assertion confirms `bt_flag_config` holds the `deferred_unique_mcp_sweep_results='pending'` row after the index-less `0→58` run. The same test runs the index-PRESENT branch (step 4b is a no-op) to cover both arms.
- **Backfill is idempotent + deferrable.** Re-running seals the same rows; a fresh DB (0→58) applies the identical DDL and starts the marker at `not_started`, yielding a schema byte-identical to an in-place 57→58 upgrade (REQ-MIG-040). During rollout the **pre-flight estimator treats SOR-present-but-unsealed days as WARM** so a feasible warm run is never spuriously rejected before the backfill completes (REQ-PERF-038).
- **Partition hazard — REPORT is not enough; the default partition must be RECONCILED (R2-F6/R2-F7, REQ-STORE-001, REQ-MIG-035).** A sealed range >6mo old may live in `kline_cache_default` (monthly partitions only span ±6mo from migration-38 time — `async_persistence.py:636–646`). The naive claim that "`store_klines` auto-creates partitions on write satisfies REQ-STORE-001" is **false when default-partition rows already exist for the target month** (the normal case for a >6mo backtest written before the partition existed): `CREATE TABLE … PARTITION OF kline_cache FOR VALUES FROM … TO …` for that month then FAILS with *"default partition contains rows that would violate"*, `_ensure_partition_exists` swallows the error (`kline_cache_service.py:341–346`), and the INSERT falls back into `kline_cache_default` **again** — the default never drains, REQ-STORE-001 is violated, and the seal/columnar layout must read from the unpruned default. The actual remediation is a bounded maintenance routine (owned by `MaintenanceAdmin` §3.12 — **NOT** `SealBackfillRunner`, see the MIG-019 scoping note next): for each month with rows in `kline_cache_default`, **(1)** `CREATE` the monthly partition as a standalone table, **(2)** move the default's rows for that month into it (move-out-of-default → create → re-insert/`ATTACH PARTITION`), **(3)** verify the default is empty for that month. A test asserts a >6mo write lands in its month partition with `kline_cache_default` empty **even when the default already held rows for that month**.
- **Partition reconciliation is a SEPARATE maintenance task, NOT the seal pass — MIG-019 no-mutation is scoped to sealing only (R5-F9-batch4, Medium).** MIG-019 mandates the **seal backfill** mutate ONLY `kline_cache_coverage`/`symbol_lifecycle` and NEVER insert/update/delete any `kline_cache` candle row (byte-identical content diff before/after). But default-partition reconciliation (move `kline_cache_default` rows into monthly partitions) is by construction a **DELETE+INSERT of `kline_cache` rows** — so it CANNOT live in `SealBackfillRunner` without contradicting MIG-019's own no-mutation invariant. **Resolution:** partition reconciliation is owned by `MaintenanceAdmin` (§3.12) as its OWN task with its OWN **content-hash before/after validation** (the moved rows are a physical relocation that MUST preserve row content byte-for-byte — same `(symbol,interval,open_time,o,h,l,c,v,...)` tuples, only the physical partition changes), gated by its own test. MIG-019's "no `kline_cache` mutation" guarantee is **scoped to the seal pass** (SealBackfillRunner), and the architecture documents that partition moves are physical relocations preserving content, performed out-of-band by MaintenanceAdmin with a per-row content-hash equality assertion (no candle value may change across the move). A test asserts the seal pass touches zero `kline_cache` rows (MIG-019) AND the MaintenanceAdmin partition move preserves every row's content hash.
- **Partition-tree integrity pre-flight (R2-F35, REQ-MIG-035).** Before any v58 DDL / backfill, validate the `kline_cache` partition tree: parent exists, the migration-38 monthly RANGE scheme is intact, **no gaps/overlaps between monthly bounds**, and the default partition is present. A broken layout **fails fast** (schema_version unchanged, actionable message) rather than letting the seal/read path silently mis-route. Tests: partition-gap-refusal and default-reconciliation (REQ-MIG-035).
- **Pre-DDL resource + blocker checks (R2-F42/R2-F22 dup, REQ-MIG-042).** The dry-run/pre-flight gate covers partition + lifecycle gaps, but REQ-MIG-042 additionally mandates, before any DDL/backfill, a **resource/blocker sweep** (owned by `PreflightEstimator`/the migration runner): **(a)** sufficient Postgres **disk/WAL headroom** for the DDL + partition creation + projected backfill row/WAL footprint (estimate WAL/row footprint vs free disk); **(b)** no **blocking long-running transaction** holding a conflicting lock on `kline_cache_coverage`/`backtest_runs` (query `pg_stat_activity`); **(c)** no **inactive replication slot** (`pg_replication_slots`) or **xmin-pinning** transaction that would prevent autovacuum from cleaning the backfill's dead-tuple churn (check the backend xmin horizon). On a shared prod DB a full-history backfill behind an inactive slot / long xmin-pinning txn can balloon into unvacuumable bloat / disk exhaustion that degrades live trading — the same shared-process hazard the design takes seriously elsewhere. On any failed check the runner **fail-fasts/warns with an actionable message** (schema_version unchanged) rather than starting the backfill. Tests: insufficient-disk-refusal, blocking-transaction refusal, inactive-slot refusal (REQ-MIG-042).
- **Submission-quiesce DRAIN protects the v58 DDL window — the contended writer is the LIVE SCANNER, not just submissions (R2-F4/R2-F5 + R4-F3-batch6, REQ-MIG-032 — corrected mapping). [FLEET-load-bearing / PRIMARY-degenerate — R5-F4-batch4].** **Scope note (R5-F4-batch4):** on the PRIMARY single-Windows-host target the committed restart discipline is **stop-then-start** (§2.0), so the live scanner is DOWN during the v58 DDL window and this entire gate/DRAIN apparatus is **degenerate dead-weight** (the contended-writer race cannot occur — a test asserts v58 runs with no live `_update_coverage` writer present). It becomes **load-bearing only under the SECONDARY fleet variant**, where a rolling deploy overlaps old+new pods and pod-A's live scanner races pod-B's DDL. The mechanism below is specified for the fleet case (and as defence against an accidental second host process). REQ-MIG-032's DRAIN/QUIESCE is **NOT** the `SealBackfillRunner` pause (that runs AFTER `schema_version=58`, so pausing it does nothing to protect the DDL window). The real requirement: during the brief v58 DDL window, the `ADD COLUMN` on live-scanner-written `kline_cache_coverage` and the `DROP/ADD CONSTRAINT` swap on `backtest_runs` each take a momentary `ACCESS EXCLUSIVE` that must not race the live scanner's continuous `_update_coverage` GREATEST upserts or in-flight backtest/sweep result-upserts. **The primary contended writer is the live scanner's continuous `_update_coverage` upsert on `kline_cache_coverage` — a submission-only quiesce does NOT touch it (R4-F3-batch6).** A scanner upsert holding `ROW EXCLUSIVE` on a coverage row when the migration requests `ACCESS EXCLUSIVE` queues the lock; under the savepoint-retry helper (above) the ADD COLUMN's `lock_timeout` aborts that attempt and retries, but to keep the window cheap the protection is **two-pronged**: **(1)** a **scanner coverage-write gate** — for the brief DDL window the live scanner's `_update_coverage` path observes a short DB-backed/in-process `BT_COVERAGE_WRITE_PAUSE` flag (set by the booting migrator, cleared on commit/abort) and **buffers/defers its GREATEST upserts** (or the scan loop itself is briefly paused — it already tolerates transient pauses), so the ACCESS EXCLUSIVE request is uncontended; **(2)** a **submission-quiesce** that returns a retriable `503 maintenance/busy` for NEW `POST /backtest` and `POST …/sweep` submissions for the DDL window while in-flight runs drain, so their delete-before-insert/results-upsert do not collide. Because the savepoint-retry helper splits each live-shared ADD COLUMN into its own statement, each ACCESS EXCLUSIVE is held per-statement-ms (composing with the txn-scope decision below). A **concurrent-`_update_coverage`-upserts-during-DDL test** drives live coverage upserts during the ALTERs and asserts the additive DDL **retries/succeeds without blocking the scanner beyond budget** (and the scanner resumes from the buffer with no lost coverage). A **drain-then-DDL no-collision test** is also required. (If the project instead accepts *contention→fail-fast→next-boot-retry* as the behavior, that decision is documented and the in-boot retry count is bounded — see next bullet — but the default is the tested gate+drain.)
- **Bounded lock_timeout WITH in-boot retry on the live-shared additive DDL — txn-scope decision PINNED to SAVEPOINT (R2-F5 + R3-F4-batch4 + R4-F2-batch6, REQ-MIG-020/030).** The migration runner wraps every callable in ONE `conn.transaction()` under the 30s session `lock_timeout` — but a `lock_timeout` abort **inside a single transaction rolls the WHOLE transaction back**, so "retry the `ADD COLUMN` within the boot" is **impossible without savepoints** (a transient lock conflict would discard all of v58, not just the conflicting statement), AND the originally-shown code set `SET LOCAL lock_timeout='3s'` only before the step-5 constraint swap — the **step-1 `ADD COLUMN` on the live-scanner-written `kline_cache_coverage` ran under the default 30s with no retry**, exactly the long-`ACCESS EXCLUSIVE`-vs-live-scanner crash-loop hazard the design claims to remove. **Decision (PINNED — savepoint, NOT out-of-txn autocommit):** the live-shared `ADD COLUMN`s on `kline_cache_coverage`/`backtest_runs` are bracketed in **per-statement `SAVEPOINT`s with a bounded retry/backoff loop (5 attempts, exponential backoff 0.5s→8s) and `SET LOCAL lock_timeout='3s'` set BEFORE the step-1 coverage `ADD COLUMN`** (the §4.4 `_alter_with_retry` helper). A transient conflict rolls back only that statement (`ROLLBACK TO SAVEPOINT`), never the whole v58 callable. **The out-of-transaction-autocommit alternative is REJECTED as infeasible-on-this-runner (R4-F2-batch6):** the runner already opened `conn.transaction()` and holds `pg_advisory_lock(8675309)` on **that same `conn`**, so an "autocommit ADD COLUMN" cannot run on it without either an unspecified runner change or a **second connection** — and a second connection breaks REQ-MIG-020 atomic-rollback (a later v58 statement failure could no longer roll back an already-committed ADD COLUMN) and the single-advisory-lock atomicity. The savepoint scope preserves both (every statement is additive `IF NOT EXISTS`, so a retried ALTER is idempotent and whole-callable rollback still yields no partial DDL). **Lock-window note:** savepoints do NOT release the per-statement `ACCESS EXCLUSIVE` early (it is held to the outer commit), so the window is kept short by (a) the whole callable being sub-second catalog-only DDL and (b) the §4.4 scanner coverage-write gate making the request uncontended — NOT by any early lock release. A lock-contention test asserts the additive DDL **retries-and-succeeds** rather than aborting v58, and a whole-callable-atomicity test asserts a forced failure in a LATER step leaves `schema_version` at 57 with zero columns added. (This composes with the §4.4 scanner-gate + submission-quiesce DRAIN, which shrink the contention window in the first place.)
- **Per-chunk `statement_timeout` AND `idle_in_transaction_session_timeout` survival (R2-F5-dup, REQ-MIG-036).** The migration runner deliberately leaves `statement_timeout` UNSET for migrations (`async_persistence.py:1597`), so `lock_timeout` alone is insufficient: a prod cluster with a **server-global `statement_timeout`** can kill a too-large seal-chunk `UPDATE` mid-flight, and a global `idle_in_transaction_session_timeout` can kill a chunk txn that pauses between statements. Each `SealBackfillRunner` chunk transaction therefore `SET LOCAL statement_timeout` sized to the per-chunk budget and is short enough to survive any server-global `idle_in_transaction_session_timeout`. A "short-idle-timeout / statement_timeout-survival" test is required (REQ-MIG-036).
- **Durable flag/config store + flag-change audit — DB-backed source of truth (R2-F37/R2-F8 dup + R3-F1-batch4, REQ-MIG-037, REQ-ROLL-003/004, §7.2).** REQ-MIG-037 calls for a durable flag/config STORE + flag-change AUDIT table seeded with every flag at its documented SAFE default; REQ-ROLL-003 requires the flag/kill-switch state to be **DB-backed, durable, read-your-writes** (not redeploy-to-flip). **Decision (corrected from the earlier ENV-only model):** v58 creates **(i)** a durable **`bt_flag_config` control table** — the **source of truth**, read with read-your-writes/staleness-guard semantics, **layered above ENV defaults** (precedence ENV-default `<` DB-override), so a flag/SAFE_MODE flip survives restart and is honored on the next run fleet-wide without redeploy (§7.2 `CapabilityResolver` re-resolves per run); and **(ii)** an append-only **`bt_flag_audit` table** (idempotent `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS`) recording each effective-flag snapshot at boot/flip (flag name, effective value, capability-resolved reason, engine SHA, `applied_at` UTC). **Seeding is performed by `CapabilityResolver` at boot, NOT by v58 (R4-F7-batch6-c3):** v58 creates both tables empty; on first boot `CapabilityResolver` (which owns the flag registry) seeds `bt_flag_config` one row per registered flag at its documented safe default via `INSERT … ON CONFLICT(flag_name) DO NOTHING` and appends a `bt_flag_audit` snapshot. Per **REQ-CFG-008** an ABSENT `bt_flag_config` row resolves to the safe default, so empty-post-v58 is correct, not catastrophic. The control surface (`bt_flag_config`) and the audit log (`bt_flag_audit`, BIGSERIAL append-only, no idempotent conflict target) are **distinct**. The migration-completeness meta-test enumerates both AND asserts they are **POPULATED after first boot** (not merely present — REQ-OBS-044-style), so an unseeded control table fails CI. This satisfies REQ-MIG-037's audit clause AND REQ-ROLL-003's durable-control clause, rather than leaving the ENV-only contradiction implicit.
- **schema_version ledger self-repair + durable per-migration provenance (R2-F43/R2-F9 dup, REQ-MIG-043).** The runner (verified `:1602–1639`) does `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS schema_version` → `SELECT` one row → `UPDATE`, with **no** detection for a duplicate/multiple/NULL/corrupt ledger and **no** per-migration provenance. v58's runner spec is extended to: **(a)** detect a duplicate/multiple/missing/NULL `schema_version` row and **fail-loud with a documented repair path** rather than silently picking one (never assume 0/57); **(b)** write durable per-migration provenance (`version`, `applied_at` UTC, `git_sha`) **idempotently** (no duplicate row on re-run) into a `schema_migration_log` table created by the same additive DDL. Tests: corrupt/duplicate-ledger fail-loud, and provenance-recorded-once-on-re-run (REQ-MIG-043).
- **Conflict-target safety + incompatible-column detection — FAIL-LOUD pre-checks live in the callable body, not only prose (R4-F7-batch6, REQ-MIG-007/008/039).** Idempotent writes rely on `store_klines` unique `(symbol,interval,open_time)` and the seal upsert on `(symbol,interval,date)`. The §4.4 callable's **step-0 introspection** (shown in the code block) runs BEFORE any ALTER: (1) it queries `pg_index`/`pg_attribute` and asserts the live `kline_cache_coverage` PK is **exactly `(symbol,interval,date)`**, raising a key-mismatch `RuntimeError` if not (REQ-MIG-007); (2) for each target column it queries `information_schema.columns` and **fails loud on a pre-existing incompatible type/width** rather than letting `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` silently keep it (REQ-MIG-008) — the canonical hazard is a hand-added `first_open_ts INT4` that would overflow epoch-ms (REQ-MIG-006). Analytics aggregates COALESCE/ignore NULL new fields over a mixed pre/post-v58 population (REQ-MIG-039). The two REQ-MIG-007/008 tests (wrong-PK, pre-created-wrong-typed-column) are wired to the **actual callable** (they boot a DB seeded with the bad PK / bad column and assert the callable raises before adding columns), not to a prose claim.
- **Status-CHECK relaxation ships `NOT VALID` WITHOUT VALIDATE for the superset case — REQ-MIG-030's literal "then VALIDATE" clause is intentionally waived here (R4-F4-batch6 traceability note, REQ-MIG-030).** REQ-MIG-030 reads "the status CHECK relaxation applied as `ADD CONSTRAINT NOT VALID` then `VALIDATE`." The architecture **deliberately does NOT run `VALIDATE`** for the `backtest_runs` status relaxation because the new enum is a **strict superset** of the old one: every existing row already conforms, `NOT VALID` still fully enforces every new INSERT/UPDATE, and `VALIDATE`'s `SHARE UPDATE EXCLUSIVE` seq-scan under the global advisory lock would re-couple a data-dependent scan to the boot path (the exact deploy crash-loop the boot-safety split kills). **Traceability resolution:** REQ-MIG-030 is read as **"`NOT VALID`, and run `VALIDATE` only when the new enum is NOT a superset of the old"** — for superset relaxations the VALIDATE clause is waived and a traceability audit MUST mark REQ-MIG-030 satisfied by the NOT-VALID-only path (NOT flag it violated). The non-superset path retains the out-of-band `VALIDATE` in `SealBackfillRunner` (its own short txn, `SHARE UPDATE EXCLUSIVE`, never the global lock — §4.4 step-5 comment). An implementer MUST NOT add an in-callable `VALIDATE` for the superset case; the boot-a-second-instance-during-a-long-out-of-band-VALIDATE test (REQ-MIG-030) covers the non-superset path only.
- **Version-int collision is CI-enforced, not coordinated by hand (R1-F21, REQ-MIG-002).** A standing CI guard fails any merge that introduces a duplicate or non-strictly-increasing migration version int, or edits a released migration (`<=58`) in place (checksum/snapshot of the released `_MIGRATIONS` entries); corrections ship as v59+. Version-int collisions have happened twice before on parallel branches (discovery §9, e.g. the v42 renumber note at `:1436`).
- **Migration entrypoint is import-isolated from accel/engine modules — including the `_engine_git_sha` provenance helper (R1-F22 + R4-F8-batch6, REQ-MIG-029).** `_seal_manifest_v58` and the migration runner import ONLY the persistence/DDL layer — never transitively `BacktestEngine`/`SoADatasetBuilder`/`engine_kernel`/scanner/columnar modules — so a `migrate` on the lean pure-Python image (numba/pyarrow/duckdb force-absent) cannot fail at import. **The `_engine_git_sha()` helper the v58 callable calls (step-9 provenance INSERT) is — despite its name — defined in the persistence/DDL layer (or a zero-dependency utility module the migration runner already imports), NEVER in or importing an engine/accel/version module (R4-F8-batch6):** a git-SHA read is a `git rev-parse`/embedded-VERSION lookup with no engine dependency, and locating it in an engine module would let an import failure there abort the entire migration at boot on the lean image. A standalone CLI `migrate` entrypoint shares the same advisory-lock election as the boot path. The **REQ-MIG-029 import-graph test is extended to assert the migration module's FULL transitive import set — including `_engine_git_sha` and everything it pulls in — contains no engine/SoA/numba/scanner/columnar module**, exercised on the accel-force-absent image (CLI-vs-boot-once + accel-absent import test).
- **Runner safety net.** The DDL callable is wrapped in `conn.transaction()` (`:1629`) behind `pg_advisory_lock(8675309)` (`:1641`); a failure leaves `schema_version` unchanged, no partial DDL (REQ-MIG-043). The advisory-lock key allocation is documented and **disjoint**: the migration key (8675309), the `SealBackfillRunner` election key, and the live-scanner/app keys never collide (REQ-MIG-027).

---

# 5. API Architecture — NO breaking changes

**Hard rule:** every existing endpoint, request schema, and response shape is a **no-regress surface** (discovery §4/§5). This refactor adds **zero** new required fields and **renames/removes nothing**. New fields are **optional + nullable** only.

## 5.1 Endpoints — unchanged signatures (`backend/routers/backtest.py`)

| Endpoint | Status | Note |
|----------|--------|------|
| `POST /backtest` (create) | UNCHANGED | `BacktestCreateRequest.model_dump()` → `config.get(...)`; MCP `backtest_run` params stay 1:1 identical (discovery §3). |
| `POST /backtest/{id}/run` | UNCHANGED | Same lifecycle, faster. |
| `POST /backtest/{id}/cancel` | UNCHANGED | Cooperative `threading.Event` cancel preserved (`backtest_engine.py:1232`). |
| `GET /backtest` / `GET /backtest/{id}` | UNCHANGED | `_build_results` (`backtest_service.py:476`). |
| `DELETE /backtest/{id}` | UNCHANGED | — |
| `GET /backtest/{id}/trades` (paginated) | UNCHANGED | `get_backtest_trades` (`:1537`); must stay index-backed + cursor/limit-paginated, latency flat as rows grow (REQ-PERF-034). |
| `POST /backtest/compare` | UNCHANGED | `compare_backtests` (`:357`). |
| `GET /backtest-cache/status` | UNCHANGED shape | `CacheStatusResponse{symbols_total, symbols_cached, symbols_with_gaps, ready}` — now computed from `SealedManifest`; **may add** optional `sealed_days`/`negative_days` counts. |
| `POST /backtest-cache/warmup` | UNCHANGED | `warmup_cache` (`:417`) → `SealedManifest.unsealed_days` + bounded fetch. |

## 5.2 Result / Trade JSON contract — preserved (the frontend trap)

`BacktestResults{metrics, equity_curve, summary, warnings}`; `BacktestMetrics` ~45 keys; `EquityPoint{ts, equity, drawdown_pct?}`; `BacktestTrade` 19 fields + `strategy_kind` (discovery §5).

- **`metrics.total_trades` INVARIANT.** If absent/renamed, the UI routes completed runs to the "no trades simulated" fallback (`BacktestResultsPage.tsx:255`) — looks like data loss. **Never rename/retype/remove existing keys; only ADD optional nullable keys** (REQ-FE, REQ-API). A CI contract test asserts `total_trades` (and the full ~45-key set) is always present + correctly typed.
- **Path-dependent metrics** (`compute_max_drawdown:155`, `compute_sharpe:107`, `compute_sortino:127`, `compute_run_up:224`) depend on `equity_curve` ORDER — the SoA/numba rewrite must preserve curve ordering exactly (discovery §6).
- **`equity_curve` is LTTB-downsampled on GET** (`_downsample_equity:491`). Any manifest/hash of the curve hashes the **FULL stored JSONB**, not the downsampled API view (discovery §5). **`_downsample_equity` is modified (NOT left frozen) to force-include the global max-drawdown trough point (R4-F13-batch6-c2, REQ-FE-004):** standard LTTB does **not** guarantee retention of the global-min point — a deep single-bucket trough can be dropped, so the rendered curve could hide the max-DD extreme. The downsampler is therefore amended to **always include the first point, the last point, AND the global max-drawdown trough point** (compute the global-min-equity / max-drawdown index, then union it into the LTTB output), and its golden oracle is **re-frozen** against the amended output (the earlier "_downsample_equity LTTB frozen" claim is corrected for this one modification — a frozen downsampler that drops the trough contradicts the REQ-FE-004 must/should). A **trough-preservation fixture** (a curve whose trough LTTB would otherwise drop) asserts the trough survives downsampling; the manifest still hashes the full pre-downsample JSONB (REQ-FE-003), so the trough modification changes only the GET view, never the hash basis.
- **`equity_curve` manifest hash is STORED, version-tagged, and re-validated under the old scheme on a version bump (R4-F12-batch6-c2, REQ-FE-003/015).** The frozen manifest-hash algorithm is computed **at persist time over the full stored `equity_curve` JSONB** (never the LTTB GET view — REQ-FE-003) and stored in `backtest_results.equity_curve_manifest_hash` alongside the scheme's `manifest_hash_version` (both v58 additive nullable columns above). On read/validate, the GET-path integrity guard (§5.2 torn-persist guard) **recomputes the hash under the scheme named by the row's `manifest_hash_version`** — so when the algorithm changes, the new code bumps the version tag and a **pre-deploy-hashed result still validates post-deploy** by recompute-under-the-old-scheme rather than reporting a spurious mismatch (REQ-FE-015). The stored hash is the validate-against target REQ-FE-015's "still validates post-deploy" implies; without a stored hash+version there is nothing to validate against. Both columns are added to the migration-completeness meta-test enumeration; tests: a **hash-tracks-full-JSONB** test (REQ-FE-003), a **version-bump-re-validate** test (old-version stored hash recomputes-under-old-scheme and passes — REQ-FE-015), and a **scheme-change-is-version-gated** test.
- **Persistence idempotency unchanged + batched (R1-F11 mig, REQ-PERF-017/032):** results upsert `ON CONFLICT(run_id)`; trades delete-before-insert; NUMERIC cols need Decimal coercion + finite-guard (`_num:1449`) or one Inf/NaN aborts `_persist_results` (discovery §5). **Trade persistence uses a single `executemany`/`COPY`** so a T-trade run issues **O(1) insert round-trips, not O(T)** (persist time ∝ volume, not per-row RTT) — when the engine compresses hours→seconds, an O(T) per-row insert loop would otherwise become the dominant tail. `equity_curve` is held in **primitive columnar arrays** (parallel float64/int64) serialized in one O(n) pass. An **absolute persist budget of <3s** on a trade-heavy run is added to §11; a gate **doubles the trade count and asserts the insert round-trip count stays flat** (REQ-PERF-017/032). **Finite/Decimal guard MUST run BEFORE the COPY buffer is built (R3-F5-batch3, REQ-API-007):** asyncpg `COPY` (`copy_records_to_table`) builds a single record buffer with **no per-row recourse** — a single offending value aborts the whole COPY, and under the §5.2 single-transaction contract that rolls back the results row + curve too (the atomic+COPY combination *enlarges* the blast radius of one NaN/Inf metric from one trade row to the entire run vs the old per-row loop). Pinned ordering: the `_num` finite/Decimal guard runs **over every trade record during buffer construction** (rejecting/sanitizing non-finite values) **before** the `COPY`/`executemany` call, so the COPY buffer is pre-validated. A test injects a single non-finite trade value and asserts it is **caught pre-COPY and the run persists** (or fails loud with an actionable message naming the trade+field), NOT silently losing the whole run inside the atomic transaction.
- **Three result writes commit in ONE transaction + a read-side torn-persist guard (R2-F16-batch4, REQ-API-007).** The three writes — `backtest_results` (metrics/summary), `backtest_trades`, and the `equity_curve` JSONB — **commit inside a single `async with conn.transaction()`** so a crash between them can never leave a `completed` run whose results lack matching trades/curve (no partial-persist torn state). **Write-side:** results+trades+curve are staged then committed atomically; a failure rolls back all three and the run is NOT marked `completed`. **Read-side guard (GET path):** a completed run is reconciled before render — if its `results` row exists but trades/curve are missing/length-mismatched, OR `Σ(trade.pnl) != net_profit` (the three-way reconciliation), the GET **returns an explicit integrity error**, never a silently-wrong render (and never the `total_trades`-absent frontend trap §5.2). A test crashes between the trade insert and the curve insert and asserts the run is not served as a valid completed result.

## 5.3 New optional fields (additive only)

Candidate additive keys (all nullable, default-absent so old clients ignore them): `metrics.engine_path` (`"sequential"|"fastpath"`), `metrics.cache_provenance` (tier hit-rate), `summary.jit_warm_ms`, `warnings[]` entries like `max_same_sector_not_enforced` (already emitted), `columnar_degraded`. None are read by the frontend's existing render path.

## 5.4 New runtime status route (additive, non-breaking — R1-F8 mig, REQ-OBS-029/035/039/040/043, REQ-DEP-030)

A **new additive** `GET /backtest/status` (or `/backtest-runtime/status`) route is added — there is currently NO surface to report on the many OBS musts (today only `/backtest` + `/backtest-cache/status` exist). It does not alter any existing endpoint. Pinned payload (all read-only, fleet-comparable):
- per-optimization **active-vs-degraded** state (numba/columnar/fastpath/parallel-sweep/derive-coarse flags × `HAS_*` capability),
- applied **`schema_version`** + **engine git-SHA** (fingerprint),
- **deferred seal-backfill progress** + `seal_backfill_marker` state (`SealBackfillRunner.status()`, §3.10),
- resolved **numba/pyarrow/duckdb versions** (REQ-DEP-030),
- shared **Bybit circuit-breaker** state (§9.6),
- **`pitr_primary_detector`** state (`active`|`degraded` — set `degraded` when the `pg_control_*` grant is missing and the detector fell back to the sampled-integrity backstop, R4-F9-batch6, REQ-MIG-043),
- fleet-comparable **numeric config** (thread caps, concurrency, RSS ceiling).
A contract test pins the payload shape. This is the queryable surface §9.5/§9.6 report through.

**Public payload is COARSENED — exact versions + git-SHA are NOT on the unauthenticated surface (R5-F6-batch4, Medium — fingerprinting/disclosure fix).** The new `GET /backtest/status` route is unauthenticated (§8 "no new authentication"), so a payload exposing **exact engine git-SHA, resolved numba/pyarrow/duckdb version strings (REQ-DEP-030), `schema_version`, circuit-breaker state, and numeric resource config (thread caps, concurrency, RSS ceiling)** is a fingerprinting aid that maps the deployment directly to known CVEs in the (CVE-widened, §8.1) accel stack, and the resource config aids capacity/DoS targeting. Pinned reconciliation: the **PUBLIC payload is coarsened** to report **capability BOOLEANS + active/degraded states WITHOUT exact versions/git-SHA/numeric resource config** — i.e. `{numba: active|degraded|off, columnar: active|degraded|off, fastpath: …, schema_ok: bool (is ≥58, not the integer), breaker: closed|open|half-open, seal_backfill: state-enum, pitr_detector: active|degraded}`. The **precise** values (exact numba/pyarrow/duckdb version strings, full engine git-SHA, integer `schema_version`, exact thread caps / concurrency / RSS ceiling numerics) are exposed ONLY on a **loopback-only / CLI surface** (or an authenticated surface if one is introduced for §3.12). This route is added to the §8 surface analysis as a NEW unauthenticated information-disclosure surface (correcting the §8 "minimal surface change" framing), and a **contract test asserts the public payload OMITS exact version strings, the full git-SHA, and numeric resource config** while still surfacing the active/degraded booleans operators need. Given a REQ-SEC id (§8.7). (If an auth substrate is introduced for the §3.12 MaintenanceAdmin routes — R5-F3-batch4 — the status route MAY instead be auth-gated and serve the precise payload to authenticated callers.)

## 5.5 Run-lifecycle terminal-state arbitration + same-run_id single-flight (R4-F11-batch6-c3, REQ-API-012/015)

The optimized engine adds a chunked numba cancel path (§3.4) and a ProcessPool sweep (§3.6) that make two lifecycle races harder; the API category coverage-map row previously named `BacktestService [UNCHANGED-CONTRACT]` but no design paragraph resolved them. Both are pinned here:
- **Exactly-one terminal state under a near-simultaneous timeout-kill / natural-finish / cooperative-cancel (REQ-API-012).** When the 120s `threading.Timer` kill, the engine's natural finish, and a `POST /cancel` can all fire within the same window, the terminal write is arbitrated by a **single atomic compare-and-set on `backtest_runs.status`**: the transition `running → {completed | failed_with_timeout | cancelled | interrupted_by_restart}` is a guarded `UPDATE … WHERE status='running'` (or a CAS on an in-memory run-state guarded by the run's lock), so the **first writer wins** and the losers observe the row already terminal and no-op. An invalid transition (e.g. `completed → failed`) is impossible because the CAS only fires from a non-terminal state. The `_MAX_CONCURRENT` slot and the `AdmissionAccountant` reservation (§3.9) are released **exactly once**, by the winning terminal writer, in the run-finalizer `finally`. A **near-simultaneous-race test** drives timeout+finish+cancel concurrently and asserts exactly one terminal state, no invalid transition, and a single slot+reservation release.
- **The `queued`-state transitions are ALSO CAS-arbitrated — `queued→running` (slot grant) and `queued→cancelled` cannot race (R5-F8-batch3, Medium — double-start / stuck-queued-row / leaked-reservation fix).** REQ-API-012's CAS as first written guards only `running→terminal`. But the new persisted `queued` state (admission queue, §3.9/§4.4) adds two transitions the prior arbitration did NOT cover: **`queued→running`** (the `AdmissionAccountant` dequeue-trigger grants a slot) and **`queued→cancelled`** (a `POST /cancel`, or a queue-wait-timeout, on a still-queued run). A cancel-while-queued **racing** a slot-grant is otherwise unspecified — risking a **double-start** (both fire) or a **stuck `queued` row + leaked `AdmissionAccountant` reservation** (neither completes the transition). Pinned: BOTH transitions are guarded compare-and-sets on `backtest_runs.status` from `WHERE status='queued'`, so exactly one wins: **(a) cancel-while-queued** = a single guarded transition that, atomically, removes the entry from the `AdmissionAccountant` queue AND (if it had been granted bytes) releases the reservation AND sets `cancelled` — the queue-removal + reservation-release + status-write are one guarded unit, so a cancel cannot leave a granted-but-never-started reservation; **(b) slot-grant** = the `queued→running` CAS fires ONLY from `queued`, so if a cancel already flipped the row to `cancelled`, the slot-grant CAS no-ops and **immediately releases the bytes it was about to assign** (back to the accountant's drain loop for the next waiter). The 120s run-clock arms at the **winning `queued→running`** transition (not at enqueue, §3.9). A **cancel-vs-slot-grant race test** drives a `POST /cancel` and a dequeue-trigger slot-grant concurrently on a `queued` run and asserts exactly one outcome (cancelled OR running, never both), no double-start, no stuck `queued` row, and the reservation is released exactly once on either path.
- **Same-run_id double-submit coalesces/rejects to one clean terminal result (REQ-API-015).** A second `POST /backtest/{id}/run` (or a duplicate create) for a run_id already `pending`/`queued`/`running` is a **single-flight guard at create/enqueue**: the duplicate is **coalesced** (returns the in-flight run's handle) or **rejected** with a retriable conflict, never started as a second concurrent execution over the same run_id — so slot accounting stays correct (one reservation per run_id) and the result is one clean terminal record, not two racing writers. A **double-submit test** asserts the second submission coalesces/rejects and the run ends in exactly one terminal result with correct slot accounting. Both tests are added to §12.3.
- **Preflight-`reject` / queue-wait-`capacity` is a DISTINCT ERROR CONTRACT, NOT a completed result row (R5-F13-batch3, Medium — frontend no-trades-trap fix).** A `PreflightEstimator` `verdict='reject'` run (or a `'queue'` run that times out on queue-wait, §3.9) **never reaches the engine early-out** that guarantees `metrics.total_trades` present-and-0 (§3.3) — so its API response shape was unpinned. If a rejected/capacity run were surfaced as a `backtest_runs` row the frontend reads, it could hit the `BacktestResultsPage.tsx:255` "no trades simulated" fallback or a missing-keys render (the frontend trap §5.2). Pinned: a reject/capacity disposition is returned as a **distinct structured error contract** — an HTTP `4xx` (e.g. `422` for `reject` with the `reason`, `503`/retriable for `capacity`/queue-wait-timeout) with a typed body `{status:'rejected'|'queued_timeout', reason, pred_ms, pred_rss_bytes}` — **NOT** a `completed` result row and **NOT** a zero-trade `BacktestResult`. The frontend renders this as an explicit "rejected / capacity — warm the cache or narrow the run" state, never the no-trades-simulated fallback (which is reserved for a genuine zero-trade *completed* run). A **reject-shape contract test** asserts (a) a rejected run yields the 4xx error contract (not a `completed` row), (b) the frontend renders "rejected/queued" not "no trades simulated", and (c) `metrics.total_trades` is not consulted on the reject path (there is no metrics object). Added to §12.3.


---

# 6. Integration Architecture — Bybit REST

Bybit v5 public is the **only** external integration, hit **only** for cold gap-fill (ADR-003). Sealed days never call it (rerun `call_count == 0` for fully-sealed ranges).

## 6.1 Kline fetch (`KlineCacheService._fetch_klines_from_bybit`)

- **Endpoint:** `_BYBIT_KLINE_URL` (`kline_cache_service.py:18`), `category=linear`.
- **Page size 200 → 1000** (REQ-CACHE / findings §9): `_PAGE_SIZE` (`:19`) raised to Bybit's documented max → ~5× fewer paginated requests on gap-fills. **`_MAX_PAGES` is recomputed for REACH (candles needed), NOT merely for the new page size (R2-F7-batch1, REQ-CACHE / REQ-MIG-035).** Today `_PAGE_SIZE=200 × _MAX_PAGES=5` ⇒ ≤1000 candles/call. Naively "recomputing `_MAX_PAGES` to preserve the same reach" for a 1000-page would DECREASE it (→1), but a first-ever cold seal of a long unsealed history needs the **opposite**: 365 days of 5m ≈ 105k candles/symbol ≈ ~105 pages. **Resolution:** the per-call page cap stays bounded (it caps a single REST call), but cold gap-fill for unsealed history is driven by an **OUTER chunked loop (per-symbol-month), owned by `SealBackfillRunner`/`ensure_coverage`**, so the **total reach is unbounded-by-design** while each call stays page-bounded — the cap can never truncate the tail of a long gap and strand days unsealed (the precise false-refetch bug Phase 1 kills). `_MAX_PAGES` is sized to cover one outer chunk's worth of candles (one month at the interval), and the outer loop iterates chunks until the whole range is covered. A test seals a >5000-candle cold range and asserts full coverage + 0 refetch on rerun.
- **Cold kline-fetch CONCURRENCY is budgeted + the cold-fetch component is named (R3-F6-batch1, REQ-PERF-018/037).** The §6.1 outer chunked loop gives unbounded *reach*, but a cold canonical 90d×50sym ≈ 1.296M candles ≈ ~1300 pages **serial at ~100–300ms/page far exceeds the 120s cap** — and REQ-PERF-018's batched/semaphore fan-out covers only `instrument_info` + `symbol_lifecycle`, **explicitly NOT klines**, so cold kline fetch had no concurrency budget. The reject-then-warm UX (REQ-PERF-037 directs an infeasible cold run to "warm the cache first") also needs a named surface that **cold-fetches a never-seen range**: `SealBackfillRunner` only SEALS rows already present in the Postgres SOR — it does not cold-fetch new ranges. The only cold-fetch surface is **`POST /backtest-cache/warmup` → `ensure_coverage`** (§5.1), which carried no documented concurrency budget. Pinned: the cold kline-fetch path (`ensure_coverage`/`warmup` + the §6.1 outer per-symbol-month chunk loop) uses an **explicit semaphore-bounded concurrent fan-out across symbols** with a committed throughput budget (mirroring REQ-PERF-018's `wall ≈ ceil(N/cap) × per-fetch`), governed by the **shared Bybit circuit breaker** (§6.1) so a 429 storm backs off coordinately. `ensure_coverage` is named as **the component that cold-fetches a never-seen range** (the "reject-then-warm" target), and a test asserts its concurrency (fan-out ≤ cap, RSS-flat, breaker-gated) so warming a 50-symbol multi-month new range is a bounded in-band path, not an unbounded serial pull.
- **Optional bulk path (UNTRUSTED ingress, R1-F11):** for large cold ranges, `public.bybit.com` daily archive download is an OPTIONAL accelerator (findings §4.1) behind a flag; default stays the REST kline endpoint. This is a **new untrusted, compressed ingress path** (gzip/zip-bomb DoS, CSV parse of attacker-influenceable bytes, integrity only via TLS) and is treated as untrusted — contradicting §8.1's "we read only files this process wrote." It enforces: a **decompressed-size ceiling + compression-ratio guard** (zip-bomb), **row schema / symbol / interval / time-range validation** before store, a **published-checksum verification** if available, and **quarantine to a temp dir** (validate-then-atomic-rename into the SOR path). If any guard fails, fall back to the REST endpoint. §8.4 covers this ingress; if the guards are not implemented, the bulk path stays out of scope.
- **Retry / fail-soft:** `_MAX_RETRIES=3` (`:21`) preserved; per-symbol isolation — one symbol's network/parse failure must not abort the batch (`:261`, `try/except` + `still_missing`), it is counted `failed` and its gap retained.
- **Shared circuit breaker — REUSE the existing instance, decided not deferred (R1-F9 mig, R2-F4-batch5, REQ-OBS-029, REQ-CACHE-007/028):** the Bybit circuit breaker **IS the existing `backend/mcp/core/breaker.py` shared instance** (`closed`/`open`/`half-open` + consecutive-failure count + next-probe time) — NOT a second reimplementation with separate state (a new breaker would split state and let one path keep hammering while the other backs off). The kline + instrument + drill fetch paths wrap that one shared breaker so a storm of 429s/timeouts triggers **coordinated backoff** instead of `_MAX_RETRIES`-per-symbol hammering. Its state is exposed on the runtime status route (§5.4/§9.6). **Failed / 429 / timeout responses never seal** a day (a day only seals on durable valid rows past the frontier — §4.2), so the breaker can never cause a false negative-cache.
- **Pagination correctness:** existing reverse-iteration + `[start_ms, end_ms]` filter (`:452–471`) preserved; off-grid/misaligned candles handled by one documented oracle-frozen rule applied identically in bucketing/count/sha/SoA (REQ-STORE-008).

## 6.2 Instrument info (`InstrumentInfoCache.refresh:516`)

- `_BYBIT_INSTRUMENTS_URL` (`:480`), `limit=1000` already. Unchanged. `_DEFAULT_INSTRUMENT_INFO` (`:487`) NO-OP defaults (`tick_size=0`, `max_leverage=0`) preserved — an unknown symbol behaves as if no instrument info supplied (parity-critical for the golden NO-OP guarantee, discovery §8).

## 6.3 Drilldown fetch fallback

The 1m `DrilldownLoader` (§3.5): a per-bar fetch failure falls back to **5m resolution for that bar only**, never aborts the run, never persists partial 1m data, stays non-optimistic (REQ-DRILL-023). A no-1m-candles drill falls back to 5m and never fabricates a fill (REQ-DRILL-013).

---

# 7. Infrastructure & Deployment

## 7.1 New dependencies (optional extra, import-guarded — ADR-005)

```toml
# pyproject.toml — NOT in [project].dependencies (would brick install on a wheel-less target)
[project.optional-dependencies]
accel = [
  "numba>=0.61,<0.67",      # coupled JIT ABI; BOTH floor + ceiling (REQ-DEP-002)
  "llvmlite>=0.44,<0.48",   # single pinned resolution; couples to numba
  "pyarrow>=16,<21",        # Apache-2.0
  "duckdb>=1.0,<2",         # MIT
]
```
A committed hash-pinned lockfile captures exact versions + transitives; CI asserts lockfile↔pyproject sync and that numpy simultaneously satisfies numba's pin AND pandas' floor (REQ-DEP-002). The accel stack is a **separable image layer** so the base pure-Python image stays lean (REQ-DEP-003). `requires-python ≥ 3.10` for the extra; core stays at the project floor.

## 7.2 Feature flags (per-optimization, independent rollback — REQ-ROLL)

| Flag (env) | Gates | Fallback when off/unavailable |
|------------|-------|-------------------------------|
| `BT_USE_NUMBA` (+ `HAS_NUMBA`) | Phase 4 JIT kernel | Pure-Python kernel (oracle of record) |
| `BT_USE_COLUMNAR` (+ `HAS_PYARROW`/`HAS_DUCKDB`) | Phase 5 Parquet/Feather read tier | Postgres-identical read (REQ-DEP-004) |
| `BT_USE_FASTPATH` | Phase 6 vectorized barrier exit | Sequential kernel (its own oracle) |
| `BT_PARALLEL_SWEEP` | Phase 2/6 ProcessPool fan-out | **Bounded `ThreadPoolExecutor` over the `nogil=True` kernel, or sequential** — NOT `asyncio.gather` (R2-F9-batch5: gather over sync CPU work gives zero parallelism; the executor is the parallelism source) |
| `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR` | Columnar cache root | Validated at boot for existence/writability/free-space; degrade to Postgres + warning (REQ-STORE-034) |
| `BT_DERIVE_COARSE` (R3-F3-batch2, REQ-ROLL-015) | Phase 5 derive-coarse-from-fine resampling (15m/1h/4h from sealed 5m) | **Legacy NATIVE per-interval fetch/load path** (byte-identical klines+trades) — the documented rollback lever when derived-coarse diverges from native; flag-OFF native-1h byte-identical parity test (§12.3) |

Phases 1–3 (cache fix, batched loaders, SoA) ship **unflagged** — they are parity-neutral pure-Python and must hit "minutes" alone (D5). Flags gate only the accel-dependent Phases 4–6.

**`CapabilityResolver` / `RuntimeConfig` singleton owns flag×capability resolution (R2-F6-batch5).** No call site resolves flags independently. ONE `CapabilityResolver` singleton computes the **effective** state of each flag as `effective = flag_source AND HAS_<capability> AND boot_validation_passed` (e.g. `BT_USE_NUMBA` on but `HAS_NUMBA` false ⇒ effective off, with a logged degrade reason), and is read by every consumer (engine, store, sweep, §5.4 status route). This prevents the 6 flags being re-resolved inconsistently at each call site. The §5.4 status route reports exactly this resolver's snapshot; a contract test pins resolver-snapshot == status-route-reported state. (The durable `bt_flag_audit` row, §4.4 REQ-MIG-037, records each resolved snapshot.)

**Flag source of truth is a DB-backed durable store LAYERED ABOVE ENV defaults — NOT ENV-only-resolved-once (R3-F1-batch4, Critical, REQ-ROLL-003/004).** ENV-only flags resolved once per process **cannot** satisfy REQ-ROLL-003 (kill-switch / per-path flag state must be **DB-backed, durable, read-your-writes fleet-wide** so a flip survives pod restart/autoscale and is honored on the very next run on every pod, even under replica lag) or REQ-ROLL-004 (a runtime re-enable re-runs the health self-check) — an immutable per-process snapshot honors neither without redeploying every pod, and `bt_flag_audit` is an audit log, not a control surface. **Pinned model:** a DB-backed `bt_flag_config` control table (§4.4) is the **source of truth**, read with **read-your-writes / staleness-guard** semantics, **layered above the ENV defaults**. Precedence is **ENV-default `<` DB-override**: ENV provides the safe boot default; a `bt_flag_config` row overrides it. `CapabilityResolver` **re-resolves the effective state per run (or on a watched-config signal / bounded TTL refresh), NOT once per process**, so a flip takes effect on the next run on every instance without redeploy. `effective = resolve(DB-override ?? ENV-default) AND HAS_<cap> AND boot_validation`. REQ-ROLL-004's runtime re-enable **re-runs the per-tier health self-check** before the tier is honored. On the PRIMARY single-host target (§2.0) "fleet-wide read-your-writes" is trivially one process; on the [FLEET] variant the staleness guard bounds cross-pod propagation. A test flips a `bt_flag_config` row and asserts the next run on a second (simulated) instance honors it without restart.

**Master SAFE_MODE kill-switch — ONE lever, owned by `CapabilityResolver` (R3-F3-batch4, High, REQ-ROLL-001/002).** A single master control **`BACKTEST_SAFE_MODE`** (ENV default + `bt_flag_config` override, same layered model) does in ONE operation what REQ-ROLL-001/002 require: **(a)** forces ALL 6 optimization flags to effective-**off** (reproducing the golden master — pure-Python kernel + Postgres read + sequential + native-coarse), **(b)** signals the engine/sweep cooperative cancel `threading.Event` to **abort in-flight accel runs/sweeps**, **(c)** flips `SealedManifest`/`SealBackfillRunner` to **halt new seal writes**, **(d)** calls the `SealBackfillRunner` **DRAIN/QUIESCE** hook to pause the backfill. It is owned by the `CapabilityResolver` singleton (the one place that already gates every flag), surfaced on the §5.4 status route, and added to the Requirements-Coverage ROLL row. A test asserts SAFE_MODE forces every flag effective-off in one op, cancels an in-flight sweep, and halts seal writes + backfill.

**SAFE_MODE control wiring is EXPLICITLY DEFINED — a config resolver does not reach into running engines undefined (R5-F9-batch1, Medium — undefined-cross-component-wiring fix).** Actions (b)/(c)/(d) above require holding/reaching references to the in-flight run registry's cancel Events, `SealedManifest`, and the `SealBackfillRunner` instance — but `CapabilityResolver` is otherwise a pure flag×capability RESOLVER (a config function read per run). A config resolver silently reaching into running engines + background tasks is undefined wiring for a safety-critical kill switch. Pinned: a dedicated **`SafeModeController`** (or a clearly-scoped responsibility on `BacktestService`, which already owns the in-flight run registry + the `AdmissionAccountant`) is **injected at lifespan startup** with handles to: the **in-flight run registry** (which exposes a `broadcast_cancel()` setting every in-flight run's cancel `threading.Event`), the **`SealedManifest`** (a `halt_seal_writes()` latch), and the **`SealBackfillRunner`** (its existing `drain()`/`quiesce()` hook). `CapabilityResolver` owns only action (a) — forcing flags effective-off (its native job); it **signals** the `SafeModeController` to perform (b)/(c)/(d), rather than reaching into engines itself. The **ordering is pinned + idempotent:** (a) flags-off → (b) broadcast-cancel in-flight → (c) halt new seal writes → (d) drain backfill; re-invoking SAFE_MODE while already in SAFE_MODE is a no-op (idempotent latches). The dependency edges (`BacktestService`/`SafeModeController` → run-registry, SealedManifest, SealBackfillRunner) are added to §7.2. A test asserts **SAFE_MODE cancels a LIVE sweep AND halts seal writes via the defined `SafeModeController` interface** (not an ad-hoc reach), and that the four actions apply in order and are idempotent on re-trigger.

**SAFE_MODE is honorable WITHOUT a successful DB read — fail-safe resolution order (R5-F7-batch5, Medium — DB-coupled-kill-switch fix).** The layered flag model resolves overrides from `bt_flag_config` (DB-backed) above ENV — but coupling the EMERGENCY control to Postgres availability is exactly wrong: **when Postgres is degraded/overloaded (precisely when an operator most wants SAFE_MODE to shed backtest/backfill load OFF the shared DB), the `bt_flag_config` override may be unreadable**, and `CapabilityResolver`'s per-run re-resolve had no defined behavior on a failed `bt_flag_config` read. Pinned fail-safe order: **SAFE_MODE MUST be honorable without ANY successful DB read** — an **ENV/file-based `BACKTEST_SAFE_MODE`** (env var or a sentinel file on local disk) **short-circuits to all-optimizations-OFF + (b)/(c)/(d) independent of `bt_flag_config`**. The resolution order for ALL flags on a FAILED `bt_flag_config` read is pinned: use the **last-known-good cached snapshot** if present, else the **ENV default** — and in BOTH cases an ENV/file SAFE_MODE still forces effective-off; a failed DB read **NEVER blocks a run and NEVER silently re-enables an optimization** (it can only resolve to the safe side). A test asserts **Postgres-unreachable + ENV/file `BACKTEST_SAFE_MODE` set ⇒ every flag resolves effective-off** (the kill switch works with the DB down), and a failed `bt_flag_config` read resolves to last-known-good/ENV-default, never to a more-permissive state.

**Flag-combination support matrix is bounded + enumerated (R2-F7-batch5).** The 5 booleans (numba/columnar/fastpath/parallel-sweep/derive-coarse — R3-F3-batch2) × reader (DuckDB|Polars) × load mode (batch|stream) are NOT all independently supported. The design pins: **(a)** the **canonical baseline** = pure-Python kernel + Postgres read + sequential + native-coarse = the equality target ALL other combinations must match (the all-supported-equal-baseline invariant); **(b)** the **CI-exercised** combinations (each flag independently on over the baseline, plus the all-on prod profile); **(c)** the **illegal** combinations explicitly (e.g. `BT_USE_FASTPATH` on requires the sequential kernel as its oracle, so fastpath-on is only meaningful with the kernel present; columnar reader requires `HAS_PYARROW`). A **CI matrix test** runs the canonical fixture under every CI-exercised combination and asserts byte/discrete-identity to the baseline (the §12.3 module-absent matrix is necessary but not sufficient — this adds the *combination-equality* matrix).

## 7.3 Incremental phase deploy

Each phase is an independent, individually-revertable deploy gated by its golden-master diff (findings build order). P0 (harness) ships first and stays green through P6. P5 is the only phase touching the deploy volume contract: the columnar dir's persistence (survives deploys → cross-process mmap warm; vs ephemeral → documented cold-build budget, 0 Bybit, served from Postgres — REQ-STORE-038). Bulk pre-materialization of the sealed universe is EITHER a bounded/resumable/throttled background job with a checkpoint marker OR strictly lazy-on-first-touch — never an unbounded synchronous mass-build at P5 deploy (REQ-STORE-037).

**Deploy-contract decisions PINNED (R3-F7/R3-F13-batch4) — these were dangling "stated in the deploy contract" forward-references; resolved here:**
- **Columnar-dir persistence (REQ-STORE-038/015).** On the PRIMARY single-host target (§2.0) `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR` is a **persistent local volume** that survives deploys, so the §11.1 **<5s cross-process warm-rerun** budget (mmap'd Feather survives a deploy) is **in force**. If a deploy uses an **ephemeral** columnar volume (or the [FLEET] variant without a shared persistent volume), the <5s warm-rerun budget is **explicitly waived** and the **cold-build budget** governs instead (rebuild from Postgres, 0 Bybit, documented in §11.1) — the deploy states which, and the <5s gate is conditioned on the persistent choice.
- **ProcessPool availability (REQ-DEP-026).** REQ-DEP-026 notes ProcessPool is unavailable on the **win32 dev/CI** host while §3.6 designs Windows 11 + `spawn` ProcessPool + `shared_memory` as the primary transport. Reconciled: **prod Windows 11 supports `spawn` ProcessPool + `shared_memory`** (the committed sweep transport, §3.6); the constrained **win32 dev/CI** environment falls back to a **bounded `ThreadPoolExecutor` over the `nogil=True` kernel** (§3.4 — threads parallelize only because the kernel drops the GIL), and pure-sequential as the final fallback. The prod transport and the dev/CI fallback are pinned, NOT silently auto-degraded; a test asserts the dev/CI host selects the ThreadPool-over-nogil path and prod selects ProcessPool+shared_memory.
- **Multi-worker uvicorn model (REQ-PERF-013).** Per §2.0 the PRIMARY target pins the **single-worker constraint** (option (a)) for the backtest-bearing process — so the RSS watchdog budget is **per-process == whole-host** and `Σ_workers` does not multiply resident kline bytes. The [FLEET] variant, if it runs multiple workers, MUST use **mmap/shared-memory-backed hot tiers** (option (b)) so sealed Feather/Arrow bytes are shared across workers (file-backed pages counted once) and the RSS watchdog is evaluated **against the cgroup limit in aggregate** (`Σ workers`). The chosen option is stated per deploy; the §7.4 asserting test (aggregate resident kline bytes do not scale ∝ worker count under (b), or single-worker enforced under (a)) runs accordingly.

**CD promotion + restore-point gating (R3-F10-batch4 — REQ-ROLL-007, REQ-ROLL-028/029, REQ-MIG-041).** The deploy contract carries three CI/CD gating steps (named even if the platform is TBD):
- **Promotion guard — block schema-version DOWNGRADE (REQ-ROLL-007).** The runner hard-fails when the stored `schema_version` > the binary's max-supported version (`async_persistence.py:1617-1621`), which would crash-loop a rolled-back binary against a forward DB. CD therefore **blocks promoting any binary whose max-supported `schema_version` < the live DB's** — a pre-deploy gate, not a boot crash. (Pairs with the §9.7 boot schema-version-mismatch alert and the SAFE_MODE kill-switch as the operational lever.)
- **Verified restore-point BEFORE v58 (REQ-ROLL-028/029).** Taking AND verifying a Postgres restore-point/backup is a **mandatory gating step immediately before applying v58** (and before any later contraction migration), so a bad additive deploy is recoverable. The restore-point id is recorded; the verify step confirms it is restorable.
- **Restored-prod-clone migration rehearsal (REQ-MIG-041).** Before promotion, v58 is rehearsed on a **restored clone of prod on the exact PG major + partitioning tech**, asserting it applies **within the lock/time budget** AND is a **post-apply no-op on second run** (idempotency on the real shape, not a fresh empty DB). These are CI/CD gates; the platform may be marked TBD but the gates are required.

## 7.4 Resource budgets (the engine shares the live FastAPI process)

| Resource | Budget | Enforcement |
|----------|--------|-------------|
| Process RSS | ≤ **1 GB** total (**re-derived**, see below) | Pre-flight rejects/streams a WIDE run; a **runtime RSS watchdog** cooperatively aborts before OOM (REQ-PERF-039, R1-F15). |
| Klines in RAM (final SoA) | ≤ **150 MB** | `_ProcessLRU` bounded eviction (§3.1); SoA int64+float64 is ~6×8B/candle. |
| **Global timeline** (ADR-004 sorted-unique) | **OWN budget line, ADDED to (not carved from) the 150 MB klines sub-budget** | `Σ(distinct timestamps) × 8B` — ~10 MB canonical (aligned), up to ~168 MB for the 200sym×365d **misaligned** worst case (REQ-ENG-014). **The worst case (~168 MB) ALONE exceeds the entire 150 MB klines sub-budget**, so the timeline gets its OWN `timeline_bytes` line ADDED to the klines budget, not carved out of it; the WIDE class ceiling = `klines(≤150 MB) + timeline_bytes + book + curve + transients` (R5-F4-batch2). Counted as a distinct PreflightEstimator term (§3.9), gated by the WIDE run-class cap. A misaligned-listing fixture is in the acceptance-parity replay set and asserts a legacy-feasible misaligned run is NOT newly rejected (R4-F6-batch6-c2 + R5-F4-batch2). |
| **Drill-ON klines sub-budget** (1m fine residency on top of 5m) | 5m base + 1m fine SoA + 1m memo ≤ run-class ceiling | A drill-ON run's klines budget is **5m final SoA + per-bar 1m fine-SoA arrays + the `DrilldownLoader` 1m memo** — NOT the 5m SoA alone (R4-F5-batch6-c5, REQ-PERF-012). Estimated by the §3.9 drill-ON RSS residency term (`drilled-fraction × per-bar 1m bytes + memo`) and admitted/queued at pre-flight; a run whose 5m+1m residency exceeds the ceiling is rejected at pre-flight, not watchdog-aborted mid-run. |
| **Load-stage transient** | ≤ **~1.5× final SoA** | Streaming/chunked read seam (§3.1 `iter_klines_streamed`, server-side cursor) releases `Record`s as consumed — NOT `pool.fetch()` materializing all rows first (REQ-PERF-014/015, R1-F3). |
| **SoA-BUILD-stage transient** (distinct from load) | ≤ **`input-SoA + O(unique-timestamps) timeline`** | k-way merge of `dict[str,KlineColumns]`→global SoA+timeline holds ALL per-symbol input arrays resident simultaneously (the merge needs every symbol's head; inputs ARE the run's SoA and cannot be released) PLUS the growing union timeline — a SECOND peak streaming does NOT bound (R4-F5-batch6-c2). **The incremental-release option is STRUCK (R5-F8-batch1): k-way merge is incompatible with releasing inputs mid-merge.** Sole bound: counted in the PreflightEstimator admission sum (§3.9) as `input-SoA + O(unique-timestamps)`, so the build peak is admitted, not discovered at runtime. A `tracemalloc` test pins the build-stage peak against this bound. |
| Columnar materialization | Off the asyncio loop | Serialize+compress+fsync+rename runs in the executor so a cold build can't stall the shared loop or live scanner/auto-trade coroutines (REQ-STORE-035). |
| Concurrent runs | `_MAX_CONCURRENT=3` slots (`backtest_service.py:50`) | Pre-flight estimator runs BEFORE acquiring a slot (rejected runs consume no slot — REQ-PERF-037); admission is **concurrency-aware/aggregate** — `Σ(resident in-flight SoA+book+curve) + this_run ≤ 1GB`, queue-not-kill (§3.9, R3-F2-batch1/R3-F4-batch5). |
| **CPU / threads** | Σ ≤ configured CPU budget | Thread pools pinned + coordinated with sweep concurrency (see CPU-budget subsection — REQ-PERF-024, REQ-DEP-021/022/023/024). |

**RSS budget re-derived (R1-F3).** The 1GB ceiling is the **total** process budget, NOT the SoA alone. A WIDE 200sym×365d SoA ≈ 1GB would consume the *entire* budget, leaving nothing for the position book, equity curves, the Python interpreter, or the **live-trading coroutines that share this RSS**. The budget is therefore split: `final_SoA + load-stage transient (≤1.5× SoA) + book/curve working set + interpreter baseline + reserved live-process headroom ≤ 1GB`.

**Interpreter + accel baseline RSS is a PINNED MEASURED NUMBER, subtracted from the admittable budget up front (R5-F3-batch2, High — OOM-under-nominal-load fix).** The "interpreter baseline" term above was never assigned a number, yet on the accel image it includes a **warmed numba + llvmlite + pyarrow + duckdb stack which is commonly several hundred MB resident** (LLVM codegen buffers, Arrow/DuckDB allocator arenas, JIT-compiled function cache). With `_MAX_CONCURRENT=3` each run holding its own up-to-150MB klines SoA plus book/curve, the `AdmissionAccountant` could otherwise admit 3 runs whose `Σ(SoA) + accel-baseline + live headroom` exceeds 1GB → the RSS watchdog (the OOM backstop for live trading) fires under **nominally-admitted** load. Pinned: a **measured `accel_baseline_rss` constant** is captured at boot (the delta between the base pure-Python image RSS and the accel-loaded RSS after warm-up of numba/pyarrow/duckdb), recorded on the §5.4 status route, and the `AdmissionAccountant` reserves against **`(1GB − accel_baseline_rss − live_headroom)`** as the admittable budget — NOT the full 1GB. The baseline is re-measured per host/image (it is environment-specific) rather than hard-coded, but it is a concrete subtracted number, not an unbudgeted term. A **3-concurrent-run-with-accel-loaded RSS test** asserts `Σ(per-run resident) + accel_baseline_rss` stays under the real 1GB ceiling (i.e. the third run queues if the measured baseline leaves no room), proving admission accounts for the warmed-stack footprint.

**Streaming bounds the LOAD transient ONLY — it does NOT shrink RUN-stage residency (R2-F2-batch1, REQ-PERF-014/015 vs REQ-PERF-013, ADR-001/ADR-004, R12).** A correction to the earlier "stream an over-ceiling wide run" framing: the engine is a **cross-sectional shared-capital portfolio sim** — `_evaluate_candles_until` needs EVERY open symbol's mark at each timeline tick to compute basket equity `E = wallet + Σ open-uPnL` (REQ-PAR-006), and positions/signals persist across the whole window, so a batch-1 symbol with a still-open position CANNOT be released before batch-2 loads (its mark is needed on every subsequent bar). Therefore:
- **Symbol-batched `iter_klines_streamed` bounds the LOAD/SoA-BUILD transient** (peak ≤ ~1.5× final SoA, REQ-PERF-014/015) — one raw batch resident, parsed into the SoA, released before the next batch's raw bytes load. This shrinks the *build peak*, not the steady state.
- **RUN-stage residency IS the full SoA** (every symbol×candle, float64) for the run's entire duration — streaming cannot reduce it.
- **Decision:** a run whose **FINAL SoA** (not its load peak) exceeds the klines budget is **REJECTED by `PreflightEstimator`** before taking a slot — NOT "streamed through." The only exception is a partition strategy that provably preserves cross-sectional correctness (i.e. positions are provably symbol-independent — the §3.4 fast-path eligible subset); absent that proof, reject. R12/§7.4/§11.1 are reconciled to this LOAD-peak-vs-RUN-residency distinction; the earlier "feasible vs merely rejected" wording is superseded.

**WIDE run-class reconciled with the 150MB klines budget (R3-F4-batch1, REQ-PERF-002/039, REQ-ENG-031/032).** The committed WIDE fixture (`200sym×365d` SoA ≈ **1GB** ≈ 6.7× the 150MB klines sub-budget, ≈ the entire process RSS) is **always REJECTED** by the general cross-sectional/shared-capital path (it is not symbol-independent), so its REQ-PERF-002 "benchmarked fixture with its own latency+RSS budget proving linear scaling" and the REQ-ENG-031/032 "scaling toward the wide point" tests cannot be produced on the path they validate — even moderately-wide cross-sectional runs are rejected well before 200sym×365d. The conflict is resolved by **explicitly defining the run-class budgets** (REQ-PERF-039 configurable per-run-class cap), choosing per fixture:
- **Define an explicit WIDE run-class with a RAISED klines/RSS cap + relaxed latency.** For the WIDE *benchmark* fixture only, a WIDE run-class is sized so the `200sym×365d` SoA fits with book/curve/interpreter/live headroom (e.g. a klines cap raised toward ~1GB on a host with the RAM, RSS ceiling raised correspondingly, latency budget relaxed well past the canonical ≤50%-of-cap). The REQ-PERF-002 wide fixture + REQ-ENG-031/032 length/symbol-doubling scaling run **in this WIDE run-class**, on a host provisioned for it — NOT on the default interactive 1GB/150MB budget. The default interactive class still rejects such a run (protecting the shared live process).
- **OR re-scope the scaling evidence to the largest IN-BUDGET cross-sectional size + the fast-path subset.** REQ-PERF-002 and the "toward the wide point" scaling tests are re-scoped to the **largest cross-sectional size that fits the default klines budget** (the linear-scaling curve is demonstrated up to that point), and the **true 200sym×365d point is benchmarked only on the fast-path-eligible (provably symbol-independent) subset** that CAN be partitioned/streamed — documenting that the **general cross-sectional wide point is intentionally rejected, not benchmarked**.

The architecture commits to **option (a) for the dedicated WIDE benchmark fixture** (a provisioned WIDE run-class proving linear scaling) and **option (b) framing for the default interactive class** (reject + fast-path-only true-wide). The WIDE run-class klines/RSS cap is sized explicitly here rather than left as a dangling REQ-PERF-039 reference; a test asserts the WIDE fixture runs in the WIDE class and is rejected in the default class.

**Runtime RSS watchdog (R1-F15, REQ-PERF-039).** The 1GB ceiling cannot be enforced by the pre-flight estimator alone — §9.4 itself allows the estimate to be off by ±50% and only "bracket" actual, and a path-dependent peak can exceed 1GB mid-flight. A **standing RSS watchdog** (sampled like the 120s timer) **cooperatively aborts the backtest before the OS OOM-killer hits the shared FastAPI process** when RSS approaches the budget. An under-estimate within the allowed ±50% is thus caught at runtime, not by killing live trading. Watchdog threshold documented here; an abort-vs-OOM test is in the plan.

**Watchdog RSS metric is PINNED to anonymous/private RSS — file-backed mmap EXCLUDED, matching the budget's exclusion (R5-F6-batch1, Medium — false-abort fix).** §3.1/§7.4 state mmap'd Feather pages are "OS-paged and excluded from the 150MB RSS count" (counted once by the OS, reclaimable). But process RSS as naively sampled (e.g. `psutil.Process().memory_info().rss`) **INCLUDES resident file-backed mmap pages** — so a warm cross-process rerun that page-ins a large sealed Feather frame could push sampled RSS toward 1GB and trip the watchdog into a cooperative ABORT, which §9.7 (R4-F8-batch6-c3) classifies as an **acceptance-parity incident** — even though those pages are reclaimable and not heap pressure. The "mmap excluded from budget" accounting and a "watchdog samples total RSS" enforcement would be unreconciled. **Pinned:** the watchdog samples **anonymous/private RSS only** = `RSS − shared/file-backed-resident` (on Linux: `private_clean + private_dirty` from smaps, or `USS`; on Windows: private working set via the process memory counters, excluding mapped-file pages), so the watchdog metric matches the budget's mmap exclusion exactly. The watchdog therefore fires on genuine heap/anonymous growth (the SoA, book, curve, transients) and NOT on reclaimable mapped Feather pages. (Equivalently the implementer MAY include mmap in BOTH the budget AND the watchdog — but the committed choice is EXCLUDE-from-both, since the Feather tier is explicitly reclaimable and double-counting it would shrink the runnable surface.) A test **maps a large Feather frame and asserts the watchdog does NOT abort** on the reclaimable mapped pages (private RSS stays flat), while a genuine anonymous-allocation spike still trips it.

**The watchdog is driven by an INDEPENDENT wall-clock sampler that covers the pre-engine LOAD + SoA-BUILD transients, NOT only between-chunk boundaries (R4-F5-batch6-c4).** §3.4 schedules the cancel/loop-lag/RSS samplers *between kernel chunks*, but the **peak-RSS moments of a run are the streaming LOAD transient (≤1.5× SoA, §7.4) and the SoA k-way-merge BUILD transient (`input-SoA + O(unique-timestamps)`, §3.3)** — BOTH occur **before the chunked engine loop begins**, so there is no chunk boundary at which to sample, and momentary residency can reach a multiple of the final SoA during load+merge. If the watchdog only fired between engine chunks, the OOM backstop would be **asleep during exactly the window an under-estimated run actually OOMs the shared process**. Therefore the RSS watchdog runs on its **own `threading.Timer`-style wall-clock sampler** (like the existing 120s timer) that fires **throughout load + SoA-build + merge + engine run**, independent of the kernel chunk cadence. §3.3/§7.4 state the watchdog covers the pre-engine load/build transient; an **abort-DURING-SoA-build test** is added alongside the existing abort-vs-OOM test, asserting a build-stage anonymous-RSS spike is preempted before OOM.
