**Multi-worker uvicorn — budget is AGGREGATE, not per-process (R2-F13-batch4, REQ-PERF-013).** The 1GB/150MB budgets above are derived for a **single process**, but prod may run **multiple uvicorn workers**, each with its own hot SoA + LRU + 1m-drill memo — so `Σ_W (per-process hot/LRU/1m-drill)` could N-multiply resident kline bytes past the cgroup limit. Two options are documented and one is chosen explicitly: **(a)** **single-worker constraint** for the backtest-bearing process (documented as a deployment requirement, the simplest correct choice), OR **(b)** **mmap/shared-memory-backed hot tiers** so the sealed Feather/Arrow bytes are **shared across workers** (file-backed pages counted once by the OS) and adding a worker does not multiply resident kline bytes. The RSS watchdog budget is then evaluated **against the cgroup limit in aggregate** (`Σ workers`), not per-process. The chosen option is stated in the deploy contract (§7.3); a test asserts aggregate resident kline bytes do not scale ∝ worker count under option (b), or that the single-worker constraint is enforced under option (a).

**CPU / thread budget (R1-F4, R1-F8 mig, R1-F11 mig — REQ-PERF-024/029/030, REQ-DEP-021/022/023/024).** The engine runs synchronously in `ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=_MAX_CONCURRENT=3)` **inside the same FastAPI process** as the live scanner/auto-trade coroutines (`backtest_service.py:103,824,834`). RSS budgeting alone is insufficient; CPU oversubscription directly starves real order placement. Rules:
- **Pin all thread pools at import/connection setup**, derived from the **container cgroup CPU quota if containerized, ELSE the host core count (PRIMARY Windows target — R5-F6-batch5)** (NOT bare `os.cpu_count()` on a containerized host): `NUMBA_NUM_THREADS`, `OMP_NUM_THREADS`/`OPENBLAS_NUM_THREADS`, DuckDB `threads`, Polars `POLARS_MAX_THREADS` (REQ-DEP-021/023). Default numba/BLAS/OMP to **1** unless explicitly coordinated with `executor max_workers`.
- **Windows CPU-reservation mechanism is PINNED (R5-F6-batch5, High — cgroups do not exist on the committed target).** §2.0 pins a single Windows host where cgroups/cpusets do not exist, so "reserve a CPU share for live coroutines" has no cgroup enforcement primitive. On the PRIMARY target the reservation is enforced by: **(a) HARD-CAPPED worker counts sized to leave ≥1 physical core free for the asyncio loop + live order placement** — `_MAX_CONCURRENT` engine threads + sweep workers + their BLAS/numba threads are capped at `host_cores − reserved_live_cores` (reserved_live_cores ≥1), computed at boot from the host core count; AND **(b) Windows process/thread PRIORITY classes** — the sweep/backfill worker threads (and spawn-worker processes) run at `BELOW_NORMAL_PRIORITY_CLASS`/`THREAD_PRIORITY_BELOW_NORMAL` so the OS scheduler preempts them in favour of the normal-priority live-trading loop; OPTIONALLY **(c) a Windows Job Object with CPU rate control** (`JOBOBJECT_CPU_RATE_CONTROL_INFORMATION`) capping the sweep/backfill job's aggregate CPU percentage when available. The fleet/Linux variant uses cgroup quota as before. The chosen mechanism is stated in the deploy contract (§7.3).
- **AUTOMATIC mitigation — concurrency SHED on sustained loop-lag breach, not only an alert (R5-F6-batch5, High — detection-without-mitigation fix).** The §9.5 loop-lag SLI **detects + alerts** live-path starvation but, by itself, leaves a live-trading-starvation gap on the committed single-host target precisely when a saturating sweep runs (priority classes reduce but do not eliminate contention on a fully-subscribed box). Pinned: on a **sustained loop-lag / live-probe-latency breach** (a documented threshold over a documented window), the `SweepRunner`/`SealBackfillRunner` **cooperatively SHED concurrency** — reduce active sweep workers / pause the backfill chunk loop — until the loop-lag returns under threshold, then ramp back up. This is an automatic feedback control, not merely an alert. A test drives a **saturating sweep + a degrading live-probe latency** and asserts the runner **sheds concurrency** (active workers drop) rather than only emitting an alert, and that live-probe p95 recovers under the documented bound.
- **Coordinate with sweep concurrency** so `Σ(active engine threads + sweep workers × per-worker kernel threads × BLAS threads) ≤ CPU budget` — with ProcessPool sweeps (P6 `prange`) × 3 concurrent runs × BLAS, nested parallelism must not multiplicatively exceed cores (REQ-PERF-024, REQ-DEP-022).
- **Pin `NUMBA_THREADING_LAYER`** to a fork/spawn-safe layer (REQ-DEP-024); the spawn start method (§3.6) is the portable default.
- **Reserve a CPU + asyncpg-pool share for live coroutines** during a saturating sweep (REQ-PERF-030) and **guard that process-global BLAS caps do not regress the in-process live scanner's** fetch/compute latency (REQ-DEP-021). On the Windows target this "reserve" is the worker-cap + priority-class mechanism above, NOT a cgroup share.
- **Cooperative GIL-yield:** the CPU-bound/GIL-bound pure-Python kernel **yields/releases the GIL on a chunk boundary** (or runs in process isolation) so a live-path probe's p95 degrades by ≤ a documented factor during a backtest/sweep (REQ-PERF-029) — measured by the standing event-loop-lag SLI (§9.5).
- **REQ-PERF-025's ≥2.5× aggregate-throughput floor is SCOPED to the nogil-numba lane / ProcessPool, NOT the pure-Python fallback (R5-F2-batch2, High — false-fail fix).** REQ-PERF-025's "≥2.5× aggregate throughput for 3 concurrent runs" is owned by `KlineStore` as a **lock-free read-path** gate — but the **pure-Python kernel (the fallback of record, ADR-005) is GIL-bound for its COMPUTE**. Three concurrent runs in `ThreadPoolExecutor` **serialize on the GIL** for the per-candle compute, so end-to-end aggregate throughput is ~1× regardless of how lock-free the cache read is. The 2.5× floor is reachable ONLY on (a) the **numba nogil lane** (`@njit(nogil=True)` releases the GIL so threads run compute in parallel) or (b) a **ProcessPool** (separate interpreters, no shared GIL). As written against the pure-Python lane the gate would **false-fail**. Pinned: **REQ-PERF-025's ≥2.5× is asserted ONLY on the nogil-numba lane (or ProcessPool) — the lane where concurrent compute is genuinely parallel.** A **separate, lower pure-Python concurrent-throughput expectation** is stated for the fallback: the lock-free read path removes **cache-read serialization** (a real win — no run blocks another on cache access) but **cannot remove GIL serialization of pure-Python compute**, so the pure-Python aggregate floor is "≈1× compute + eliminated cache contention" (documented as "no aggregate compute speedup under concurrency; the lock-free cache prevents read-path contention from making it WORSE than 1×"), NOT ≥2.5×. A test asserts the ≥2.5× gate on the nogil-numba/ProcessPool lane and the cache-contention-removed (not compute-parallel) expectation on the pure-Python lane.
- Tests assert caps are applied at setup and that `Σ threads ≤ budget` under a P6 sweep.

## 7.5 Boot / readiness contract + warm-up orchestration (R3-F5-batch4, High — REQ-MIG-010, REQ-DEP-012/013/015)

The design starts many things off the boot path — `SealBackfillRunner`, `SymbolLifecycleRefresher`, numba JIT warm, DuckDB/Polars warm, asyncpg pool pre-warm, RSS watchdog, loop-lag sampler — but never defined how a readiness/liveness probe behaves while they run, so under any orchestrator a liveness probe could kill a pod mid-backfill. Pinned (owned by a named **`BootOrchestrator`** in `backend.main` lifespan):
- **Readiness contract (REQ-MIG-010 — readiness BEFORE population).** The app reports **READY as soon as `schema_version ≥ 58` AND the asyncpg pool is live** — it does NOT wait for the seal backfill, lifecycle refresh, or accel warm-up to complete (those are async/background). A run arriving before the backfill finishes is correct-but-unoptimized (unsealed days are WARM/refetchable, ADR-003). The liveness probe never fails due to an in-progress backfill/warm-up.
- **Per-tier hang watchdog (REQ-DEP-012).** Each warm-up tier (numba JIT, DuckDB/Polars connection, Feather mmap, pool pre-warm) runs under a **bounded timeout**; a tier whose warm-up **HANGS is disabled and falls back** (numba→pure-Python, columnar→Postgres) with a structured warning, rather than blocking boot or the probe. The tier is marked `degraded` on the §5.4 status route.
- **Aggregate boot warm-up budget (REQ-DEP-015).** The sum of all warm-up tiers has a **documented aggregate budget under the probe deadline**; exceeding it disables the slowest remaining tier (fallback) rather than risking a probe-kill. The budget and per-tier timeouts are documented numerics.
- **Await-bounded-or-fallback for an early run (REQ-DEP-013).** A backtest/sweep arriving DURING warm-up **awaits the relevant tier for a bounded time, then proceeds on the fallback** (e.g. a run needing numba waits ≤ the JIT budget, else runs pure-Python) — it never blocks unboundedly on a half-warm tier and never crashes.
- **Warm-up state on the status route.** §5.4 surfaces each tier's `warming|ready|degraded` + elapsed, so an operator sees boot progress. The JIT warm-compile specifically runs **off the event loop** (§3.4) and its window is excluded from the §9.5 loop-lag SLI.
A test boots with a deliberately-hung tier and asserts the app reports READY, the hung tier degrades to fallback within budget, and an early run completes on the fallback.

**Long-lived task supervision — crash ≠ silent death (R3-F11-batch4, Medium — REQ-PERF-039).** The singleton safety/background tasks started by lifespan (`SealBackfillRunner`, `SymbolLifecycleRefresher`, the **RSS watchdog**, the **loop-lag sampler**, the shared breaker reaper) carry a **supervision contract**: each is **health-monitored** (periodic heartbeat), **auto-restarted on crash with bounded backoff**, and its `alive`/`last_heartbeat` state is reported on the §5.4 status route. **Fail-safe specifically for the RSS watchdog:** if the watchdog task dies, the 1GB OOM protection must not silently vanish — admission **tightens** (the aggregate accountant §3.9 treats the watchdog as down and **rejects/queues new wide runs**) until the watchdog is back, so a dead watchdog cannot let the next wide run OOM the shared FastAPI process and take down live trading. A test kills the watchdog task and asserts new wide-run admission tightens + the task auto-restarts.

**Connection budget — direct (session-pinned) + pooled reconciled against `max_connections` (R3-F12-batch4, Medium — REQ-PERF-021).** New **DIRECT, non-pooled, session-pinned** asyncpg connections are introduced by the migration runner, the `SealBackfillRunner` election + chunk txns, the `SymbolLifecycleRefresher` election, and the survivor re-election poll (correctly direct, for pgBouncer-safety §3.10). These are budgeted alongside the app pool so the total cannot exceed managed-Postgres `max_connections`:

| Connection class | Per-instance count | Note |
|------------------|--------------------|------|
| **Live scanner / auto-trade pool `max_size`** (DEDICATED — R5-F8-batch5) | `live-baseline` (its OWN pool, never shared with backtest/sweep) | pooled; **reserved floor** the backtest/sweep path can NEVER consume |
| Backtest/sweep asyncpg pool `max_size` | `_MAX_CONCURRENT×per-run-stream + sweep-read cap` (§3.6) | pooled; separate from the live pool |
| Migration runner direct | 1 (boot only, released after v58) | session-pinned, transient |
| `SealBackfillRunner` election + chunk | 1 | session-pinned, lifetime of backfill |
| `SymbolLifecycleRefresher` election | 1 | session-pinned |
| Survivor re-election poll | 1 (shared with election where possible) | session-pinned |

**Live and backtest/sweep pools are STRUCTURALLY SEPARATE — the live order path has a reserved connection floor (R5-F8-batch5, Medium — live-order DB-starvation fix).** Earlier the table listed ONE pooled class shared by the live scanner/auto-trade AND the backtest. But `iter_klines_streamed` (§3.1) holds a pooled connection inside an explicit `repeatable_read` transaction for the ENTIRE load+SoA-build stage (seconds, paused between batches), so **three concurrent wide streaming runs can pin multiple pooled connections for seconds** against a single shared pool, and "reserve a share" for the live order path was asserted but not structurally enforced — risking live-order DB starvation under concurrent wide backtests. Pinned: the **live scanner/auto-trade path gets its OWN dedicated asyncpg pool** (or, equivalently, a reserved minimum connection count carved out of `max_connections` that the backtest/sweep pool's `max_size` is sized to never touch), distinct from the backtest/sweep read budget. A backtest/sweep can exhaust ITS pool without ever reducing the live path below its reserved floor. A test asserts **3 concurrent streaming wide runs cannot reduce the live path's available connections below its reserved floor** (the live pool's free count stays ≥ its reserved minimum throughout).

The **per-instance direct-connection ceiling** is pinned (≤ ~4 beyond the pools) and, on the [FLEET] variant, `Σ_pods (live-pool max_size + backtest/sweep-pool max_size + direct ceiling) + live-scanner headroom ≤ Postgres max_connections` is asserted as a deploy guard. On the PRIMARY single-host target this is one instance, trivially within budget. A test asserts the aggregate connection count stays within the configured ceiling under a concurrent backfill + sweep + live scanner, AND that the live pool's reserved floor is never consumed by backtest/sweep load.

---

# 8. Security

Minimal surface change — no new authentication, no new external callers, no new PII. Threats are confined to **new dependencies**, **new filesystem writes**, and **one new unauthenticated read-only information-disclosure surface** (the `GET /backtest/status` route, §5.4 — coarsened to capability booleans/states, exact versions+git-SHA+resource-config moved to a loopback/CLI surface per R5-F6-batch4). All §8 controls are wired to **REQ-SEC** requirements with named tests (§8.7) so none can be silently dropped. The MaintenanceAdmin destructive operations are **CLI-only** (§3.12, R5-F3-batch4) — they add no new authenticated route, so "no new authentication" remains accurate.

## 8.1 New-dependency CVE surface

numba/llvmlite/pyarrow/duckdb widen the transitive CVE surface the project already tracks via pip-audit floors (discovery §10). Mitigations: hash-pinned lockfile (REQ-DEP-002); pip-audit run over the accel extra in CI; floors+ceilings bound the resolvable set; the extra is optional so a base deploy carries none of it. pyarrow historically carries deserialization CVEs (e.g. arbitrary-code via crafted IPC) — we read **only files this process wrote** (no untrusted Arrow/Parquet ingress, except the explicitly-guarded bulk-archive path §8.4), and the format/schema-version stamp + sha verification (REQ-STORE-028/029) reject anything not self-produced.

**`content_sha256` is integrity-of-content, NOT a parser-CVE mitigation (R1-F13).** Verifying `content_sha256` requires first **parsing** the Parquet/Feather with pyarrow (the hash is over the day's rows — §4.1) — i.e. the very operation a malicious-file pyarrow CVE would exploit. The sha therefore cannot defend the parse step; it only catches post-parse content drift. The real control against a hostile file is the **process-ownership + directory-mode guard** in §8.2 (the file provenance is "this process wrote it"), not the hash. For files of genuinely uncertain provenance (bulk archive §8.4), hash the **raw file bytes pre-parse**.

## 8.2 Parquet file-path safety

The hive path is built from `symbol` + `interval` + UTC `year/month`. `symbol` originates from stored scans / Bybit but flows into a **filesystem path** → path-traversal risk (`BTC/USDT`'s `/`, or a crafted `../`). Mitigation: the documented **reversible `SAN(SYM)` encoding** (REQ-STORE-021) percent-/hex-encodes every non-`[A-Za-z0-9._-]` char (so `/` and `..` cannot escape), and the resolved absolute path is asserted to be **within** `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR` before any open/write. `interval` is validated against the closed enum (`5m/15m/1h/4h/1m`). The columnar dir is operator-configured and boot-validated (REQ-STORE-034), never silently writing to an unintended path.

**Directory-ownership + TOCTOU close — Windows-primary + POSIX-lane (R1-F13 + R5-F1-batch4, High — unimplementable-on-Windows fix).** `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR` must be **process-owned, not writable by other principals, and not a reparse/symlink target** — boot-validated (the within-dir path check alone does not prove the directory itself is safe), and the per-file open must close the **TOCTOU window** between the path-within-dir check and the open. The earlier control used POSIX-only primitives (`os.O_NOFOLLOW`, `realpath`-then-`fstat`, `st_mode` "non-world-writable") — but the **PINNED primary target is Windows 11 (§2.0)**, where `os.O_NOFOLLOW` **does not exist** (Python: Unix-only → `AttributeError`), there is **no world-writable mode bit** (access is ACL-based, so an `st_mode` check is meaningless), and the real traversal/swap vector is an **NTFS junction / reparse point** that `O_NOFOLLOW` would not catch even if it existed. So the control is specified **per-OS**:
- **Windows (PRIMARY):** **(a)** reject reparse points — open with `FILE_FLAG_OPEN_REPARSE_POINT` semantics / check `FILE_ATTRIBUTE_REPARSE_POINT` on the path and every parent up to `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR` and **refuse** if any is a junction/symlink/mount-point; **(b)** validate `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR` ownership + ACL via the win32 security APIs (owner SID == the process SID; **no write ACE for non-owner / `Everyone` / `Authenticated Users`**) instead of mode bits; **(c)** canonicalize (`os.path.realpath`/`GetFinalPathNameByHandle`) **then re-stat BY HANDLE** (open the handle, then validate the handle's final path is within `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR`) so the check and the open refer to the SAME object — a handle-based check that closes TOCTOU on win32. A **Windows-host test** asserts a **junction swap** in `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR` (replacing a part-dir with a reparse point between check and open) is **rejected**.
- **POSIX (CI / Linux lane only):** `O_NOFOLLOW` + `realpath`-then-`fstat` + boot-validate dir mode (non-world-writable) + ownership, exactly as before. `O_NOFOLLOW` applies ONLY to this lane.

This — process provenance (Windows reparse-reject + ACL-owner check, or POSIX `O_NOFOLLOW`+mode) — is the actual control against a hostile columnar file (§8.1 says the `content_sha256` cannot defend the parse), complementing (not replaced by) the integrity check. Given a REQ-SEC id (§8.7).

## 8.3 DuckDB read-engine injection + capability lockdown (R1-F12 + R5-F2-batch4, High — technically-corrected)

The DuckDB reader (§3.1, §4.3) is a long-lived connection that can **read AND write the local filesystem** and **auto-install/load extensions**; if `symbol`, `interval`, or a hive path were ever string-interpolated into a SQL/scan string it would be an injection / arbitrary-file-read+write vector (the `SAN(SYM)` encoding protects the *filesystem* hive path but NOT a DuckDB SQL string). The earlier lockdown was **technically incorrect and, taken literally, both unimplementable and incomplete** (R5-F2-batch4): `enable_external_access` is a **BOOLEAN** — setting it false disables ALL external file reads INCLUDING `read_parquet`, breaking the entire columnar use case; it **cannot be "locked to `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR`"**. Directory scoping is the SEPARATE `allowed_directories`/`allowed_paths` setting (DuckDB ≥1.1). And the injection vector itself is only durably closed with `lock_configuration=true` so a successful injection cannot SET the access settings back on. Corrected, pinned controls:
- **Keep `enable_external_access=true` (Parquet reads need it) but CONSTRAIN with `allowed_directories=[BT_COLUMNAR_DIR]`** (and/or `allowed_paths`), so file access is scoped to the columnar dir — NOT by flipping the boolean off.
- **`lock_configuration=true` with a minimal `allowed_configs` allowlist** so a successful injection **cannot re-widen access** (cannot SET `enable_external_access`/`allowed_directories`/extension settings back on after lockdown). This is the durable close of the R1-F12 injection vector and was missing.
- **`autoinstall_known_extensions=false` + `autoload_known_extensions=false`** (no extension fetch/load) and **`access_mode='READ_ONLY'`**.
- **The scanned Parquet PATH is necessarily string-built into `read_parquet('…')`** (it is a filename, not a bindable SQL parameter) — so path safety rests on **`canon()` + `SAN()` + the within-`allowed_directories` validation** (§8.2), NOT on "parameter binding". Real **predicates** (`WHERE symbol=$1`, `interval=$2`, time bounds) DO use proper `$n` parameter binding / a query builder that never interpolates identifiers; `interval` is validated against the closed enum before use.
An **injection test** asserts a crafted symbol **cannot escape `allowed_directories`** (no read/write outside `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR`) **AND cannot mutate config** (a `SET enable_external_access=true` / `SET allowed_directories=…` inside an injected string fails under `lock_configuration`). The earlier "crafted symbol cannot escape the parameter binding" framing is corrected: the path defense is SAN+allowed_directories, the predicate defense is binding. Given a REQ-SEC id (§8.7).

## 8.4 Bulk-archive untrusted ingress (R1-F11)

The optional `public.bybit.com` daily-archive path (§6.1) is the ONE untrusted, compressed ingress and is treated as such: a **decompressed-size ceiling + compression-ratio cap** (zip-bomb guard), **row schema / symbol / interval / time-range validation** before store, **published-checksum verification** when available, and **quarantine to a temp dir** with validate-then-atomic-rename. Raw bytes are hashed pre-parse (§8.1). On any guard failure the path falls back to the trusted REST endpoint. If these guards are not built, the bulk path is out of scope (default REST only).

## 8.5 Migration / wrong-DB safety

v58 itself ships **DDL only** (no destructive backfill — §4.4); the destructive-capable path is the deferred `SealBackfillRunner` (§3.10). Guard against a misconfigured `DATABASE_URL` (or `copy-prod-scans`) running it on the wrong/prod DB via **ONE committed concrete control: a required DB-identity row** checked before any seal write (R1-F7 mig — not three alternatives); detect a READ-ONLY/standby connection and **SKIP/DEFER** rather than crash-loop; least-privilege role surfaces the missing privilege + statement by name (REQ-MIG-043). The advisory-lock keys are **disjoint** (migration `8675309`, backfill-election key, live-scanner keys never collide — REQ-MIG-027). On the win32/Linux ProcessPool path, **`spawn` start method + env-secret ALLOWLIST (§3.6, R5-F4-batch3) + disabled core dumps** prevent a sweep worker from inheriting/dumping `ACCOUNTS_ENCRYPTION_KEY`, `DATABASE_URL`, `COINGECKO_API_KEY`, LLM keys, or decrypted credentials (R1-F10 mig, §3.6). No secrets are added; `ACCOUNTS_ENCRYPTION_KEY` and trading credentials are untouched (the backtester places no real orders).

**Expected DB-identity is OPERATOR-PROVISIONED, not self-seeded; missing `pg_control_*` grant FAILS CLOSED (R5-F5-batch4, High — first-deploy + least-privilege fix).** The §4.4 v58 migration creates `sor_identity` with NULL `system_identifier`/`timeline_id`/`control_digest` and `INSERT … ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` — but the doc never said WHO provisions the EXPECTED identity or WHEN. Two failure modes are closed:
- **First-deploy self-seed is REJECTED.** If the expected identity were self-seeded from the first connection's `pg_control_system()`, the guard would **capture whatever DB it first connects to as "expected"** and happily seal there — providing **zero protection on the FIRST deploy** against a misconfigured `DATABASE_URL` pointing at prod (it would only catch a LATER swap). Pinned: the **expected DB-identity is OPERATOR-SUPPLIED at deploy** (an env/config value, e.g. `BT_EXPECTED_PG_SYSTEM_IDENTIFIER`, asserting the intended `system_identifier`); the boot guard compares the live `pg_control_system()` identity against the OPERATOR-supplied expected value, so a first-deploy `DATABASE_URL` pointing at the wrong DB is caught **on the first boot**, before any seal write. `sor_identity` records the last-seen tuple for PITR-rewind detection (§4.1), but it is NOT the source of the "expected" value — the operator config is.
- **Missing `pg_control_*` grant FAILS CLOSED.** R4-F9-batch6 notes the `pg_control_system()`/`pg_control_*` grant may be **absent under least-privilege / managed-Postgres roles**, dropping the detector to a "degraded/sampled backstop" — which would weaken the wrong-DB guard precisely on hardened roles. Pinned: when the `pg_control_*` grant is absent AND no operator-supplied expected identity can be verified by an alternative means, the destructive seal path **FAILS CLOSED** — it **refuses destructive seal writes** (SKIP/DEFER, surfaced as `degraded` on §5.4) rather than silently degrading-and-proceeding. A `degraded` PITR detector may still serve READS, but it must NOT authorize a destructive seal/backfill against an unverifiable DB identity.
A **first-deploy-against-wrong-DB test** (operator expected-identity set to DB-A, `DATABASE_URL` pointing at DB-B) asserts the guard refuses to seal on the first boot. A **missing-grant fail-closed test** (role lacking `pg_control_*`) asserts the seal path refuses (fails closed), NOT proceeds. Given a REQ-SEC id (§8.7).

## 8.6 Spawn-worker secret minimization (cross-ref §3.6)

Worker env is an **ALLOWLIST, deny-by-default** (R5-F4-batch3, §3.6): spawn workers launch with only the non-secret kernel vars (thread caps, `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR`, numba cache dir, `NUMBA_THREADING_LAYER`) explicitly constructed by the pool initializer — they NEVER inherit `ACCOUNTS_ENCRYPTION_KEY`, `DATABASE_URL`, `COINGECKO_API_KEY`, or `TRADINGAGENTS_LLM_PROVIDER` keys. Core dumps disabled; no forked asyncpg pool handed to a child. The test asserting a worker's `os.environ` contains none of those secrets is REQ-SEC-tagged (§8.7).

## 8.7 Security requirements (REQ-SEC) + coverage map — controls are TRACEABLE (R5-F7-batch4, Medium — orphaned-controls fix)

The §8 controls previously had **no backing REQ-ID** — the requirements set (517 reqs, 15 categories) had no SECURITY/SEC category, so the document's own traceability discipline (every control wired to a REQ-ID with a named test) did NOT cover §8, and these controls could be **silently dropped during implementation with no failing test and no coverage-map row flagging it**. This subsection adds explicit **REQ-SEC** requirements (each with a named test) and wires them into the Requirements Coverage Map so §8 is traceable like every other section:

| REQ-ID | Control | Owning § | Named test |
|--------|---------|----------|------------|
| **REQ-SEC-001** | Path-traversal/TOCTOU rejection — Windows reparse-reject + ACL-owner check (POSIX `O_NOFOLLOW`+mode on the Linux lane) | §8.2 | Windows junction-swap-rejected test; POSIX symlink-swap-rejected test |
| **REQ-SEC-002** | DuckDB capability lockdown — `allowed_directories` + `lock_configuration=true` + read-only + no-autoload | §8.3 | injection-cannot-escape-allowed_directories + injection-cannot-mutate-config test |
| **REQ-SEC-003** | Untrusted-archive guards — zip-bomb decompressed-size+ratio ceiling, schema/symbol/interval/time-range validation, pre-parse raw-byte checksum, quarantine+atomic-rename | §8.4/§6.1 | zip-bomb-refusal + bad-schema-refusal + checksum-mismatch-fallback test |
| **REQ-SEC-004** | Spawn-worker secret minimization (allowlist, deny-by-default) + core-dumps-off | §8.6/§3.6 | worker-os.environ-omits-all-secrets test |
| **REQ-SEC-005** | Unauthenticated-surface disclosure limits — coarsened public `/backtest/status` payload (no exact versions / git-SHA / numeric resource config) | §5.4/§8.6 | public-payload-omits-exact-versions contract test |
| **REQ-SEC-006** | Wrong-DB safety — operator-provisioned expected identity + missing-`pg_control_*`-grant fail-closed | §8.5 | first-deploy-wrong-DB-refusal + missing-grant-fail-closed test |
| **REQ-SEC-007** | MaintenanceAdmin destructive ops are CLI-only (not bound to the public port) + DB-identity guarded | §3.12 | maintenance-ops-not-registered-as-routes test |

These REQ-SEC rows are added to the **Requirements Coverage Map** (and the REQ-ID→test traceability matrix §12.3) so a dropped §8 control fails CI exactly like a dropped functional requirement. (The existing REQ-STORE-021 covers only reversible path *encoding*; REQ-STORE-022/023 are DuckDB *performance/parity*, not *lockdown* — so the security controls genuinely needed their own category, now provided.)

---

# 9. Observability

All always-on instrumentation must be **O(trades + signals + manifest-days), NOT O(candles)**, adding ≤ a documented ~2% overhead (counters-on vs counters-off — REQ-PERF-036). Emitted via the existing `logging` (`logger.info/debug` structured `extra={}`, e.g. `kline_fetch_complete` `kline_cache_service.py:473`).

**Single metrics registry/catalog — emitters AND the §5.4 status route import it (R2-F16-batch5, REQ-OBS-044).** The 30+ named telemetry signals scattered across §9.1–§9.6 (`kline_tier_hits`, `bybit_kline_calls`, `sealed_day_fetched_once`, `event_loop_lag_ms`, `jit_compile_ms`, `accel_wasted_ms`, `live_scanner_fetch_latency_p95`, the §9.1 stage timers, the invariant-check signals, …) are defined ONCE in a **central registry** (`backend/services/backtest_metrics_registry.py`) — a catalog mapping each **canonical name → {type (counter/gauge/timer), unit, cardinality, owning §, redaction class}**. Ad-hoc `logger.info(extra={})` emitters and the §5.4 status route both **import the canonical name from the registry** rather than string-literal it, so a rename/drop/duplicate cannot silently desync the status payload from the emitters. A **test asserts every emitted signal name is registered** (no unregistered emit) and that the §5.4 status route only surfaces registered names. This also backs the §4.4 JSONB payloads (`stage_timings`, `data_quality_counters`) whose keys are the registry's timer/counter names + a `schema_version` (R2-F13-batch5 versioned schema — pinned key set + types so consumers parse a versioned contract, not drifting prose).

## 9.1 Per-phase timing (re-target the next phase from real numbers)

Per-stage timers logged once per run (not per candle): `warmup_ms`, `load_klines_ms`, `soa_build_ms`, `timeline_build_ms`, `phase_a_engine_ms`, `phase_b_drill_ms`, `metrics_ms`, `persist_ms`, `jit_warm_ms`. Findings §9 magnitudes are estimates, not profiled — these timers let us **profile after Phase 3 to re-target Phase 4** (findings "honest risks").

**Partial telemetry survives timeout/cancel/degrade (R1-F19, REQ-OBS-012/013).** On a 120s timeout-kill, cancel, or mid-flight degrade, the partial per-stage timings + cache/Bybit/Postgres/candle-eval counters + flag/SHA fingerprint are **still emitted and persisted** (into `backtest_runs.stage_timings`/`engine_fingerprint`, §4.4) with the **terminal reason + the stage that was aborted**, reconciling to elapsed-until-failure — so a timed-out run is diagnosable, not a black hole. Wasted accelerator-attempt wall-time (a JIT compile that then fell back, a columnar build that was discarded) is attributed to a **distinct stage** (`accel_wasted_ms`) rather than hidden in another timer (REQ-OBS-012).

**Timing model is exclusive-vs-overlap-aware — Σ(stage) reconciles to wall-time (R2-F18-batch4, REQ-OBS-011/013).** B&H fetch, 1m-drill fetch, and async kline loads run **concurrently**, so a naive `Σ(stage_ms)` exceeds wall-clock and is misleading. The model is pinned: each stage timer is **exclusive (non-overlapping CPU/loop occupancy)** so `Σ(exclusive stage_ms) == wall_ms` within a documented tolerance, **AND** a separate `overlap_ms` term records concurrency-saved time (`Σ(naive stage durations) − wall_ms`) so the concurrency win is visible, not hidden. Stage timers are recorded as `(start, end)` spans and reduced to exclusive occupancy (interval-union), not summed raw. **On timeout/cancel, partial timings reconcile** to elapsed-until-failure under the same model (REQ-OBS-013) — the aborted stage's open span is closed at the kill instant. A test runs overlapping fetch+load stages and asserts `Σ(exclusive) == wall ± tol` and `overlap_ms` is the measured savings.

## 9.2 Cache hit/miss + refetch counters (proves the re-download is dead)

| Metric | What it proves | Req |
|--------|----------------|-----|
| `kline_tier_hits{arrow, feather, parquet, postgres}` | Read-tier provenance per symbol/day; warm rerun = all-arrow | REQ-STORE-012 |
| `bybit_kline_calls` | **0 on a fully-sealed rerun** (the headline counter) | REQ-CACHE |
| `sealed_day_fetched_once` | A sealed day's lifetime fetch count == 1 across N reruns | Prime Directive |
| `unsealed_days_fetched` / `negative_cache_skips` | Gap-fill scope = unsealed-only; negative days never re-probed | REQ-STORE-009 |
| `postgres_kline_selects` | **0 on a warm same-process rerun OF A FULLY-SEALED WINDOW**; **== forming-day-only** on a to-present (forming-tail) rerun — NOT 0 (R3-F5-batch1) | REQ-STORE-012 |

A dedicated **"sealed day fetched once" counter** is asserted in a mock-client test (`call_count == 1` across reruns).

## 9.3 JIT + parity diagnostics (with log-redaction discipline)

- `jit_compile_ms` per kernel (first-call 1–10s, amortized — REQ-PERF-040); `engine_path` label (`sequential`/`fastpath`/`pure_python`).
- **Log-redaction discipline (R1-F14, redaction-bypass guard).** The platform's MCP surface deliberately redacts absolute money by default (`financial_detail=false` across accounts/positions/trades/analytics). Parity-diff and invariant-check logs must NOT bypass that: by default they emit **ratios / deltas / hashed-or-bucketed** values, never raw absolute P&L/equity. Raw-value emission is gated behind an explicit debug flag that is **off in prod**. This applies to BOTH the parity-diff field dump AND the invariant-check value emission (the `Σ trade.pnl == final_equity − starting_capital == net_profit` numbers are absolute money — they are logged as a boolean pass + a bucketed magnitude by default, raw only under the debug flag).
- **Two-tier shadow / dark-compare mode (R1-F14 mig, REQ-ROLL-016, REQ-OBS-046).** Shadow mode is **two tiers, both persistence-neutral**:
  - **(a) Read-path shadow:** read BOTH Postgres and the columnar tier, log a byte-divergence metric, and **return the authoritative Postgres** result. Catches columnar drift without ever serving or persisting a columnar value.
  - **(b) Engine shadow — SIZE-CAPPED to feasibility (R2-F8-batch4, REQ-ROLL-016):** sample runs through BOTH the legacy and optimized engines, **persist the optimized result** (the legacy run is the throwaway comparison), and emit a **localized** divergence payload — trade ordinal/symbol + the specific field + magnitude-vs-legacy (not just "diverged"). **Bound:** the legacy engine is the multi-hour `O(scans×N_total)` path being eliminated; on a real 90d×50sym run it hits the 120s kill and yields NO comparison. So engine-shadow runs **only on small synthetic/bounded configs** (a documented cap: ≤ a few symbols × ≤ a few days, well under the legacy engine's feasible envelope) **OR** off the prod critical path entirely (an offline replay job with its **own relaxed budget**, not the live 120s wall). The size cap is documented and enforced; a real over-cap prod run is shadowed by the read-path tier (a) only, never by dual-engine execution that cannot complete.
  Both tiers are sampling-rate-bounded; disabling removes ALL dual-execution cost (REQ-PERF-036). Off by default in prod. Divergence alerts carry the localized field payload so a regression is pinpointed, not just flagged.
- **Per-run invariant checks** (O(trades), always on): three-way `Σ trade.pnl == final_equity − starting_capital == net_profit` reconciliation (emitted redacted per the discipline above); data/signal provenance fingerprint hash (REQ-PERF-036).

## 9.4 Pre-flight estimator telemetry

The estimator (REQ-PERF-037, §3.9) logs its predicted vs actual (compute candles×scans×book-depth, cold Bybit pages `ceil(missing/1000)`, drill fraction, cold-columnar-build term) so calibration drift is visible; it must bracket actual within a documented factor (±50%) on the **deterministic compute+network+cold-build terms** on the canonical + wide fixtures, host-aware (REQ-PERF-038). The drill term is a bounded worst-case and is **excluded from the ±50% accuracy gate** (R1-F7, §3.9).

## 9.5 Standing event-loop-lag SLI (always-on runtime-safety canary — R1-F8, REQ-PERF-029/030)

The single most important runtime-safety SLI for a CPU-bound engine sharing the live FastAPI process is an **always-on event-loop-lag gauge** — a periodic `loop.time()` drift sampler — asserted under a documented bound for the **ENTIRE duration of a backtest AND a sweep** (spanning kline load, SoA build, columnar materialization, persist, sha recompute, HTTP fetch). It is the canary for starvation of the live auto-trade coroutines by the threadpool engine: any incidental blocking call a later phase adds on the loop thread shows up here. On breach it alerts/breaks. Mapped SLIs (named, not test-only):
- `event_loop_lag_ms` (standing gauge, bounded across backtest + sweep — REQ-PERF-030).
- `live_scanner_fetch_latency_p95` vs a baseline during the v58 DDL + the `SealBackfillRunner` backfill window **AND the distinct out-of-band `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` build window (R4-F6-batch6-c4)** — the CIC build is a separate, potentially much-longer operation than the in-txn v58 DDL + backfill, so its window is named and measured explicitly here (must not regress beyond a factor — REQ-PERF-031); its own `cic_build_ms{index}` + stall gauge are registered (§9.7).

## 9.6 Runtime status surface + Bybit circuit-breaker state (R1-F8 mig / R1-F9 mig)

The runtime status route (§5.4) exposes the **shared Bybit circuit-breaker** state (`closed`/`open`/`half-open` + consecutive-failure count + next-probe time). **Decision (R2-F4-batch5): the backtest/kline/instrument/drill fetch paths REUSE the existing `backend/mcp/core/breaker.py` breaker INSTANCE — they do NOT construct a second breaker.** A new breaker with separate state would let the kline path keep hammering Bybit while the MCP path is open (or vice-versa); a single shared instance is the authoritative state across the kline + instrument + drill fetch paths (REQ-OBS-029). A storm of 429s/timeouts trips the breaker into a coordinated backoff; **failed/429/timeout responses never seal** a day (REQ-CACHE-007/028) and the breaker state is observable, not silent. A test asserts the kline fetch path and the MCP path share one breaker object (same id), not two.

**Priority/quota layer reconciles the single shared breaker with REQ-CACHE-040 "backtest cold-fill rate-prioritized below live" (R4-F9-batch6-c2).** A single binary breaker (closed/open/half-open) has **no notion of priority** — a backtest cold-warmup 429 storm would OPEN the shared breaker and cut off LIVE scanner/auto-trade/reconciler Bybit access too, the **opposite** of "live prioritized". The shared breaker is kept (state-coherence is correct), but a **priority/quota layer sits in front of it** so the two requirements are no longer in tension:
- **Backtest cold-fetch holds its OWN lower-share semaphore** (a small fraction of the global Bybit concurrency budget), distinct from the live fetch path's reservation. Backtest cold-fill **backs off on its own semaphore + a per-source rate quota BEFORE it can drive the shared breaker toward open** — so a backtest storm degrades *backtest* throughput first.
- **Live fetches retain reserved capacity even when the breaker is half-open:** on half-open, the single probe slot and the reserved live quota are **allocated to live first**; backtest cold-fetch only consumes Bybit capacity from its own residual share. The breaker still trips on a genuine Bybit-wide outage (protecting everyone), but routine backtest-induced 429s are absorbed by the backtest semaphore/quota, not by opening the shared breaker.
- **Test:** a **backtest-429-storm-does-not-starve-live** test drives a backtest cold-warmup into sustained 429s and asserts (a) backtest fetch throughput degrades (its semaphore/quota throttles) while (b) a concurrent live scanner/auto-trade fetch **retains its reserved capacity and is not starved** — i.e. the shared breaker is not opened by backtest-only pressure.

## 9.7 Migration / deploy observability + storage-health alerting (R3-F8/R3-F9-batch4 — REQ-OBS-031/032/033/034/041/042/047)

§9.1–§9.6 are run-centric; migration/deploy + storage-health signals were thin or orphaned. All names are registered in the §9 central registry; deploy-gating alerts are distinct from in-run degradation.

**Migration / deploy signals:**
- **Migration duration + outcome with anomaly-multiple alert (REQ-OBS-031).** Each migration emits `migration_ms{version}` + outcome; an alert fires when duration exceeds an **anomaly multiple** of its historical baseline (a v58 that normally runs sub-second taking 30s signals lock contention / a table rewrite).
- **DDL/backfill FAILURE deploy-gating alert (REQ-OBS-032).** A migration DDL failure or a `SealBackfillRunner` fatal is a **deploy-gating** alert (distinct from in-run degradation), naming the **version int + the failing statement** so the boot crash-loop hazard is diagnosable from one log line.
- **Boot schema_version mismatch alert (REQ-OBS-033).** At boot, if the applied `schema_version` ≠ the binary's expected/max-supported version, emit a **mismatch alert** and route to the legacy path (this pairs with the §7.3 promotion guard, which blocks a downgrade outright).
- **`application_name` + lock-hold-time labeling (REQ-OBS-034).** The migration connection AND the `SealBackfillRunner` connection set a distinctive `application_name` so they are identifiable in `pg_stat_activity`; the **ACCESS-EXCLUSIVE / advisory-lock hold time** is measured and alerted if it exceeds the bounded `lock_timeout` budget.

**Storage-health signals (rolling/boot):**
- **Expected-persistent columnar volume EMPTY at boot (REQ-OBS-041).** If `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR` is configured persistent but comes up **empty** at boot (misconfigured mount → cold rebuild every deploy), alert — this silently forfeits the §11.1 <5s warm-rerun budget.
- **`kline_cache_default` non-empty in prod (REQ-OBS-041).** A gauge alerts when the default partition holds rows (partition-create-miss, §4.4) — the seal/columnar pruning invariant depends on it being empty.
- **Monthly-partition / part-file sprawl gauge (REQ-OBS-041).** A gauge tracks partition count + per-month part-file count so unbounded small-file sprawl (compaction not keeping up) is visible.
- **Fallback-rate rolling-window alert (REQ-OBS-042).** The RATE of runs **degrading to a fallback** (numba→pure-Python, columnar→Postgres, fastpath→sequential) over a rolling window is alerted — a creeping rise means an accel tier is silently broken in prod even though each run "succeeds."
- **Soft-SLO wall-time-vs-estimate breach (REQ-OBS-047).** A per-run **soft-SLO** alert fires when wall-time exceeds the `PreflightEstimator` prediction by a documented factor — distinct from the hard 120s kill — so latency regressions surface before they hit the wall.
- **RSS-watchdog abort counter + budget gauge — a watchdog abort is an ACCEPTANCE-PARITY incident (R4-F8-batch6-c3, REQ-API-021, REQ-OBS-013/047).** §3.9 documents that a runtime RSS-watchdog abort of an individually-admitted run is an **acceptance-parity violation** (a config the legacy engine completed gets killed) — to be PREVENTED by concurrency-aware admission, NOT relied upon — yet §9 previously registered no counter for it, so the very event the architecture calls a violation was invisible in prod (a mis-calibrated aggregate accountant that lets aborts happen produces no telemetry). Pinned: a registered **`rss_watchdog_aborts` counter** + a **`peak_rss_bytes` vs budget gauge** are added to the §9 central registry; the aborted run persists its **terminal reason = `rss_watchdog_abort`** (REQ-OBS-013) and they surface on the §5.4 status route. **Any non-zero watchdog-abort rate is a deploy/health alert DISTINCT from the soft-SLO breach** above (a soft-SLO breach is "slower than predicted"; a watchdog abort is "killed a feasible run" — a harder incident). This makes the §3.9 "3-concurrent-wide-run aggregate-RSS" happy-path test's failure mode observable in prod, not just in CI.
- **Admission-queue + watchdog-tightening telemetry — a silently-queued/tightened admission is observable (R5-F10-batch1, Medium — invisible-admission-state fix).** The `AdmissionAccountant` (§3.9) queue is a NEW runtime mechanism that can **DELAY interactive UI backtests** waiting for aggregate RSS to free, and §7.5 says admission **tightens** when the RSS watchdog dies — but §9 previously registered no telemetry for either, so a queue silently holding user runs (or a tightened-admission state silently rejecting feasible runs) would be invisible in prod, contradicting the §9 "every degradation is observable" posture. Pinned: register (in `backend/services/backtest_metrics_registry.py`) **`admission_queue_depth`** (gauge — runs currently waiting for a slot's bytes), **`admission_queue_wait_ms`** (timer — how long queued runs wait before slot-grant), **`admission_rejected_aggregate`** (counter — runs rejected/queued specifically because the aggregate Σ-reserved would breach, distinct from a per-run over-ceiling reject), and **`admission_tightened`** (gauge/boolean — set when the watchdog is down and admission has flipped to the conservative reservation multiplier §3.9). These join `admission_reservation_vs_actual_bytes` (already registered §3.9), surface on the §5.4 status route, and **sustained queueing OR a stuck `admission_tightened`=1 is alerted** — same treatment as `rss_watchdog_aborts`. A test asserts a forced aggregate-exhaustion drives `admission_queue_depth`>0 and the gauge clears when a slot frees, and that killing the watchdog sets `admission_tightened`=1.
- **Standing per-run wall-time-vs-budget SLI — sub-kill latency regressions are observable in prod, not only in CI (R5-F12-batch3, Medium — invisible-drift fix).** There was no ALWAYS-ON production SLO on per-run wall-time-vs-budget: the benchmark regression gate is **CI-only**, and the §9.5 loop-lag SLI catches LIVE starvation but NOT a backtest that silently drifts from <10s to ~100s while staying under the 120s kill (a real-world latency regression from a cold tier, a cache-miss storm, or B-drift is then invisible until it crosses the kill threshold). The REQ-OBS-047 soft-SLO (above) compares wall-time to the **pre-flight `pred_ms`**; this is **extended** to ALSO emit a standing **`run_wall_vs_budget_ratio`** gauge = `completed-run wall-time / its run-class budget` (the §7.4 run-class cap, e.g. ≤50%-of-cap for the canonical class) AND `wall-time / pred_ms`, alerting when EITHER ratio exceeds a documented bound over a rolling window. The per-stage timers (§9.1 `stage_timings`) already exist; this adds a **budget-breach gauge** so a sub-kill regression (e.g. canonical run drifting 10s→100s, still under 120s) is **alerted in prod**, not discovered only when a CI benchmark happens to run. A test asserts a synthetically-slowed run (under 120s but over its class budget) trips the `run_wall_vs_budget_ratio` alert.

These are registered emitters surfaced on the §5.4 status route (rolling gauges) and the alerting pipeline (threshold alerts).

---

# 10. Resilience & Failure Modes

Every new fast path has a **slower correct fallback**; the system degrades, never breaks. The pure-Python + Postgres path is always reachable.

| # | Failure | Detection | Response | Req |
|---|---------|-----------|----------|-----|
| R1 | **numba unavailable / JIT fails** (likely Py3.14.3) | `HAS_NUMBA=False` or first-call exception | Transparent fallback to pure-Python kernel (identical output, slower). Phase 3 alone meets "minutes" so this is non-fatal (D5). | REQ-DEP-001/004 |
| R2 | **Parquet corrupt / missing / short-read** | sha256 mismatch or `row_count ≠ candle_count − gap_count` (REQ-STORE-028) | Invalidate + rebuild-from-SOR, or PG fallback for that partition; never return corrupt/truncated klines. | REQ-STORE-028 |
| R3 | **Incompatible/unknown columnar format stamp** (rolling deploy both directions) | Format/schema version check | Rebuild from Postgres rather than mis-read garbled columns; mmap also validates byte-order/arch. | REQ-STORE-029 |
| R4 | **Columnar dir unwritable / out of space** | Boot self-check (existence/writability/free-space) | Degrade read path to Postgres + structured warning; boot reports tier "degraded"; never crash boot. | REQ-STORE-034 |
| R5 | **Partial cache** (some sealed columnar, some forming PG tail in one batch) | Per-symbol tier routing | Each symbol routed independently; assembled byte-identical to a uniform Postgres read; no cross-symbol interleave. | REQ-STORE-016/031 |
| R6 | **Columnar write fails after rows durable** | Materialize step exception | Day stays **sealed** (PG-served, lazily retried), never unsealed/refetchable; seal commit doesn't depend on Parquet. | REQ-STORE-026 |
| R7 | **Seal-upsert fails after rows durable** | Seal step exception | Non-fatal: run completes oracle-identical; day stays unsealed for next-run lazy-seal. | REQ-CACHE-050 |
| R8 | **Cold store_klines PG write fails** | Insert exception | Day left unsealed/refetchable, no torn manifest row; fail loud (symbol+range) or documented partial-data warning; never seal unpersisted rows. | REQ-CACHE-050 |
| R9 | **1m drill fetch fails mid-run** | Per-bar fetch exception | Fall back to 5m for THAT bar only; never abort, never poison other bars, never persist partial 1m; non-optimistic. | REQ-DRILL-023 |
| R10 | **Cancel / 120s timeout** | `threading.Event` (every 100 candles `:1232`) / `threading.Timer` (`:770`) | Cooperative stop; `_persist_results` idempotent (upsert/delete-before-insert) so a re-run is clean; slot released; partial sweep results retained. | discovery §4/§5 |
| R11 | **>6mo partition gap** (sealed range in `kline_cache_default`) | v58 dry-run gate + `store_klines` partition auto-create | Auto-create the missing monthly partition on write (migration-38 bounds/naming); gate blocks apply on un-partitioned >6mo range. | REQ-STORE-001, REQ-MIG-041 |
| R12 | **WIDE run exceeds SoA RAM ceiling** (200sym×365d ~1GB) | Pre-flight estimate vs 1GB budget **+ runtime RSS watchdog** (R1-F15) | **REJECT (or partition only on the provably symbol-independent fast-path subset, ADR-001) a run whose FINAL SoA exceeds the klines budget — NOT "stream it through" (corrected R2-F2-batch1/R3-F1-batch1).** RUN-stage residency IS the full SoA in a cross-sectional shared-capital sim, so streaming bounds only the **LOAD transient** (one batch resident, released before next — §3.1) for runs whose final SoA already fits. The **runtime RSS watchdog cooperatively aborts** a path-dependent overshoot before OOM; admission is concurrency-aware (§3.9). Never OOM the shared process. A doc-consistency check keeps this row in lockstep with §7.4/§3.1/Appendix B. | REQ-PERF-014/015/039 |
| R13 | **Forming-day torn read** (concurrent live-scanner upsert) | Forming day routes to PG primary | Point-in-time/repeatable-read snapshot query; forming day **never enters Arrow/Feather/Parquet hot tiers** (§11.4); a replica-offloaded sealed read is joined to the primary forming read only under one snapshot or a generation-token check (no torn seam). | REQ-STORE-030, REQ-PERF-022 |
| R14 | **Out-of-order intra-scan query** to merge-walk pointer | Target time precedes previous query | Fall back to `searchsorted` O(log N) for that query; never rescan O(N) or reset pointer; bit-identical to linear oracle. | REQ-ENG-004 |
| R15 | **Bybit 429/timeout storm** | Shared circuit breaker (consecutive-failure count) | Breaker opens → coordinated backoff across kline/instrument/drill paths; failed responses never seal; state observable on status route (§9.6). | REQ-OBS-029, REQ-CACHE-007/028 |
| R16 | **Seal backfill contends with live coverage upserts** | Chunk `lock_timeout` exceeded | `SealBackfillRunner` chunked separate commits + short `lock_timeout`+retry/backoff + optional `SKIP LOCKED`; DRAIN/QUIESCE pause; never deadlocks/long-blocks the live scanner (§3.10). | REQ-MIG-030/031/032 |
| R16b | **v58 DDL `ACCESS EXCLUSIVE` contends with the live scanner's continuous `_update_coverage` upserts (R4-F3-batch6)** | ADD COLUMN on `kline_cache_coverage` queues behind a scanner `ROW EXCLUSIVE`; without protection the `lock_timeout` aborts v58 (crash-loop, global advisory lock blocks every booting instance) OR the scanner is blocked for the migration | **The contended writer is the LIVE SCANNER, not just submissions.** Two-pronged: (1) a brief **scanner coverage-write gate** (`BT_COVERAGE_WRITE_PAUSE`) defers/buffers the scanner's GREATEST upserts for the sub-second DDL window so the request is uncontended; (2) per-statement `SAVEPOINT`+`lock_timeout='3s'`+bounded retry (`_alter_with_retry`, §4.4) so a transient conflict retries that statement only, never aborts v58; plus the submission-quiesce DRAIN. Concurrent-`_update_coverage`-during-DDL test asserts retry/succeed without blocking the scanner beyond budget (§4.4). | REQ-MIG-030/031/032 |
| R17 | **Live-trading breaker opens mid-sweep** | Parent-side `mcp_permitted()` False + worker IPC heartbeat | `SweepRunner` stops dispatching new combos (optionally drains in-flight), resumes when breaker clears — live order placement is never starved by a parallel sweep (§3.6). | FR-037/NFR-002 |
| R18 | **Prior SIGKILL/OOM left orphaned shared_memory / temp files** | Boot reaper liveness check | Unlink stale named segments (versioned names) + sweep orphaned columnar temp files before first use; same-named segment never `EEXIST`s, reader never reads a leftover (§3.6). | REQ-STORE-044 |
| R19 | **Engine-SHA/flag generation mismatch on sweep resume** | `mcp_sweep_results.engine_fingerprint` differs (real sweep table, R2-F1) | Re-run or refuse-merge the cross-generation combos; a ranked set is never silently multi-generation; boot reconcile frees stuck slots/workers/segments (§3.6). | REQ-ROLL-017/018/019 |

**Idempotent persistence (crash-resume):** results `ON CONFLICT(run_id)` upsert; trades delete-before-insert; kline `INSERT ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`; seal upsert on `(symbol,interval,date)`; sweep per-combo result write retained for crash-resume (REQ-SWEEP-009). Any failure leaves a re-runnable state.

---

# 11. Performance

## 11.1 Canonical fixture + latency budgets

**Canonical fixture: 90 days × 50 symbols, 5m.** All single-run budgets are gated on it, **distinct from any relative-speedup ratio** (REQ-SWEEP-005). The fixture is **≈1.296M 5m candles** (90×50×288) over **≈2160 scans** (REQ-PERF-001).

**Candle-eval count is pinned, not implicit (R1-F1).** The per-candle kernel runs **per OPEN POSITION** (equity valuation + liq/TP/SL + MFE/MAE per position), so the real work unit is **candle-evals ≈ candles × avg-concurrent-book-depth `B`**, NOT raw candles. A dedicated fixture **measures and asserts avg/peak `B`** so the eval denominator is fixed; budgets below are derived from it (canonical assumes `B≈5` avg unless the fixture says otherwise). **This fixture also populates and asserts `backtest_runs.peak_open_positions` (max P) and `turnover` (close count) against the seeded fixture's true peak-P and close count (R4-F4-batch6-c3, REQ-OBS-009)** — both are additive nullable run metrics that calibrate the PreflightEstimator book-depth `B` (§3.9/§11.1) and diagnose deep-book vs high-turnover slow runs; they are enumerated in the migration-completeness meta-test and the OBS schema-snapshot (REQ-OBS-016).

**Basket-equity recompute CADENCE is pinned as the parity oracle; the denominator is TWO terms, not one product (R3-F1-batch1, REQ-ENG-032, REQ-PAR-006, REQ-PERF-032/009/010).** The earlier single product `1.296M × B` is **dimensionally conflated**: `1.296M = ticks(25,920) × symbols(50)` already, and multiplying by `B` (open positions across all symbols at one tick) would encode a per-**symbol-candle** O(B) basket-equity recompute (≈`symbols×` more than necessary), making the Σ-uPnL reduction run `symbols × ticks × B` — super-linear in symbols, which **violates REQ-ENG-032** (≤2× on symbol-doubling) and REQ-PERF-032/009/010 (O(1)-amortized / linear reduction). The cadence is also parity-relevant: recomputing basket equity after each symbol-candle vs once per timeline tick changes EQUITY_DROP/RISE firing points (REQ-PAR-006 / REQ-ENG-023 deterministic Σ order), so it cannot be silently changed to fix scaling. **Pinned oracle:** the legacy engine recomputes basket equity `E = wallet + Σ open-uPnL` and fires the equity rules **ONCE per timeline tick over the open book** (NOT once per symbol-candle) — this is frozen as the parity oracle (the golden master catches any change). **This cadence is VERIFIED against the legacy code in a P0 step BEFORE it is frozen as the oracle, not assumed (R4-F7-batch6-c4, REQ-ENG-032/PAR-006):** the doc cites legacy lines for the equity RULES (`:1496`/`:1580`) and funding (`:1243`) but NOT a line proving the basket recompute is invoked once-per-tick rather than inside the per-symbol candle loop — and the linear-symbol-scaling MUST (REQ-ENG-032) plus the headline symbol-scaling speedup rest entirely on this premise. So a **P0 verification step reads the cited `_evaluate_candles_until` / `_eval_equity_core` code, determines the ACTUAL legacy recompute cadence relative to the symbol loop, and records it as evidence (the proving line) before the once-per-tick oracle is frozen.** If legacy is genuinely once-per-tick, the proving line is cited here and the oracle stands. **If legacy turns out to be per-symbol-candle**, that is surfaced as a parity-relevant finding: the once-per-tick rewrite would change equity firing points (a silent golden-master break), so it is resolved BEFORE P3 — NOT deferred to the conditional "REQ-ENG-032 is formally amended to drop linear-symbol-scaling" escape hatch, which is retained only as the documented fallback if the cadence cannot be made once-per-tick without changing decisions. The P0 cadence-evidence step is added to Appendix A / the P0 checklist.
- **LIGHT term — `O(total_candles)` pointer/mark advances** ≈ `ticks × symbols` ≈ **1.296M** cheap merge-walk pointer advances + per-symbol mark updates (one `searchsorted`-free pointer step + float assignment each). This is the dominant *count* but each unit is near-trivial. **The LIGHT term gets its OWN per-advance cost ceiling + symbol-scaling micro-gate — it is NOT left unbudgeted (R4-F4-batch6-c4, REQ-ENG-032):** the LIGHT count scales with symbol count (LIGHT = `ticks × symbols`), so doubling symbols doubles it — the most likely hiding place for a high-constant or super-linear cross-symbol term (e.g. a per-symbol dict/attribute lookup in the pure-Python lane). Because "near-trivial" is asserted but nothing previously enforced it, two gates are pinned: **(1) a per-advance cost ceiling (ns/advance)** on the LIGHT step (pointer-advance + mark-update only), so a regression that makes each advance expensive is caught; **(2) a LIGHT-term symbol-scaling micro-gate** that isolates the LIGHT term (NOT the HEAVY term) and asserts **≤~2× on symbol-doubling** (REQ-ENG-032), separate from the HEAVY-term symbol-scaling gate. A registered **`light_advance_count`** counter (§9 registry) makes the LIGHT cost observable (advances/s), so the "near-trivial" claim is measured, not asserted. A 1.296M-iteration pure-Python loop is not free (tens of ns each minimum), so the ceiling is set from the measured native-list/memoryview advance cost after P3.
- **HEAVY term — `O(ticks × B)` per-position + basket work** ≈ `25,920 × B` (≈130k at `B≈5`): the liq/TP/SL barrier check, the per-position uPnL contribution to the **once-per-tick** basket Σ, the cascade/trailing/time passes. The Σ-uPnL reduction is `O(B)` per tick (linear, once per tick) — **NOT** `O(symbols×B)` — so doubling symbols at fixed `B` leaves the heavy term unchanged and doubling the book depth `B` doubles it linearly, satisfying REQ-ENG-032/PERF-032/009/010.

The throughput floors (§11.2) are denominated in the **HEAVY-term unit** (`ticks × B` per-position passes — the work the kernel actually optimizes), and the LIGHT term is budgeted separately as near-linear cheap advances. The §11.1 wall-time rows below are re-derived against this two-term model rather than the inflated `1.296M × B` single product (which over-counted the heavy work by ≈`symbols×`). **The actual canonical wall-time is gated by MEASUREMENT after P3** (§9.1 profiling) against the ≤50%-of-cap envelope, not by a hand-derived product; the fixture that pins `B` also pins the measured LIGHT/HEAVY split so the floor is checkable. **REQ amendments recorded explicitly (not buried):** (i) if a future config genuinely requires the per-symbol-candle cadence for parity, REQ-ENG-032/PERF-032/009/010 are **formally amended to drop the linear-symbol-scaling guarantee for the Σ-uPnL reduction** (it is provably super-linear under that cadence) — but the committed default is the once-per-tick cadence that keeps them satisfiable; (ii) the **REQ-PERF-005 floor raise from 100k→150k evals/s is an explicit requirement amendment** (previously tagged only "R1-F1"), recorded here as a committed change so test authors enforce the single 150k gate.

**Eval UNIT is pinned so the floor is falsifiable (R2-F17-batch5; denominator corrected per R3-F1-batch1).** "1 candle-eval" = **one full per-(tick×open-position) pass that INCLUDES all per-position passes folded together**: the liq/TP/SL barrier check, the once-per-tick basket-equity `Σ-uPnL` reduction contribution, the cascade step, the trailing pass, and the time pass — they are **one eval per (tick, open position)**, not five separate evals, and **counted on the HEAVY term `ticks × B`, NOT the inflated `candles × B = symbols × ticks × B`** (the cadence is once-per-timeline-tick, §above). So the HEAVY denominator is `ticks × B` ≈ `25,920 × 5 ≈ 130k` per-position passes (plus the separate `O(total_candles)` LIGHT advances). The floor is checked on this inclusive HEAVY unit — a kernel that hit the floor by counting only the barrier check (excluding cascade/trailing/time) would NOT satisfy the gate. The earlier `1.296M×5 / 150k ≈ 43s` figure **conflated** the LIGHT count (`1.296M` = ticks×symbols) with the HEAVY per-position work; the corrected canonical wall-time is **measured after P3** against the ≤50%-of-cap envelope (the LIGHT term ≈1.296M cheap advances + the HEAVY term ≈130k×(per-position passes), each profiled separately), not asserted from the single product. The microbench gate measures evals on this inclusive HEAVY unit.

| Path | Budget | Note |
|------|--------|------|
| 5m no-drill, **warm (numba P4)** | **< 10s** | ≤ ~8% of cap. At 5M evals/s: `1.296M×5 / 5M ≈ 1.3s` — comfortably inside (§11.2). |
| 5m no-drill, **warm (pure-Python P3)** | **"minutes," ≤ 50% of cap** | At the raised ≥150k evals/s floor on the HEAVY `ticks×B` unit: HEAVY term ≈ `130k / 150k ≈ 0.87s` (R4-F2-batch6-c4 — NOT the prior `6.48M / 150k ≈ 43s`, which charged the inflated `candles×B` numerator; the governing figure is the measured ≤50%-of-cap envelope, dominated by the LIGHT-advance + load/build stages, not the HEAVY math). numba stays **optional for feasibility** (D5) — P3 alone finishes under the 120s cap — but the **<10s** row is explicitly the **numba** path (R1-F1). |
| Drill-on, warm | **< 20s** | ≤ ~17% of cap. |
| Headroom vs cap | All warm runs **≤ 50% of 120s** | The cap may be raised but is never relied upon (REQ-SWEEP-005). |
| Warm same-process rerun (**fully-sealed window**) | **< 2s** | RAM slice, 0 disk, **0 PG kline reads** — only valid when the window is entirely inside sealed history (REQ-STORE-012). |
| Warm same-process rerun (**forming-tail window**, e.g. "last 90d" to now) | **< 2s** with **exactly one bounded forming-day PG read** | `postgres_kline_selects == forming-day-only` (NOT 0). The forming UTC day routes exclusively to Postgres primary (§11.4) and never enters a hot tier, so any to-present rerun pays ≥1 PG select for the forming day — the 0-PG-read invariant holds ONLY for sealed-only windows (R3-F5-batch1). |
| Cross-process warm rerun (**fully-sealed window**) | **< 5s** | mmap'd Feather page-in, 0 Bybit, **0 kline SELECTs** — sealed-only window (REQ-STORE-015). |
| **HEAVY-config, warm (numba P4)** | **< 30s** (≤25% of cap) | HEAVIEST fixture (REQ-PERF-002): drill-ON + every close rule armed + regime + mean-reversion + deep concurrent book (higher `B`) + per-eval gates (regime/session/BTC-vol + MR cohort routing). Measured against its OWN avg/peak `B` + per-eval cost, not the canonical `B≈5`. |
| **HEAVY-config, warm (pure-Python P3)** | **≤90s (HEAVY run-class cap, < 120s wall)** | Committed HEAVY pure-Python budget (R4-F9-batch6-c3, option (a)); D5 numba-optional preserved for HEAVY. REQ-PERF-005 "BOTH paths" floor gated here; see HEAVY-lane derivation below. |

**HEAVY/HEAVIEST-config lane budgets — BOTH paths, derived not silently omitted (R3-F2-batch1, REQ-PERF-002/005).** REQ-PERF-005 requires the eval-throughput floors gated on **BOTH the canonical AND the HEAVY-config paths**, and REQ-PERF-002 commits a HEAVIEST fixture with its own latency budget — but §11 previously derived wall-time only for the canonical `B≈5` profile, leaving the HEAVY pure-Python budget an unmet MUST. The HEAVIEST fixture has a **materially higher `B`** (deep concurrent book) AND a **heavier per-eval cost** (regime/session/BTC-vol gates + MR cohort routing + all close-rule passes), so its HEAVY-term denominator `ticks × B_heavy × per-eval-cost` is several× the canonical. Pinned:
- The HEAVIEST fixture **measures and pins its own avg/peak `B_heavy`** (mirroring the canonical `B` fixture), and BOTH a **numba** budget (`<30s` above) AND a **pure-Python** budget are derived from `B_heavy` + per-eval cost.
- **DECISION COMMITTED — option (a), concrete number (R4-F9-batch6-c3, REQ-PERF-005/039):** the HEAVY/HEAVIEST pure-Python lane is governed by an **explicit HEAVY run-class wall budget of `≤90s`** (a documented REQ-PERF-039 per-run-class cap: > the canonical 60s pure-Python budget, < the 120s hard cap, leaving headroom below the wall). This is committed NOW so a test author can write the HEAVY pure-Python gate against a falsifiable target, rather than leaving the either/or unresolved. Locked-Decision **D5's "numba-optional" guarantee is PRESERVED for the HEAVY class too** (numba is not made mandatory) — the pure-Python HEAVIEST lane must finish ≤90s. The numba HEAVY budget stays `<30s` (above). If post-P3 profiling (§9.1) shows pure-Python HEAVIEST cannot meet ≤90s on the provisioned HEAVY-class host, the fallback is option (b) (scope D5 numba-optional to canonical-class, numba-REQUIRED for HEAVIEST) — recorded as the documented contingency, but the **committed default is option (a) ≤90s pure-Python**. The §12.3 Performance gate runs the HEAVIEST fixture on both lanes and asserts `<30s` numba / `≤90s` pure-Python.
- **If pure-Python CANNOT meet ≤90s at HEAVIEST (contingency only):** fall back to option (b) — scope D5's "numba-optional" to canonical-class, declare numba REQUIRED for HEAVY/HEAVIEST, and mark the HEAVY pure-Python lane parity-only (not budget-bound). This is the recorded fallback, NOT the default.


**§11.1 ↔ §11.2 reconciliation (R1-F1; denominator corrected R3-F1-batch1).** The two numbers are made consistent by pinning `B`, pinning the **once-per-tick basket-equity cadence**, and deriving wall-time per engine lane from the **two-term model** (LIGHT `O(total_candles)` cheap advances + HEAVY `O(ticks × B)` per-position passes — §11.1 above), NOT the inflated `candles × B` single product. The lane table's "derived wall-time" column is an **upper-bound sanity figure** (it charges the full `1.296M` LIGHT count at the HEAVY floor, which over-counts); the **governing gate is the measured ≤50%-of-cap envelope** after P3 (§9.1), with the HEAVY floor (§11.2) checked on the `ticks × B` unit:

**REQ-PERF-001 lane-split amendment — surfaced as an explicit decision, not buried (R2-F4-batch4).** REQ-PERF-001 commits `<10s` drill-off / `<20s` drill-on as MUST budgets, but the `<10s` figure is achievable **only on the numba lane** (pure-Python is ~43–60s). Rather than silently leave the MUST conditionally unmet, this architecture **formally amends REQ-PERF-001 to lane-split budgets:** `<10s` (drill-off) / `<20s` (drill-on) are the **numba-lane** MUST budgets on the named canonical profile; the **pure-Python lane** MUST budget is **`≤60s` (≤50% of cap)**. numba is the mandatory lane for the `<10s` SLA — and because numba may have **no wheel on Py3.14.3 or musl/Alpine**, the deploy contract (§7.3) states the `<10s` SLA is met **only on a profile where the numba wheel is present**; on a numba-absent profile the pure-Python `≤60s` budget is the governing MUST. This requirement edit is recorded here explicitly (not deferred to implementation).

| Lane | Floor (§11.2, HEAVY `ticks×B` unit ≈ 130k evals canonical) | Wall-time figures — each numerator stated explicitly (R4-F2-batch6-c4); measured ≤ these after P3 | Satisfies |
|------|---------------|----------------------------|-----------|
| Pure-Python (P3) | **≥150k evals/s** (raised from 100k — explicit REQ-PERF-005 amendment so `≤50%`-of-cap holds — R1-F1/R3-F1-batch1) | **HEAVY term (governing): `130k / 150k ≈ 0.87s`.** LIGHT-term cheap advances are charged separately at their own per-advance ceiling (R4-F4-batch6-c4), NOT at the HEAVY floor. (A naive over-count charging the full `1.296M` LIGHT count at the HEAVY floor gives `1.296M / 150k ≈ 8.64s` — corrected from the prior erroneous "≈43s", which actually used the inflated `6.48M = candles×B` numerator, not `1.296M`.) Measured canonical wall-time is profiled after P3 against the ≤50%-of-cap envelope. | "minutes" + ≤50%-of-cap; numba-optional feasibility |
| numba (P4) | **≥5M evals/s** (post-P3-calibrated, §11.2) | HEAVY term: `130k / 5M ≈ 0.026s`; comfortably inside the **<10s** warm budget even adding LIGHT-advance + load/build stages. | the **<10s** warm budget |

The frozen **P0 baseline** (current engine on the canonical fixture) is the denominator for the **≥100× headline** target on long, scan-heavy backtests (findings §9: combined ≈100–1000×). **P0-baseline capture is pinned because the legacy engine cannot complete the canonical fixture under the 120s wall (R4-F8-batch6-c4, REQ-PERF-003/004).** §9.3 notes the legacy engine on a real 90d×50sym run **hits the 120s kill and yields NO comparison** — so there is no finite P0 wall-time on the canonical fixture, only a `≥120s` killed lower bound, which would make the ≥100× ratio unmeasurable (it could only ever assert "≥~1×"). Resolution (pinned): the P0 canonical baseline for the ≥100× gate is captured with the **`_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` (120s) kill DISABLED** — a deliberate one-off multi-hour (or as-long-as-needed) legacy run — and the frozen denominator is **engine-only CPU time** (consistent with REQ-PERF-004's engine-only normalization, excluding load/persist), NOT wall-time-under-the-killed-budget. (Equivalent permitted alternative: capture on a **scaled-down sub-fixture** the legacy engine CAN finish and **document the extrapolation** to the canonical size from the legacy `O(scans×N_total)` complexity.) The "P0 freezes the canonical baseline" claim and the "120s kill yields no comparison" statement are reconciled by this timeout-disabled (or extrapolated-sub-fixture) capture protocol, recorded in §11.1 and Appendix A.

## 11.2 Throughput floors (engine core)

| Floor | Phase | Mechanism | Req |
|-------|-------|-----------|-----|
| **≥ 150k HEAVY-evals/s** (`ticks×B` unit, `heavy_eval_count`) | P3 (pure-Python SoA) | searchsorted/merge-walk kills O(scans×N_total) setup + quadratic seeding; **native-list/memoryview hot loop, zero element-wise numpy `__getitem__`** (R1-F2, REQ-PERF-011) | REQ-PERF, REQ-ENG-001/003/007 |
| **≥ 5M HEAVY-evals/s** (`ticks×B` unit) — **post-P3-calibrated target, see below** | P4 (warmed numba kernel) | `@njit` removes interpreter overhead on per-candle math; nopython lowering plan §3.4 | REQ-PERF-040 |

P3 must reach "minutes" on its own (D5) so P4 is an earned bonus, not a dependency. **The 150k/s floor (raised from 100k — R1-F1) is set so the pure-Python lane finishes the canonical HEAVY-term evals at ≤50% of the 120s cap; the <10s warm budget §11.1 is the numba lane only.** **The eval UNIT is the §11.1 HEAVY unit = `ticks × B` per-(tick×open-position) passes (R4-F1-batch6-c4), NOT `candles × B = symbols × ticks × B`** — the earlier "candles × book-depth B" phrasing over-counted by ≈`symbols×` (it folded the LIGHT `ticks×symbols` pointer-advance count into the HEAVY denominator). One unit governs everywhere: §11.1, §11.2, REQ-PERF-005, REQ-PERF-011, and the §3.4 microbench gate all measure evals/s over the **`ticks × B` HEAVY denominator** (canonical ≈ `25,920 × 5 ≈ 130k` per-position passes). A **canonical registered counter `heavy_eval_count`** (§9 central registry) fixes the denominator both the §3.4 microbench gate and the §12.3 benchmark gate read, so evals/s is computed over one agreed number, not a re-derived product. The separate `O(total_candles)` LIGHT advances are counted by `light_advance_count` (R4-F4-batch6-c4 below), never folded into evals/s. Profile after P3 to confirm/re-target P4 (§9.1).

**The ≥5M/s numba floor is a POST-P3-CALIBRATED target with an explicit re-target protocol — NOT an unprofiled hard CI gate (R4-F3-batch6-c4, REQ-PERF-040).** The 5M evals/s figure comes from analogous public numba benchmarks, NOT from a profiling of THIS kernel — and the pinned HEAVY eval unit folds together the branchy cascade/trailing/time logic AND the deterministic, **non-vectorized** left-to-right Σ-uPnL reduction mandated for parity (§3.4 R2-F6), exactly the shapes that resist 200ns/eval composite throughput. So the document does NOT hard-gate CI on the unprofiled 5M number. Protocol:
- **Until P3 profiling exists, the 5M/s floor is PROVISIONAL / non-gating** — the numba lane must beat the pure-Python lane and meet the **<10s** wall budget (the real SLA), but the specific 5M evals/s number is not a blocking CI regression gate.
- **After P3 profiling (§9.1)** measures the actual warmed-kernel HEAVY-eval rate on the pinned-`B` fixture, the floor is **RE-TARGETED to a documented fraction of the measured kernel rate** (e.g. 80% of measured, to catch regressions without false-failing a legitimate large speedup on an unprofiled number). Only then does it become a hard benchmark-regression gate.
- The §11.1 "measured after P3 / re-target" language and the §11.2/§12.3 "floor" language are reconciled by this protocol: the **<10s wall budget is the hard gate**; the evals/s floor is the **post-P3-calibrated regression tripwire**, not a pre-profiling absolute. The §12.3 Performance row references this calibration so a sub-5M-but-faster-than-legacy kernel is not failed on a number nobody measured.

## 11.3 Sweep budgets

- **Warm sweep:** 100-combo < 60s, 500-combo < 5 min (REQ-SWEEP-005). All sweeps finish well under the 120s cap.
- **Parallel efficiency:** K-combo on M cores ≥ **0.7 × min(M, K, concurrency)** vs serial (REQ-SWEEP-006); steady-state per-combo time within ~1.5× the engine-only floor (REQ-SWEEP-007a); inherently-serial shared setup (pre-load + SoA + timeline) < **15%** of total sweep wall-time (REQ-SWEEP-007b, not Amdahl-capped).
- **Shipped-once inputs:** aggregate IPC/pickling bytes independent of combo count; process-tree RSS ≈ `base_snapshot + C×small-per-combo-working-set`, NOT `C×full-kline-bytes` (REQ-SWEEP-002).

## 11.4 Cache strategy (what / where / TTL / invalidation)

| Layer | What | Where | TTL / Invalidation |
|-------|------|-------|--------------------|
| Arrow hot frame | `{(symbol,interval,date-range): pa.Table}` — **SEALED days only** | In-process RAM (≤150MB LRU) | Process-lifetime; LRU evict. **The forming UTC day NEVER enters this tier (R1-F10).** |
| mmap'd Feather V2 | On-disk == in-memory Arrow IPC — **sealed days only** | `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR` | Persistent across processes; format-version + sha verified on map; forming day never mapped |
| Parquet | Immutable sealed months | `BT_COLUMNAR_DIR` hive | Sealed = **no TTL** (immutable); invalidate only on sha-mismatch rebuild (REQ-STORE-028) |
| Postgres SOR | All rows + forming edge | Postgres | Write-of-record; forming day **exclusively** served here, point-in-time snapshot |

**Forming-day staleness owner — DECIDED (R1-F10, REQ-STORE-030).** The forming UTC day has **no hot-tier staleness problem because it is never admitted to a hot tier**. The `KlineStore` tier-router **routes any range that includes `≥ completion_frontier` exclusively to Postgres primary** — the Arrow/Feather hot frames and Parquet hold sealed data only. This is the simplest resolution and removes the unowned "frontier advanced, evict the hot `today` frame" race entirely (the frontier advances every T — every 5 min for 5m — and nothing previously owned detecting that to evict). A test runs **two reruns straddling a 5m boundary and asserts both reflect fresh forming-day rows** (served from Postgres, not a stale hot frame). **Consequence for the warm-rerun budget (R3-F5-batch1):** a to-present window therefore pays **exactly one bounded forming-day PG read per warm rerun** — the "0 PG kline reads" claim (§11.1/§9.2) is scoped to **fully-sealed windows**; a forming-tail rerun's `postgres_kline_selects == forming-day-only`, measured against the separate forming-tail warm budget (<2s with one forming-day read), not the unachievable 0-PG-read gate.

**Key invariant:** sealed history has **no TTL** (that's the whole point — ADR-003). Only the forming UTC day (`open_time ≥ frontier`) is ever re-read, it is **always served from Postgres primary**, and it never enters Arrow/Feather/Parquet.

## 11.5 Progress/instrumentation overhead

`on_progress` + throttled DB `progress_pct` are time/percentage-throttled (not per-candle) → total progress writes **O(100)** regardless of candle count, overhead < 2%, first signal < 1s after run start; the Phase-1 cache fix collapses the history-proportional `_WARMUP_BAND=10%` stage to a bounded constant (REQ-PERF-035).

## 11.6 Persistence budget (R1-F11 mig, REQ-PERF-017/032)

| Budget | Mechanism | Gate |
|--------|-----------|------|
| **Persist < 3s** on a trade-heavy run | `executemany`/`COPY` for trades → O(1) insert round-trips; `equity_curve` columnar one-pass serialize | Double the trade count, assert insert round-trip count stays **flat** (∝ volume, not per-row RTT) |
